Talaq — Divorce
beginner
5 min
Wife's Denial Disproves Ruju' Claim
Dispute resolution in ruju' claims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on whose statement is accepted when the husband claims ruju' but the wife denies, and apply it to the slave girl case.

Core Idea
The wife's knowledge of her own iddah outweighs the husband's claim of ruju'.

The Hanafi school gives decisive weight to the wife's statement regarding the expiry of her iddah. Even if the husband insists he returned before her iddah ended, his claim is not accepted if she denies. This principle extends to a slave girl: even her master's confirmation of the husband's ruju' does not override her denial.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
The husband says he performed ruju' during iddah; the wife says her iddah had already expired. The question is whose word is taken.
2
Determine the relevant knowledge
The wife has direct knowledge of her own menstrual cycles and when her iddah ends. The husband may not be certain.
3
Apply the Hanafi rule
The wife's statement is accepted (قول معتبر). The husband's claim of ruju' after iddah is invalid.
This is based on the principle that the person with superior knowledge is believed.
4
Extend to the slave girl case
Even if the master (mawla) confirms the husband, the slave girl's denial prevails. Her knowledge of her own iddah is still superior.
The master's confirmation does not change the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر عورت نے تکذیب کر دی عورت کا قول معتبر مانا جائے گا مرد نے کہا میں رجوع کر چکا عورت کہتی ہے میری عدت گذر چکی تھی رجوع معتبر ہے یا نہیں اقوال فقہاء باندی کے شوہر نے اس کی عدت گذرنے کے بعد کہا میں رجوع کر چکا تھا مولیٰ نے شوہر کی تصدیق کر دی باندی تکذیب کرتی ہے قول کس کا معتبر ہوگا ، اقوال فقہاء رجوع کا حق کون سے حیض کے بعد ختم تصور کیا جائے گا عورت نے غسل کر لیا اور بدن کے کسی عضو پر پانی پہنچانا بھول گئی اگر عضو کامل یا ایک عضو سے زیادہ پر پانی نہیں پہنچا رجوع کا حق منقطع نہیں ہوگا اور اگر ایک عضو سے کم ہے منقطع ہو جائے گا حاملہ بیوی کو طلاق دی یا اس نے اس مرد سے بچہ جنا اور شوہر نے کہا میں نے اس سے جماع نہیں کیا شوہر کیلئے رجوع کا حق ہے عورت کے ساتھ خلوت کی اور دروازہ بند کر لیا اور پردہ لٹکا دیا اور کہالم جامعہا پھر طلاق دیدی رجوع کا اختیار نہیں ہے عورت کو کہا از اولدت فانت طالق عورت نے بچہ جنا پھر دوسرا بچہ لائی تو یہ ولادت ثانیہ رجوع ہے مرد نے کہا کلما ولدت ولد أفانت طالق عورت نے تین بچے جنے پہلا بچہ طلاق ہے اور دوسرا اور تیسرا بچہ رجعت ہے مطلقہ رجعیہ کیلئے زیب وزینت کا حکم طلاق رجعی وملی کو حرام نہیں کرتی ، امام شافعی کا نقطہ نظر
If the woman denies, the woman's statement is accepted. The husband said, 'I have returned,' the woman says, 'My iddah had passed,' is the ruju' valid or not? Statements of jurists: The husband of a slave girl, after her iddah had passed, said, 'I had returned,' the master confirmed the husband, the slave girl denies. Whose statement will be accepted? Statements of jurists: After which menstruation is the right of ruju' considered ended? The woman performed ghusl and forgot to pour water on some body part; if a complete limb or more than one limb did not receive water, the right of ruju' is not severed; if less than one limb, it is severed. He divorced a pregnant wife or she gave birth from that man and the husband said, 'I did not have intercourse with her,' the husband has the right of ruju'. He secluded with the woman and locked the door and hung a curtain and said [something] then divorced her, there is no option of ruju'. He said to the woman, 'If you give birth, you are divorced,' the woman gave birth then brought a second child, so this second birth is ruju'. The man said, 'Every time you give birth to a child, you are divorced,' the woman gave birth to three children; the first child is divorce, the second and third child are ruju'. Ruling on adornment for a revocably divorced woman. Revocable and irrevocable divorce does not make her unlawful. Imam Shafi'i's viewpoint.
Source pages p. 5

Commentary
This passage presents a series of rulings on ruju' (revocation of divorce) from the Hanafi school. The first ruling establishes that in a dispute between husband and wife regarding whether ruju' occurred, the wife's statement is accepted because she is more knowledgeable about her own iddah. For a slave girl, if the master confirms the husband's claim of ruju' but the slave girl denies, the slave girl's statement is accepted as she is the one whose iddah is in question. The passage then addresses the effect of incomplete ghusl on ruju': if the husband performed ghusl after the wife's iddah but missed less than one limb, the right of ruju' is severed; if a complete limb or more, it remains. For a pregnant woman, ruju' is valid even if the husband denies paternity. Seclusion (khalwah) with the wife without consummation then pronouncing talaq does not create ruju' rights. Conditional divorces linked to childbirth are discussed: if a woman gives birth multiple times, the first birth may effect divorce and subsequent births may constitute ruju'. The passage concludes that a revocably divorced woman is not forbidden from adornment, and Imam Shafi'i's [likely disagreeing] view is noted.

Key Terms
رجوع (rujūʿ): Revocation of a revocable divorce during the iddah period.
عدت (ʿiddah): The waiting period after divorce or death before a woman may remarry.
مطلقہ رجعیہ (muṭallaqah rajʿiyyah): A woman who has received a revocable divorce (one or two pronouncements) and is still in her iddah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a Hanafi fiqh dispute between husband and wife over whether ruju' occurred during iddah, whose statement is accepted?
A) The husband's, because he is the one who returns
B) The wife's, because she is more certain about her iddah
C) The qadi's, based on witnesses
D) Both statements are rejected

Key Takeaway
The wife's statement regarding her iddah expiry is accepted over the husband's claim of ruju'.

intermediate

Incomplete Ghusl and the Right of Ruju'
Effect of incomplete ghusl on ruju' right

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine whether the husband's right of ruju' is severed based on the extent of deficiency in the wife's ghusl after her final menstruation.

Core Idea
Missing water on less than a full limb during ghusl severs the right of ruju'; missing a full limb or more preserves it.

The end of the iddah period is marked by the wife's ghusl after her final menstruation. If she performs ghusl but forgets to wash some part, the effect on the right of ruju' depends on the quantity of the missed area. Missing a complete limb or more means the ghusl is significantly deficient, so the iddah is not considered fully complete, and the husband retains the right to ruju'. Missing less than a limb is a minor omission, so the iddah ends and ruju' is no longer possible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the context
The wife's iddah ends when she completes her ghusl after her final menstrual period. Until then, the husband has the right of ruju'.
2
Determine the deficiency in ghusl
If she forgets to pour water on some part of her body, classify the missed part: less than one limb (e.g., a hand's area) or a complete limb or more (e.g., an entire arm).
A limb here means a complete member like an arm, leg, head, etc.
3
Apply the Hanafi rule
If the missed part is less than one limb → the ghusl is considered complete → iddah ends → ruju' is severed. If the missed part is a complete limb or more → ghusl is deficient → iddah not fully ended → ruju' remains.
This is based on the principle that a significant deficiency invalidates the completion of the act.

Source Text

Key Terms
غسل (ghusl): Ritual washing of the entire body, obligatory after menstruation, janabah, etc.
عضو کامل (ʿuḍw kāmil): A complete limb such as an arm, leg, head, or torso.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a woman performs ghusl after her final menstruation but forgets to wash her entire leg, what is the status of the husband's right of ruju'?
A) The right is severed because ghusl was performed
B) The right is not severed because a complete limb was missed
C) The right is severed only if she missed more than three limbs
D) The right depends on her intention

Key Takeaway
Missing a complete limb or more in ghusl preserves the right of ruju'; missing less than a limb ends it.

Special Ruju' Cases: Pregnancy, Seclusion, Conditional Divorces
Miscellaneous rulings on ruju'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi rules for ruju' in cases of pregnancy, seclusion without consummation, and conditional divorces tied to childbirth, and note the permissibility of adornment for the revocably divorced woman.

Core Idea
Pregnancy keeps ruju' valid even if paternity is denied; seclusion without consummation prevents ruju'; conditional divorces can create ruju' upon subsequent births.

The Hanafi school addresses various scenarios affecting the right of ruju'. If the wife is pregnant, ruju' remains valid even if the husband denies paternity. If the husband secluded with her but did not consummate, then divorced, there is no ruju' right. In conditional divorces tied to childbirth, the first birth may effect divorce and subsequent births may act as ruju'. Additionally, a revocably divorced woman may adorn herself as she wishes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Four distinct scenarios are presented: (1) pregnant wife, husband denies paternity; (2) seclusion without consummation then divorce; (3) conditional divorce upon childbirth; (4) adornment for revocably divorced woman.
2
Rule for pregnant wife
The husband's denial of paternity does not affect his right of ruju'. He can still revoke the divorce during the iddah (which ends with delivery).
This is because ruju' is a right of the husband independent of paternity.
3
Rule for seclusion without consummation
If he secluded with her (locked door, hung curtain) but did not have intercourse, then divorced her, he has no right of ruju'. Seclusion does not create marital relations that would allow ruju'.
Ruju' is only possible if the divorce was revocable and occurred after valid consummation or valid seclusion that implies consummation? Here seclusion without consummation does not create that implication.
4
Rule for conditional divorce on childbirth
Example: 'If you give birth, you are divorced.' The first birth effects a divorce. If she then gives birth again (second child), that second birth counts as ruju' (return). Similarly, if he says 'Every time you give birth, you are divorced,' the first birth is divorce, subsequent births are ruju'.
This is based on the interpretation that each birth after the first is a new event that revokes the divorce.
5
Adornment ruling
A revocably divorced woman (muṭallaqah rajʿiyyah) is not prohibited from adorning herself (wearing jewelry, makeup, etc.) during her iddah.
This is in contrast to some other rules about iddah for bereavement.

Source Text

Key Terms
خلوت (khalwah): Seclusion of a married couple in private, which in Hanafi fiqh can imply consummation under certain conditions.
رجعت (rajʿat): Synonym for ruju' (return).
زیب وزینت (zīb wa zīnat): Adornment, including jewelry, makeup, and fine clothing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a husband secludes with his wife (locks the door, hangs a curtain) but does not have intercourse, then gives a revocable divorce, does he have the right of ruju'?
A) Yes, because seclusion implies consummation
B) No, because there was no actual consummation
C) Yes, if the seclusion was valid
D) No, regardless of seclusion

Key Takeaway
Ruju' rules vary by circumstance: valid during pregnancy despite paternity denial, invalid after seclusion without consummation, and conditional divorces create unique effects.

Conditions of Halala: When a Thrice-Divorced Woman Becomes Lawful
Rulings on when a divorced woman becomes lawful for her ex-husband

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions required for a valid halala and apply them to distinguish between free women, slave girls, and adolescent second husbands.

Core Idea
Consummation by a second husband is the essential pillar of halala.

This passage lays out the basic rules of halala – the process by which a thrice-divorced woman becomes lawful for her first husband. It clarifies the key conditions: a valid marriage with a second husband followed by actual consummation (or his death). The text also addresses special cases like adolescent boys acting as second husbands and the master's inability to be wali for his slave girl in halala. Understanding these conditions prevents common mistakes in this sensitive area of family law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal category
What is being ruled upon? It is halala – the process that makes a thrice-divorced woman lawful for her first husband. Note that the lesson distinguishes between less than three divorces (renewable after iddah) and three/two divorces requiring halala.
For a free woman, three divorces trigger the need; for a slave girl, two divorces.
2
List the essential conditions for halala
From the text: (1) A valid marriage contract with the second husband, (2) Consummation (dakhul) or death of the second husband, (3) After consummation, the second husband must divorce her or die, and (4) Her iddah from the second marriage must expire. Without these, she remains unlawful for the first husband.
The phrase 'زوج آخر دخول کے بعد طلاق دیدے یا فوت ہو جائے' makes consummation or death a requirement.
3
Examine special cases: adolescent boy and slave girl
An adolescent boy (sabi murahiq) who has reached the age of understanding marriage is considered like an adult for halala – his marriage and consummation count. For a slave girl, the master cannot act as her wali in halala because of his ownership interest; this is to prevent suspicion of collusion.
The master's inability is a legal safeguard, not a general rule of wali.
4
Apply the ruling to the practical scenario given
The text ends with a scenario: a woman claims she underwent halala – she says she married, consummated, was divorced, and completed iddah. When may the first husband remarry her? Answer: after confirmation of the entire process, i.e., after she provides evidence or the husband trusts her claim. The ruling underscores that mere claim is not enough; the conditions must be verified.
This illustrates the importance of certainty in marital matters.

فصل فيما تحل به المطلقة مطلقه با سنہ جبکہ طلاقیں تین سے کم ہوں عدت اور عدت کے بعد تجدید نکاح کر سکتا ہے حرہ کو تین طلاقیں یا باندی کو دو طلاقیں دیدیں حلالہ شرعیہ کے بغیر پہلے شوہر کیلئے حلال نہیں ہو گی زوج آخر دخول کے بعد طلاق دیدے یا فوت ہو جائے تو پہلے شوہر کیلئے عورت حلال ہو جائے گی صبی مراحق تحلیل میں بالغ کی طرح ہے مولی کا اپنی باندی سے ولی تحلیل کیلئے نا کافی ہے حرہ کو ایک یا دو طلاقیں دیدیں عورت کی عدت گزر چکی اور دوسرے شوہر سے نکاح کر لیا پھر پہلے شوہر کے پاس لوٹ آئی تو تین طلاق کے ساتھ لوٹے گی عورت کو تین طلاقیں دیں عورت نے کہا میری عدت گذر چکی اور دوسرے شوہر سے نکاح کیا اور اس نے دخول کیا اور طلاق دیدی اور میری عدت گزر چکی اس سے شوہر اول کیلئے کب نکاح کرنا جائز ہے
Section on what makes a divorced woman permissible. A divorced woman with less than three divorces, after her iddah, the husband may renew marriage. If a free woman is given three divorces or a slave girl two divorces, she is not lawful for the first husband without a legal halala. If the second husband divorces after consummation or dies, the woman becomes lawful for the first husband. An adolescent boy is like an adult in halala. The master's guardianship over his slave girl is insufficient for halala. If a free woman is given one or two divorces, her iddah passes, she marries another husband, then returns to the first husband, she returns with three divorces. If a woman is given three divorces and says, 'My iddah passed and I married another and he consummated and divorced me and my iddah passed,' then when is it permissible for the first husband to marry her?
Source pages p. 5

Commentary
This is a key section on halala (the requirement for a woman divorced thrice to marry and consummate with another man before remarrying her first husband). The passage clarifies: for a revocably divorced woman, remarriage is possible after iddah. But if three divorces are given, she must marry another man who consummates, then divorces or dies. An adolescent boy (sabi murahiq) qualifies as a second husband, but a master cannot act as a wali for his slave girl in halala because of his ownership interest. The last part highlights a practical case: if a woman claims she underwent halala, the first husband may remarry her after confirmation.

Key Terms
حلالہ (ḥalālah): The process by which a thrice-divorced woman becomes lawful for her first husband through marriage and consummation with a second husband.
صبی مراحق (ṣabī murāhiq): An adolescent boy nearing puberty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum requirement for halala to make a thrice-divorced woman lawful for her first husband?
A) A valid marriage contract with the second husband
B) A second marriage with consummation (dakhul)
C) Both marriage and consummation
D) The second husband's pronouncement of divorce

Key Takeaway
Halala requires a valid second marriage with consummation; mere marriage contract or divorce without consummation is insufficient.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate

Rulings on Khul' (Divorce by Redemption)
Rulings on khul' including compensation and validity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid khul', identify valid compensation, and apply the rulings to scenarios of uncertainty.

Core Idea
Khul' is a contract: compensation must be valid as mahr, and the ruling changes based on who is at fault.

This passage presents key rulings on khul' (divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation). Understanding these rules is essential for handling marital disputes within the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the primary ruling: khul' is permissible when there is fear of not fulfilling marital rights.
The text begins with the permissibility of khul'.
2
Classify compensation conditions
Compensation must be something that can validly be mahr; wine and swine are excluded. Consider who is at fault.
If the husband is at fault, taking compensation is makruh; if the wife is nashizah, taking more than mahr is makruh.
3
Distinguish cases of unknown compensation
Analyze scenarios where the wife says 'khul' for what is in my hand' but nothing is there, or specifies dirhams.
The ruling depends on the wording: if she mentions a specific amount, that amount is due.
4
Apply the rulings to specific cases
Practice with hypotheticals: e.g., a runaway slave as compensation, or ambiguous promises.
The text gives several examples to illustrate the application.

Chapter of Khul'. If there is fear of conflict between husband and wife that they will not fulfill each other's rights, then the wife may obtain khul' by giving wealth. If the defiance is from the husband's side, then taking compensation for khul' is disliked. If the wife is nashizah (rebellious), it is disliked for the husband to take more than he gave. If the husband received more than the mahr, it is permissible to take it judicially. If the husband divorces in exchange for wealth and the wife accepts, the wealth is obligatory on her. For a Muslim, the ruling on khul' in exchange for wine or swine: anything that can be valid as mahr can be valid as khul' compensation. The woman said to the man, 'Divorce me for what is in my hand,' and there was nothing in her hand, nothing is obligatory on her. The woman said, 'Divorce me for the wealth in my hand,' and there was nothing in her hand, then returning the mahr is obligatory on her. The woman said, 'Divorce me for the dirhams in my hand or for the money,' and the man did so, and there was nothing in her hand, three dirhams are obligatory on her. The woman made khul' on a runaway slave with the condition that she is innocent of him, she is not innocent, and the 'ayn (specific property) of the slave is on her. Definition of I'la'. Chapter of I'la'. If he fulfills within four months, he has committed perjury in his oath and expiation is obligatory. [Garbled text] He swore for four months, the oath expires with the passage of the period; however, if he rescinded the oath, it remains. One who swears for less than four months is not a muli. He swore with these words: 'I will not approach you for two months, two months after these two months,' then he is a muli. The husband said, 'By Allah, I will not approach you for two months,' then remained silent for a day, then said, 'By Allah, I will not approach you for two months after the first two months,' he is not a muli. The husband said, 'By Allah, I will not approach you for a year except for a day,' he is not a muli. Imam Zufar's viewpoint. A man in Basra said, 'By Allah, I will not enter Kufa,' and his wife was with him, he is not a muli. If he swears by hajj, fasting, charity, [unclear] or divorce, then he is a muli. If he makes i'la' with a revocably divorced woman, he is a muli; with an irrevocably divorced woman, he is not a muli. If he said to a foreign woman, 'By Allah, I will not approach you, and you are like my mother's back,' then married her, he is not a muli nor a muzahir. The duration of i'la' for a slave girl. If the muli is sick and unable to have intercourse, or the woman is sick, [unclear] or a minor with whom intercourse cannot occur, or there is a distance between them such that he cannot reach her during the i'la' period, then for him the method of ruju'. The ruling on saying to the woman 'You are unlawful to me.' Chapter of Khul'. (Duplicate of earlier text.)
Source pages p. 5

Commentary
This passage combines two major topics: khul' (divorce at the wife's instance by payment) and i'la' (a husband's vow to abstain from intercourse). For khul', the text emphasizes that it is permissible when conflict arises. If the husband is at fault, taking compensation is makruh; if the wife is nashizah (rebellious), taking more than what he gave is also makruh, but if he took more, it is still valid in qada'. The compensation must be something that can validly be mahr. Several hypothetical cases illustrate when compensation is or is not owed. For i'la', the definition is a vow to avoid intercourse for more than four months; if he returns within four months, he breaks his oath and pays kaffarah. Various expressions and conditions are examined, including Imam Zufar's view. The passage also discusses i'la' with a revocable versus irrevocable divorced woman, and the effect of conditions like sickness or distance. The text ends with a repetition of the khul' section, likely a copying error in the OCR.

Key Terms
خلع (khulʿ): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation paid to the husband.
ناشزہ (nāshizah): A wife who is rebellious or disobedient regarding marital obligations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a wife says to her husband, 'Divorce me for what is in my hand,' and her hand is empty, what is the ruling?
A) She must pay 10 dirhams (a default amount).
B) She must pay the mahr.
C) She owes nothing.
D) The khul' is invalid.

Key Takeaway
Khul' is valid with a valid compensation; uncertainty in compensation leads to rulings based on the wording used.

Rulings on I'la' (Vow of Abstinence)
Rulings on i'la' including definition, duration, and legal consequences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define i'la', identify who is a muli, and determine the legal consequences of the vow.

Core Idea
I'la' is a vow to abstain from intercourse for more than four months, with legal effects on the marriage.

This passage explains i'la' (a husband's vow to abstain from sexual relations with his wife). Understanding its definition, duration, and exceptions is crucial for marital law.

Guided Path
1
Define i'la' and identify a muli
Learn the definition: a vow by the husband to avoid intercourse for more than four months.
If the period is less than four months, he is not a muli.
2
Analyze the legal consequence
If he fulfills the vow within four months, he breaks his oath and must pay kaffarah. If he does not, the wife may seek dissolution.
The passage focuses on the case of returning within four months.
3
Examine various expressions
Certain phrasings make him a muli; others do not. For example, swearing by hajj or divorce makes him a muli.
The text provides examples of effective and ineffective phrasings.
4
Apply exceptions and special cases
Consider i'la' with a revocable vs. irrevocable divorced woman, or with a foreign woman. Also consider health and distance.
The passage includes Imam Zufar's viewpoint and conditions like sickness.

جس کے ساتھ جماع نہیں کیا جاسکتا ہے یا میاں بیوی کے درمیان مسافت ہے کہ عورت تک پہنچنے پر مدت ایلاء میں قادر نہیں اس کیلئے رجوع کا طریقہ عورت کو انت علی حرام کہنے کا حکم باب الخلع میاں بیوی کو جھگڑ کا خوف ہو کہ ایک دوسرے کے حقوق ادانہیں کر میں تو عورت مال دے کر خلع کر سکتی ہے سرکشی شوہر کی جانب سے ہو تو اس کیلئے بدل خلع لینا مکروہ ہے اگر عورت ناشزہ ہے تو مرد کیلئے دیئے ہوئے سے زیادہ وصول کرنا مکروہ ہے اگر مرد نے مہر سے زیادہ وصول کر لیا تو قضاء لینا جائز ہے شوہر نے مال کے عوض طلاق دی عورت نے اسے قبول کیا تو عورت پر مال لازم ہے مسلمان کیلئے شراب یا خنزیر کے عوض خلع کرنے کا حکم جو چیز مہر بننے کی صلاحیت رکھتی ہے وہ بدل ضلع بھی بن سکتی ہے عورت نے مرد سے کہا جو کچھ میرے ہاتھ میں ہے اس پر ضلع کرلے اور عورت کے ہاتھ میں کچھ نہیں تھا عورت پر کچھ بھی لازم نہیں ہوگا عورت نے کہا خالعنی علی مافی یدی من مال عورت کے ہاتھ میں کچھ بھی نہیں تھا تو مہر لوٹانا عورت پر لازم ہے عورت نے کہا خالعنی علی مافی یدی من در اہم او من الدار هم مرد نے ایسا کر لیا عورت کے ہاتھ میں کچھ بھی نہیں تھا عورت پر تین دراہم لازم ہیں عورت نے بھاگے ہوئے غلام پر ضلع کر لیا اس شرط پر کہ وہ اس سے بری ہے عورت بری نہیں ہوگی عورت پر غلام کا عین
Chapter of Khul'. If there is fear of conflict between husband and wife that they will not fulfill each other's rights, then the wife may obtain khul' by giving wealth. If the defiance is from the husband's side, then taking compensation for khul' is disliked. If the wife is nashizah (rebellious), it is disliked for the husband to take more than he gave. If the husband received more than the mahr, it is permissible to take it judicially. If the husband divorces in exchange for wealth and the wife accepts, the wealth is obligatory on her. For a Muslim, the ruling on khul' in exchange for wine or swine: anything that can be valid as mahr can be valid as khul' compensation. The woman said to the man, 'Divorce me for what is in my hand,' and there was nothing in her hand, nothing is obligatory on her. The woman said, 'Divorce me for the wealth in my hand,' and there was nothing in her hand, then returning the mahr is obligatory on her. The woman said, 'Divorce me for the dirhams in my hand or for the money,' and the man did so, and there was nothing in her hand, three dirhams are obligatory on her. The woman made khul' on a runaway slave with the condition that she is innocent of him, she is not innocent, and the 'ayn (specific property) of the slave is on her. Definition of I'la'. Chapter of I'la'. If he fulfills within four months, he has committed perjury in his oath and expiation is obligatory. [Garbled text] He swore for four months, the oath expires with the passage of the period; however, if he rescinded the oath, it remains. One who swears for less than four months is not a muli. He swore with these words: 'I will not approach you for two months, two months after these two months,' then he is a muli. The husband said, 'By Allah, I will not approach you for two months,' then remained silent for a day, then said, 'By Allah, I will not approach you for two months after the first two months,' he is not a muli. The husband said, 'By Allah, I will not approach you for a year except for a day,' he is not a muli. Imam Zufar's viewpoint. A man in Basra said, 'By Allah, I will not enter Kufa,' and his wife was with him, he is not a muli. If he swears by hajj, fasting, charity, [unclear] or divorce, then he is a muli. If he makes i'la' with a revocably divorced woman, he is a muli; with an irrevocably divorced woman, he is not a muli. If he said to a foreign woman, 'By Allah, I will not approach you, and you are like my mother's back,' then married her, he is not a muli nor a muzahir. The duration of i'la' for a slave girl. If the muli is sick and unable to have intercourse, or the woman is sick, [unclear] or a minor with whom intercourse cannot occur, or there is a distance between them such that he cannot reach her during the i'la' period, then for him the method of ruju'. The ruling on saying to the woman 'You are unlawful to me.' Chapter of Khul'. (Duplicate of earlier text.)
Source pages p. 5

Commentary
This passage combines two major topics: khul' (divorce at the wife's instance by payment) and i'la' (a husband's vow to abstain from intercourse). For khul', the text emphasizes that it is permissible when conflict arises. If the husband is at fault, taking compensation is makruh; if the wife is nashizah (rebellious), taking more than what he gave is also makruh, but if he took more, it is still valid in qada'. The compensation must be something that can validly be mahr. Several hypothetical cases illustrate when compensation is or is not owed. For i'la', the definition is a vow to avoid intercourse for more than four months; if he returns within four months, he breaks his oath and pays kaffarah. Various expressions and conditions are examined, including Imam Zufar's view. The passage also discusses i'la' with a revocable versus irrevocable divorced woman, and the effect of conditions like sickness or distance. The text ends with a repetition of the khul' section, likely a copying error in the OCR.

Key Terms
ایلاء (īlāʾ): A husband's vow to abstain from sexual relations with his wife for more than four months.
مولی (mūlī): A husband who has taken an oath of i'la'.
کفارہ (kaffārah): Expiation for breaking an oath, e.g., feeding or clothing ten poor people or freeing a slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband swears, 'By Allah, I will not approach my wife for four months,' what is the ruling?
A) He is a muli and must pay kaffarah after four months.
B) He is not a muli because the period is exactly four months.
C) He is a muli and must decide within four months.
D) The oath is invalid.

Key Takeaway
I'la' is defined by a vow of abstinence exceeding four months; oaths of exactly four months or less do not make the husband a muli.

Talaq — Divorce
beginner
8 min
Core Rulings of Khul' (Conditions and Compensation Validity)
Opening rules of khul' with conditions and compensation cases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid khul' and identify when compensation is obligatory or invalid.

Core Idea
Khul' requires the wife's payment and the husband's consent; only items valid as mahr can be compensation.

This lesson draws from the opening section of Bab al-Khul' to establish the basic framework of khul' (divorce by wife's payment). We will cover when khul' is permissible, what compensation is valid, and the rulings when compensation is vague or absent. The passage gives concrete scenarios to illustrate the principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that khul' is a valid divorce initiated by the wife paying compensation. The text states permissibility when there is fear of rights not being fulfilled.
2
Distinguish blame between spouses
Note the ruling: if the husband is rebellious, taking compensation is makruh; if the wife is nashizah, taking more than what the husband gave is also makruh. This affects moral permissibility but not legal validity.
3
Determine valid compensation
Anything that can be mahr can be compensation. Invalid items (wine, swine) render khul' invalid. The compensation must be specified and existing.
Contrast with vague offers like 'whatever is in my hand' – if nothing, no compensation due.
4
Apply rules to partial divorce
If the wife asks for three divorces for a specific sum but the husband gives one, only a proportional amount is due (e.g., one-third of the sum for one divorce).

Source Text

باب الخلع

میاں بیوی کو جھگڑ کا خوف ہو کہ ایک دوسرے کے حقوق ادانہیں کر میں تو عورت مال دے کر خلع کر سکتی ہے سرکشی شوہر کی جانب سے ہو تو اس کیلئے بدل خلع لینا مکروہ ہے

اگر عورت ناشزہ ہے تو مرد کیلئے دیئے ہوئے سے زیادہ وصول کرنا مکروہ ہے

اگر مرد نے مہر سے زیادہ وصول کر لیا تو قضاء لینا جائز ہے

شوہر نے مال کے عوض طلاق دی عورت نے اسے قبول کیا تو عورت پر مال لازم ہے مسلمان کیلئے شراب یا خنزیر کے عوض خلع کرنے کا حکم جو چیز مہر بننے کی صلاحیت رکھتی ہے وہ بدل ضلع بھی بن سکتی ہے

عورت نے مرد سے کہا جو کچھ میرے ہاتھ میں ہے اس پر ضلع کرلے اور عورت کے ہاتھ میں کچھ نہیں تھا عورت پر کچھ بھی لازم نہیں ہوگا

عورت نے کہا خالعنی علی مافی یدی من مال عورت کے ہاتھ میں کچھ بھی نہیں تھا تو مہر لوٹانا عورت پر لازم ہے عورت نے کہا خالعنی علی مافی یدی من دراہم او من الدار هم مرد نے ایسا کر لیا عورت کے ہاتھ میں کچھ بھی نہیں تھا عورت پر تین دراہم لازم ہیں عورت نے بھاگے ہوئے غلام پر ضلع کر لیا اس شرط پر کہ وہ اس سے بری ہے عورت بری نہیں ہوگی عورت پر غلام کا عین

سپر د کر نالازم ہے اور بحر متحقق ہونے کی صورت میں قیمت لازم ہے عورت نے کہا طلقنی ثلاثہ بالف شوہر نے ایک طلاق دیدی عورت پر ثلث الف لازم ہے

عورت نے کہا طلقنی علی الف شوہر نے ایک طلاق دیدی عورت پر کچھ لازم ہوگا یا نہیں اور شوہر کو رجوع کا حق ہوگا یا نہیں، اقوال فقہاء

شوہر نے کہا طلقی نفسک ثلاثا بالف یا علی الف عورت نے اپنے آپ کو ایک طلاق دی کوئی بھی طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی شوہر نے کہا انت طالق علی الف عورت نے قبول کر لیا عورت مطلقہ ہو جائے گی اور عورت پر ہزار لازم ہوں گے شوہر نے اپنی بیوی کو کہا انت طالق و علیک الف عورت نے قبول کر لیا یا آقا نے غلام کو کہا انت حر و علیک الف غلام نے قبول کر لیا غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا اور عورت مطلقہ ہوگی اور دونوں پر کچھ لازم نہیں ہوگا، اقوال فقہاء شوہر نے کہا انت طالق علی الف اس شرط پر کہ مجھے خیار ہے یا مجھے تین دن کا خیار ہوگا عورت نے قبول کر لیا اگر خیار شوہر کیلئے ہے تو باطل ہے اور اگر عورت کیلئے ہے تو جائز ہے اور اگر عورت نے تین دن میں رد کر دیا تو خیار باطل ہے شوہر نے بیوی کو کہا طلقتک علی الف درہم فلم تقبلی عورت نے کہا میں نے قبول کیا تھا کس کا قول معتبر ہوگا اور اگر بائع مشتری کو کہا بعت منك هذا العبد بالف درہم فلم تقبل مشتری نے کہا میں نے قبول کیا تھا مشتری کا قول معتبر ہو گا وجہ فرق

مبارات خلع کی طرح ہے یا نہیں، اقوال فقہاء

جس شخص نے اپنی صغیرہ بیٹی کا مال کے بدلے ضلع کیا یہ ضلع درست نہیں شوہر نے ہزار پر خلع کیا اس شرط پر کہ لڑکی کا باپ ضامن ہو گا ضلع ہو جائے گا اور ہزار باپ پر لازم ہوگا شوہر نے ایک ہزار کو صغیرہ پر شرط کیا تو ضلع عورت کے قبول کرنے پر موقوف ہوگا اگر عورت اہل قبول میں سے ہے عورت نے قبول کر لیا طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی شرط کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے اور مال واجب نہیں ہوگا شوہر نے صغیرہ سے اس کے مہر پر ضلع کیا اور باپ مہر کا ضامن نہیں تو صغیرہ کے قبول کرنے پر موقوف ہوگا اگر باپ مہر کا ضامن ہو گیا عورت مطلقہ ہو جائے گی
Chapter of Khul'

If there is fear of quarrel between husband and wife such that they cannot fulfill each other's rights, the wife can obtain khul' by giving wealth. If the rebellion is from the husband's side, taking compensation for khul' is makruh.

If the wife is nashizah (disobedient), it is makruh for the husband to take more than what he gave.

If the husband took more than the mahr, it is permissible to take it by court order.

The husband divorced in exchange for wealth and the wife accepted, then the wealth is obligatory upon the wife. Ruling on a Muslim performing khul' in exchange for wine or swine: anything that can be valid as mahr can be compensation for khul'.

If the wife said to the husband: 'Divorce me in exchange for whatever is in my hand' and there was nothing in her hand, nothing is obligatory upon the wife.

If the wife said: 'Divorce me in exchange for whatever wealth is in my hand' and there was nothing in her hand, then returning the mahr is obligatory upon the wife. If the wife said: 'Divorce me in exchange for whatever dirhams or house are in my hand' and the husband did so while there was nothing in her hand, three dirhams are obligatory upon the wife. If the wife divorced in exchange for a runaway slave on condition that she is free from him, she is not free; the slave's 'ayn (physical object) is obligatory upon the wife to hand over, and if confirmed by evidence, the value is obligatory. If the wife said: 'Divorce me three times for a thousand' and the husband gave one divorce, one-third of a thousand is obligatory upon the wife. If the wife said: 'Divorce me upon a thousand' and the husband gave one divorce, is anything obligatory upon her and does the husband have the right to take her back? (Statements of jurists.) If the husband said: 'Divorce yourself three times for a thousand' or 'upon a thousand' and the wife gave herself one divorce, no divorce occurs. If the husband said: 'You are divorced upon a thousand' and the wife accepted, she becomes divorced and a thousand is obligatory upon her. If the husband said to his wife: 'You are divorced and upon you is a thousand' and she accepted, or a master said to his slave: 'You are free and upon you is a thousand' and the slave accepted, the slave becomes free and the wife becomes divorced, but nothing is obligatory upon either of them. (Statements of jurists.) If the husband said: 'You are divorced upon a thousand on condition that I have the option' or 'I have three days' option' and the wife accepted: if the option is for the husband, it is invalid; if for the wife, it is valid. If the wife rejects within three days, the option is void. If the husband said to his wife: 'I divorce you upon a thousand dirhams, but you did not accept' and the wife said: 'I did accept', whose statement is accepted? And if a seller said to a buyer: 'I sold you this slave for a thousand dirhams, but you did not accept' and the buyer said: 'I did accept', the buyer's statement is accepted. The reason for the difference.

Mubarat is similar to khul' or not? (Statements of jurists.)

If a person performed khul' for his minor daughter in exchange for wealth, this khul' is not valid. If the husband performed khul' for one thousand on condition that the girl's father is guarantor, the khul' is valid and the thousand is obligatory upon the father. If the husband made the thousand conditional upon the minor, the khul' is suspended upon the wife's acceptance. If the wife is among those capable of acceptance and she accepts, the divorce occurs due to the condition being fulfilled, but the wealth is not obligatory. If the husband performed khul' from the minor in exchange for her mahr and the father is not guarantor of the mahr, it is suspended upon the minor's acceptance. If the father becomes guarantor of the mahr, the wife becomes divorced.
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah covers the chapter of Khul' (divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation). It begins by stating the permissibility of Khul' when there is fear that the spouses cannot fulfill each other's rights. If the husband is the rebellious one, it is makruh for him to take compensation; if the wife is nashizah (disobedient), taking more than what the husband gave is also makruh. However, if the husband already took more, it is permissible to enforce repayment through the court. The text then details various scenarios: Khul' in exchange for invalid items like wine or swine is invalid; only items valid as mahr can serve as compensation. Cases where the wife offers 'whatever is in her hand' but has nothing result in no obligation, but if she specifies 'wealth', she must return the mahr. Similarly, specifying dirhams or a house obligates a specific amount. Khul' in exchange for a runaway slave requires handing over the slave or paying its value. For partial divorces (e.g., asking for three divorces for a thousand but husband gives one), only a proportional amount is due. The text also discusses the validity of options in Khul' conditions: an option for the husband makes the contract invalid, while an option for the wife is valid. Disputes over acceptance are settled by the buyer's (or wife's) statement in analogy with sales. Finally, the section on Mubarat (mutual release) is compared to Khul', and special rules for a minor daughter's Khul' are given: if the father guarantees the compensation, Khul' is effective; otherwise, it is suspended upon the daughter's acceptance.

Key Terms
خلع (khul'): A divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation paid to the husband.
ناشزہ (nashizah): A disobedient wife who does not fulfill marital duties.
مهر (mahr): Mandatory bridal gift from husband to wife at marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What makes a khul' compensation invalid?
A) The compensation is less than the mahr.
B) The compensation is wine.
C) The wife offers nothing.
D) The husband refuses.

Key Takeaway
Khul' is valid when the wife offers valid compensation and the husband accepts; vague offers may not obligate payment.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
10 min
Advanced Scenarios in Khul' (Options, Disputes, Mubarat, Minor's Khul')
Detailed scenarios: partial divorce, options, disputes, mubarat, minor's khul'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Hanafi rules to khul' scenarios involving partial divorces, options in the contract, disputes over acceptance, and khul' of a minor daughter.

Core Idea
Options in khul' favor the wife; disputes over acceptance are resolved like sales; minor's khul' requires guardian guarantee.

This lesson continues with the latter part of Bab al-Khul', covering more complex cases: partial divorces (where the wife requests three but receives one), conditions of option (khiyar) attached to khul', disputes over acceptance (analogy to sales), the nature of mubarat (mutual release), and the special rules for a father performing khul' on behalf of his minor daughter. These scenarios demonstrate the Hanafi method of extrapolating rulings from established principles.

Guided Path
1
Analyze proportional compensation in partial divorce
If a wife requests three divorces for a specified sum and the husband gives one, only one-third of the sum is due. This is based on the principle of apportionment.
2
Distinguish options in khul' for husband vs wife
If the husband stipulates an option (e.g., three days to decide), it invalidates the khul'. If the wife has the option, it is valid, and she can reject within that period.
Reason: khul' is initiated by the wife, so her option is consistent with her control.
3
Resolve disputes over acceptance using sale analogy
When husband says 'I divorced you for a thousand, you did not accept' and wife says 'I accepted', the wife's statement is accepted (like the buyer in a sale).
The analogy: khul' is treated as a transaction (compensation for divorce).
4
Compare mubarat with khul'
Mubarat is similar but often without compensation; some jurists say it is identical, others differentiate. The text presents differing opinions.
5
Apply rules for minor daughter's khul'
Khul' of a minor daughter by her father is not valid unless the father guarantees the compensation. If guaranteed, khul' is effective and compensation is on the father.
If the compensation is conditioned on the minor's acceptance, it must be suspended until she becomes capable of accepting.

Source Text

باب الخلع

اگر عورت ناشزہ ہے تو مرد کیلئے دیئے ہوئے سے زیادہ وصول کرنا مکروہ ہے

اگر مرد نے مہر سے زیادہ وصول کر لیا تو قضاء لینا جائز ہے

شوہر نے مال کے عوض طلاق دی عورت نے اسے قبول کیا تو عورت پر مال لازم ہے مسلمان کیلئے شراب یا خنزیر کے عوض خلع کرنے کا حکم جو چیز مہر بننے کی صلاحیت رکھتی ہے وہ بدل ضلع بھی بن سکتی ہے

عورت نے مرد سے کہا جو کچھ میرے ہاتھ میں ہے اس پر ضلع کرلے اور عورت کے ہاتھ میں کچھ نہیں تھا عورت پر کچھ بھی لازم نہیں ہوگا

عورت نے کہا خالعنی علی مافی یدی من مال عورت کے ہاتھ میں کچھ بھی نہیں تھا تو مہر لوٹانا عورت پر لازم ہے عورت نے کہا خالعنی علی مافی یدی من دراہم او من الدار هم مرد نے ایسا کر لیا عورت کے ہاتھ میں کچھ بھی نہیں تھا عورت پر تین دراہم لازم ہیں عورت نے بھاگے ہوئے غلام پر ضلع کر لیا اس شرط پر کہ وہ اس سے بری ہے عورت بری نہیں ہوگی عورت پر غلام کا عین

سپر د کر نالازم ہے اور بحر متحقق ہونے کی صورت میں قیمت لازم ہے عورت نے کہا طلقنی ثلاثہ بالف شوہر نے ایک طلاق دیدی عورت پر ثلث الف لازم ہے

عورت نے کہا طلقنی علی الف شوہر نے ایک طلاق دیدی عورت پر کچھ لازم ہوگا یا نہیں اور شوہر کو رجوع کا حق ہوگا یا نہیں، اقوال فقہاء

شوہر نے کہا طلقی نفسک ثلاثا بالف یا علی الف عورت نے اپنے آپ کو ایک طلاق دی کوئی بھی طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی شوہر نے کہا انت طالق علی الف عورت نے قبول کر لیا عورت مطلقہ ہو جائے گی اور عورت پر ہزار لازم ہوں گے شوہر نے اپنی بیوی کو کہا انت طالق و علیک الف عورت نے قبول کر لیا یا آقا نے غلام کو کہا انت حر و علیک الف غلام نے قبول کر لیا غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا اور عورت مطلقہ ہوگی اور دونوں پر کچھ لازم نہیں ہوگا، اقوال فقہاء شوہر نے کہا انت طالق علی الف اس شرط پر کہ مجھے خیار ہے یا مجھے تین دن کا خیار ہوگا عورت نے قبول کر لیا اگر خیار شوہر کیلئے ہے تو باطل ہے اور اگر عورت کیلئے ہے تو جائز ہے اور اگر عورت نے تین دن میں رد کر دیا تو خیار باطل ہے شوہر نے بیوی کو کہا طلقتک علی الف درہم فلم تقبلی عورت نے کہا میں نے قبول کیا تھا کس کا قول معتبر ہوگا اور اگر بائع مشتری کو کہا بعت منك هذا العبد بالف درہم فلم تقبل مشتری نے کہا میں نے قبول کیا تھا مشتری کا قول معتبر ہو گا وجہ فرق

مبارات خلع کی طرح ہے یا نہیں، اقوال فقہاء

جس شخص نے اپنی صغیرہ بیٹی کا مال کے بدلے ضلع کیا یہ ضلع درست نہیں شوہر نے ہزار پر خلع کیا اس شرط پر کہ لڑکی کا باپ ضامن ہو گا ضلع ہو جائے گا اور ہزار باپ پر لازم ہوگا شوہر نے ایک ہزار کو صغیرہ پر شرط کیا تو ضلع عورت کے قبول کرنے پر موقوف ہوگا اگر عورت اہل قبول میں سے ہے عورت نے قبول کر لیا طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی شرط کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے اور مال واجب نہیں ہوگا شوہر نے صغیرہ سے اس کے مہر پر ضلع کیا اور باپ مہر کا ضامن نہیں تو صغیرہ کے قبول کرنے پر موقوف ہوگا اگر باپ مہر کا ضامن ہو گیا عورت مطلقہ ہو جائے گی
Chapter of Khul'

If there is fear of quarrel between husband and wife such that they cannot fulfill each other's rights, the wife can obtain khul' by giving wealth. If the rebellion is from the husband's side, taking compensation for khul' is makruh.

If the wife is nashizah (disobedient), it is makruh for the husband to take more than what he gave.

If the husband took more than the mahr, it is permissible to take it by court order.

The husband divorced in exchange for wealth and the wife accepted, then the wealth is obligatory upon the wife. Ruling on a Muslim performing khul' in exchange for wine or swine: anything that can be valid as mahr can be compensation for khul'.

If the wife said to the husband: 'Divorce me in exchange for whatever is in my hand' and there was nothing in her hand, nothing is obligatory upon the wife.

If the wife said: 'Divorce me in exchange for whatever wealth is in my hand' and there was nothing in her hand, then returning the mahr is obligatory upon the wife. If the wife said: 'Divorce me in exchange for whatever dirhams or house are in my hand' and the husband did so while there was nothing in her hand, three dirhams are obligatory upon the wife. If the wife divorced in exchange for a runaway slave on condition that she is free from him, she is not free; the slave's 'ayn (physical object) is obligatory upon the wife to hand over, and if confirmed by evidence, the value is obligatory. If the wife said: 'Divorce me three times for a thousand' and the husband gave one divorce, one-third of a thousand is obligatory upon the wife. If the wife said: 'Divorce me upon a thousand' and the husband gave one divorce, is anything obligatory upon her and does the husband have the right to take her back? (Statements of jurists.) If the husband said: 'Divorce yourself three times for a thousand' or 'upon a thousand' and the wife gave herself one divorce, no divorce occurs. If the husband said: 'You are divorced upon a thousand' and the wife accepted, she becomes divorced and a thousand is obligatory upon her. If the husband said to his wife: 'You are divorced and upon you is a thousand' and she accepted, or a master said to his slave: 'You are free and upon you is a thousand' and the slave accepted, the slave becomes free and the wife becomes divorced, but nothing is obligatory upon either of them. (Statements of jurists.) If the husband said: 'You are divorced upon a thousand on condition that I have the option' or 'I have three days' option' and the wife accepted: if the option is for the husband, it is invalid; if for the wife, it is valid. If the wife rejects within three days, the option is void. If the husband said to his wife: 'I divorce you upon a thousand dirhams, but you did not accept' and the wife said: 'I did accept', whose statement is accepted? And if a seller said to a buyer: 'I sold you this slave for a thousand dirhams, but you did not accept' and the buyer said: 'I did accept', the buyer's statement is accepted. The reason for the difference.

Mubarat is similar to khul' or not? (Statements of jurists.)

If a person performed khul' for his minor daughter in exchange for wealth, this khul' is not valid. If the husband performed khul' for one thousand on condition that the girl's father is guarantor, the khul' is valid and the thousand is obligatory upon the father. If the husband made the thousand conditional upon the minor, the khul' is suspended upon the wife's acceptance. If the wife is among those capable of acceptance and she accepts, the divorce occurs due to the condition being fulfilled, but the wealth is not obligatory. If the husband performed khul' from the minor in exchange for her mahr and the father is not guarantor of the mahr, it is suspended upon the minor's acceptance. If the father becomes guarantor of the mahr, the wife becomes divorced.
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah covers the chapter of Khul' (divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation). It begins by stating the permissibility of Khul' when there is fear that the spouses cannot fulfill each other's rights. If the husband is the rebellious one, it is makruh for him to take compensation; if the wife is nashizah (disobedient), taking more than what the husband gave is also makruh. However, if the husband already took more, it is permissible to enforce repayment through the court. The text then details various scenarios: Khul' in exchange for invalid items like wine or swine is invalid; only items valid as mahr can serve as compensation. Cases where the wife offers 'whatever is in her hand' but has nothing result in no obligation, but if she specifies 'wealth', she must return the mahr. Similarly, specifying dirhams or a house obligates a specific amount. Khul' in exchange for a runaway slave requires handing over the slave or paying its value. For partial divorces (e.g., asking for three divorces for a thousand but husband gives one), only a proportional amount is due. The text also discusses the validity of options in Khul' conditions: an option for the husband makes the contract invalid, while an option for the wife is valid. Disputes over acceptance are settled by the buyer's (or wife's) statement in analogy with sales. Finally, the section on Mubarat (mutual release) is compared to Khul', and special rules for a minor daughter's Khul' are given: if the father guarantees the compensation, Khul' is effective; otherwise, it is suspended upon the daughter's acceptance.

Key Terms
مبارات (mubarat): A mutual release from marriage, similar to khul', often without compensation.
خیار (khiyar): Option or right to cancel a contract within a specified period.
صغیرہ (saghirah): Minor daughter (not yet reached puberty).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if a husband says 'You are divorced and upon you is a thousand' (using 'and')?
A) The divorce occurs and she must pay.
B) The divorce occurs but she pays nothing.
C) The divorce does not occur.
D) It is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The finer points of khul' include proportional compensation, the invalidity of husband's option, and the special rules for minors, all derived from transaction principles.

Rulings on Zihar (Injurious Divorce)
Defines Zihar, its effects, and various analogies that constitute Zihar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of Zihar, identify its legal effects, and apply the ruling to various analogical statements.

Core Idea
Zihar makes intercourse haram until expiation; comparing wife to any mahram woman suffices.

In this lesson, we examine the chapter on Zihar from Ashraf al-Hidayah. Zihar is a pre-Islamic practice where a husband compares his wife to a mahram woman, such as his mother, resulting in a temporary prohibition of intercourse. The text clarifies the exact wording that constitutes Zihar and the consequences before expiation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic ruling and its effect
Read the first part of the passage: the husband says 'you are to me like my mother's back'. Note that intercourse and kissing become haram before expiation.
The prohibition is temporary; expiation lifts it.
2
Determine the scope of analogies
The text then lists various body parts (belly, thigh, head, etc.) and concludes that comparing to any mahram woman constitutes Zihar. Understand that the Hanafi school expands Zihar beyond the literal wording.
Any mahram comparison qualifies, not only the back.
3
Understand the consequence of intercourse before expiation
If intercourse occurs before expiation, the husband should seek forgiveness and no additional obligation is mentioned.
Repentance is required; the original expiation remains necessary to lift the prohibition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الظهار

شوہر نے بیوی کو کہا انت علی کظہر امی عورت مرد پر حرام ہو جائے گی کفارہ ادا کرنے سے پہلے دلی ہمس، اور تقبیل حرام ہے

کفارہ سے پہلے ولی کر لی استغفار کرے اور کچھ لازم نہیں ہے شوہر نے بیوی کو کہا انت علی کبطن امی یا کفخذ بایا کفر جہا کہا یہ مظاہر ہوگا کسی محرمہ کے ساتھ تشبیہ دے دینے سے بھی مظاہر ہوگا شوہر نے بیوی کو راسک علی کظیر امی اوفرجک اور چہک اور قتک اونصفک اوشلسٹک کہا مظاہر ہوگا
Chapter of Zihar

The husband said to his wife: 'You are to me like my mother's back' – the woman becomes haram upon the man. Before expiation, intercourse and kissing are haram.

Before expiation, if he does intercourse, he should seek forgiveness and nothing else is obligatory. If the husband said to his wife: 'You are like my mother's belly' or 'like her thigh' or 'like her [کفر]', this is Zihar. Comparing to any mahram woman also constitutes Zihar. If the husband said: 'Your head is like my mother's head' or 'your private part' or 'your face' or 'your neck' or 'half of you' or 'your leg', it is Zihar.
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explains the rulings of Zihar, a pre-Islamic practice where a husband compares his wife to a mahram woman (like his mother). Upon pronouncing such words, intercourse becomes haram until expiation is performed. The text specifies that before expiation, both intercourse and kissing are prohibited. If he commits intercourse before expiation, he must seek forgiveness, but no other penalty is mentioned. The definition of Zihar includes not only the classic 'like my mother's back' but also other body parts like belly, thigh, or any mahram woman. Even comparing specific body parts like head, private part, face, neck, half of the body, or leg constitutes Zihar. This highlights the Hanafi view that the prohibition is based on the element of disrespect and comparison to a mahram, not just a specific verbal formula.

Key Terms
ظہار (zihar): A husband's statement comparing his wife to a mahram woman, making intercourse temporarily haram.
محرمہ (mahramah): A woman forever prohibited for marriage due to blood or fosterage ties.
کفارہ (kaffarah): Expiation required to lift the prohibition of Zihar, which can be freeing a slave, fasting two consecutive months, or feeding sixty poor people.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following statements is explicitly mentioned in the passage as constituting Zihar?
A) 'You are like my mother's back.'
B) 'You are like my sister's back.'
C) 'Your hand is like my mother's hand.'
D) 'I divorce you.'

Key Takeaway
Zihar is a temporary prohibition of intercourse triggered by a husband's comparison of his wife to a mahram woman, and it is lifted by expiation.

Zihar: Definition, Ruling, and Conditions
Introduction to zihar, its conditions, and differences with other types of divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define zihar in Hanafi fiqh, state its ruling and conditions, and distinguish it from divorce and ila'.

Core Idea
Zihar makes the wife forbidden until expiation — a unique prohibition that is not divorce or ila'.

Zihar is a pre-Islamic practice of likening one's wife to a mahram relative, which Islam regulated by requiring expiation. This lesson covers the precise definition, the types of statements that constitute zihar, and the conditions that affect its validity. We will also see how the Hanafi school differs from the Shafi'i on the required wording.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its definition
Locate the core definition of zihar in the text: a husband comparing his wife to a mahram relative (e.g., 'like the back of my mother'). Understand that this is a statement, not a divorce.
The comparison must be to a mahram by lineage (e.g., mother, sister, etc.).
2
State the legal ruling (hukm) and its level
The ruling is that sexual relations become haram until the husband performs expiation (kaffarah). The act of saying the words itself is not sinful, but the prohibition that follows is a serious obligation.
The kaffarah is either freeing a slave (or equivalent), fasting two consecutive months, or feeding sixty poor people.
3
List the conditions for validity
The passage mentions that zihar only applies to a wife (not a slave girl) and requires a valid marriage at the time of the statement. If the marriage was contracted without the woman's consent and she later approves, the zihar is invalid because it was said before the marriage was fully valid.
4
Distinguish zihar from divorce and ila'
If the husband says 'you are haram' without a comparison, the ruling depends on his intention: if he intends zihar, it is zihar; if divorce, it is divorce; if ila' (oath of abstention), it is ila'. The text also notes that saying 'you are haram like the back of my mother' with the intention of divorce gives zihar, not divorce.
This shows that intention (niyyah) is decisive when the wording could be interpreted multiple ways.
5
Note the practical consequences
Before expiation, even kissing is forbidden. If the husband engages in relations before expiation, he must repent but no additional penalty. Multiple wives: saying 'you all are like the back of my mother' makes zihar with each.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الظهار شوہر نے بیوی کو کہا انت علی کظہر امی عورت مرد پر حرام ہو جائے گی کفارہ ادا کرنے سے پہلے دلی ہمس ، اور تقبیل حرام ہے کفارہ سے پہلے ولی کر لی استغفار کرے اور کچھ لازم نہیں ہے شوہر نے بیوی کو کہا انت علی کبطن امی یا کفخذ بایا کفر جہا کہا یہ مظاہر ہوگا کسی محرمہ کے ساتھ تشبیہ دے دینے سے بھی مظاہر ہوگا شوہر نے بیوی کو راسک علی کظیر امی اوفرجک اور چہک اور قتک اونصفک اوشلسٹک کہا مظاہر ہوگا اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم شوہر کا باندی کو انت علی مثل امی او کامی کہنے کا حکم شوہر کا بیوی کو انت علی حرام کا می کہا اور ظہار کی نیت یا طلاق کی نیت کی اس کی نیت پر مدار ہو گا شوہر نے بیوی کو انت علی حرام کظہر امی کہا اور طلاق یا ایلاء کی نیت کی ظہار ہوگا یا ایلاء ، اقوال فقہاء ظہار صرف بیوی سے ہوتا ہے باندی سے نہیں عورت سے اس کے امر کے بغیر نکاح کیا پھر اس سے ظہار کیا پھر عورت نے اس نکاح کی اجازت دی ظہار باطل ہے شوہر نے اپنی بیویوں کو کہا انتن علی کظہر امی سب سے ظہار کرنے والا ہو گا
Chapter of Zihar. The husband said to his wife: 'You are to me like the back of my mother.' The woman becomes forbidden to the man. Before paying expiation, sexual intercourse and kissing are forbidden. Before expiation, if he does wali, he should seek forgiveness, and nothing is necessary. The husband said to his wife: 'You are to me like the belly of my mother' or 'like the thigh of my mother [؟]', he said this is zihar. Even by likening to any mahram, it is zihar. The husband said to his wife: 'Your head is like the back of my mother' or 'your genitals' or 'your cheek' or 'your neck' or 'half of you' or 'your waist', he said this is zihar. Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya Volume Five. The ruling of the husband saying to his slave girl 'you are to me like my mother' or 'like my [؟]'. The husband said to his wife 'you are to me haram' and intended zihar or intended divorce; it depends on his intention. The husband said to his wife 'you are to me haram like the back of my mother' and intended divorce or ila'; it will be zihar or ila'? Statements of the jurists. Zihar only occurs with a wife, not with a slave girl. A man married a woman without her command, then made zihar with her, then the woman permitted the marriage: the zihar is invalid. The husband said to his wives: 'You all are to me like the back of my mother'; he becomes a mazahir with all of them.
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on zihar (injurious assimilation). Zihar is defined as a husband saying to his wife 'You are to me like the back of my mother,' which makes her forbidden to him until he performs expiation (kaffarah). Before expiation, even intimate acts like kissing are prohibited. If he approaches her before expiation, he must repent but no additional penalty is incurred. The passage then extends the ruling to other body parts (belly, thigh) and even comparing any mahram relative. It also covers partial statements (your head, your genitals) - all are zihar. The section on page 8 addresses that if the husband says 'you are haram' with the intention of zihar, it is zihar; if he intends divorce, it is divorce; if he intends ila' (oath of abstention), it is ila'. Zihar only applies to a wife, not to a slave girl. If a man marries a woman without her consent (e.g., through a guardian), then makes zihar, and later the woman approves the marriage, the zihar is invalid because the marriage was not fully valid at the time of the statement. If a husband says 'you all (plural) are like the back of my mother' to all his wives, it is zihar with each.

Key Terms
ظہار (zihar): A husband saying his wife is like a mahram relative, making her forbidden until expiation.
کفارہ (kaffarah): Expiation due for zihar: freeing a slave, fasting two months, or feeding sixty poor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following statements is NOT considered zihar?
A) 'You are to me like the belly of my sister.'
B) 'You are to me like the back of my mother.'
C) 'You are to me like the queen of England.'
D) 'Your genitals are like my mother's genitals.'

Key Takeaway
Zihar is a prohibition triggered by comparing one's wife to a mahram, requiring expiation before marital relations resume, and in Hanafi fiqh, any body part suffices for the comparison.

Dispelling Multiple Kaffarah for Zihar
Rulings on kaffarah for zihar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on intercourse during feeding kaffarah and explain how multiple expiations for zihar are discharged.

Core Idea
Intercourse during feeding does not break kaffarah; one act cannot satisfy two separate expiations.

This passage addresses two practical scenarios for those performing kaffarah for zihar. First, what happens if one has intercourse during the feeding expiation? Second, how are multiple expiations handled when only one act of freeing or feeding is performed? The text provides clear rulings based on the Hanafi position and highlights the importance of intention in discharging multiple obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The text contains two distinct rulings: one about intercourse during the feeding period, and another about discharging multiple zihar expiations with a single act.
2
Analyze the ruling on intercourse during feeding
If a man has intercourse with his wife while in the midst of feeding sixty poor people, he does not need to restart the feeding. The previous feeding remains valid.
This implies that intercourse does not nullify the ongoing expiation.
3
Analyze the ruling on multiple expiations with one act
If a man owes two separate zihar expiations and frees one slave or feeds sixty poor once, it only fulfills one expiation. He may choose which one to assign it to.
A single act cannot count for two distinct obligations unless specifically intended for one.
4
Note the role of intention
When performing multiple expiations, intention (niyyah) is crucial. If one act is done without specifying which expiation, it can be assigned later. But if intended for two different types (zihar and qatl), it fails for both.
Intention determines which obligation is satisfied.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہو گا مگر ایک ہی دن سے کھانے کھلانے کے درمیان بیوی سے جماع کر لیا از سر نو کھانا کھلانے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے اگر دو کفارہ ظہار کی جانب سے صرف صاٹھ مسکین کو کھانا کھلایا کافی نہیں ہو گا مگر ایک ہی کفارہ ہے۔ جس پر دو کفارہ ظہار لازم تھے دو غلاموں کو آزاد کر دیا کسی ایک معین سے کفارہ معینہ کی نیت نہیں کی اگر دو کفاروں کی طرف سے ایک ہی گردن آزاد کی یا ساٹھ مساکین کو کھانا کھلایا اسے اختیار ہے جس کفارہ کی طرف سے اسے کردے اگر ایک غلام کفارہ ظہار اور قتل کی طرف سے ادا کیا کسی سے بھی کافی نہیں ہوگا ، اقوال فقہاء
But if on a single day, between feeding, he had intercourse with his wife, there is no need to feed anew. If from the side of two zihar kaffarahs, he fed only sixty poor persons, it will not suffice for both, but only one kaffarah. He upon whom two zihar kaffarahs were obligatory freed two slaves without intending a specific kaffarah for each: if he freed one neck or fed sixty poor for two kaffarahs, he has the option to assign it to whichever kaffarah he wishes. If he freed one slave for the kaffarah of zihar and qatl, it will not suffice for either. Statements of the jurists.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage contains rulings on discharging multiple expiations (kaffarah) for zihar, which is a type of divorce-like oath. The first ruling clarifies that if a man who is feeding sixty poor people as expiation has intercourse with his wife during the feeding period, he does not need to restart the feeding; the previous feeding remains valid. This is because the expiation is a single continuous act and interruption does not invalidate it. The second ruling addresses a scenario where a man owes two separate expiations for zihar (e.g., due to two occurrences). If he feeds only sixty poor persons intending both, it suffices for only one; the other remains due. Similarly, if he frees one slave intending both, it counts for only one. However, if he frees two slaves without specifying which slave is for which expiation, he can later assign each to whichever he wishes. If he frees one slave intending both zihar and qatl (manslaughter) expiation, it is insufficient for either because each expiation requires its own separate act unless one act is specifically intended for one. The Hanafi position is that intention (niyyah) is necessary to determine which obligation is fulfilled.

Key Terms
ظہار (zihar): A pre-Islamic practice where a husband says to his wife 'You are like my mother's back', requiring expiation before resuming marital relations.
کفارہ (kaffarah): Expiation for a sin or broken oath; for zihar it is freeing a slave or fasting two months or feeding sixty poor.
جماع (jima'): Sexual intercourse between husband and wife.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man owes two separate zihar expiations and frees one slave intending both, what is the ruling?
A) Both expiations are fulfilled.
B) Only one expiation is fulfilled; the other remains due.
C) Neither is fulfilled.
D) It depends on the judge's ruling.

Key Takeaway
For zihar kaffarah, intercourse does not nullify ongoing feeding, and one act cannot satisfy multiple expiations unless intended for a single one.

Definition and Conditions of Li'an
Defines li'an, its cause, and rulings on who can perform it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of li'an, identify its cause, and apply the conditions under which li'an is applicable or not.

Core Idea
Li'an replaces the hadd of qadhf only when both spouses are eligible for testimony.

Li'an is a unique legal procedure in Islamic family law that allows a husband who accuses his wife of adultery without witnesses to avoid the hadd punishment for false accusation (qadhf). Instead, both spouses exchange oaths of imprecation. However, li'an is not always available; the law imposes specific conditions on the eligibility of both spouses. This lesson unpacks the definition, cause, and the key restrictions outlined in the classical Hanafi text.

Guided Path
1
Define Li'an and Identify Its Cause
Start by extracting the definition of li'an from the passage and identifying the legal cause (sabab) that triggers it: a husband's accusation of adultery without witnesses.
The cause is the husband's claim of zina without four witnesses.
2
Analyze the Procedure When a Spouse Refuses
Note the ruling: if the husband refuses to li'an, the judge imprisons him until he either performs li'an or admits his accusation is false. The same applies to the wife.
This shows li'an is wajib upon the accuser to avoid punishment.
3
Identify Cases Where Li'an Is Not Applicable
The passage lists two categories: (1) when the husband is a slave, disbeliever, or previously punished for qadhf, and (2) when the wife is a slave, disbeliever, punished for qadhf, minor, insane, or a known fornicator. In these cases, li'an does not apply, and different rulings (hadd or no punishment) follow.
Li'an requires both spouses to be legally eligible to testify (ahliyyat al-shahada).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب اللعان۔ لعان کا موجب ، لعان کی تعریف شوہر لعان کرنے سے رک جائے تو حاکم اسے قید کر دے حتی کہ لعان کرے یا اپنے نفس کی تکذیب کرے اگر عورت لعان سے رک جائے حاکم اسے قید میں ڈال دے حتی کہ لعان کرے یا مرد کی تصدیق کرے شوہر اگر غلام ہو یا کافر یا محدود فی القذف ہو اپنی عورت پر تہمت لگائے اس پر حد ہے شوہر اگر اہل شہادت میں سے ہو اور بیوی باندی ہو یا کافرہ ہو یا محدودہ فی القذف ہو یا ایسی ہے کہ جس کے قاذف کو حد جاری نہیں کی جاتی جیسے بچی ہو یا مجنونہ ہو یا زانیہ شوہر پر حد نہیں ہے اور لعان بھی نہیں ہے
Chapter of Li'an. The cause of li'an. Definition of li'an. If the husband refrains from performing li'an, the judge confines him until he performs li'an or admits the falsehood. If the wife refrains from li'an, the judge confines her until she performs li'an or confirms the husband's accusation. If the husband is a slave, disbeliever, or one who has been punished for qadhf (false accusation of zina), and he slanders his wife, then hadd (punishment) is applied on him. If the husband is among those eligible for testimony and the wife is a female slave, a disbeliever, a woman punished for qadhf, or one whose slanderer does not receive hadd such as a minor, insane woman, or a known fornicator, then the husband is not subjected to hadd nor is li'an applicable.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage defines li'an (mutual imprecation) as a legal procedure for a husband who accuses his wife of adultery without witnesses. Instead of receiving the hadd punishment for false accusation (qadhf), he can li'an, and the wife must respond. If the husband refuses to li'an, the judge imprisons him until he either li'an or admits lying. The same applies to the wife. The text then lists cases where li'an is not applicable: if the husband is a slave, a disbeliever, or previously punished for qadhf, then if he slanders his wife, he receives hadd — not li'an. Conversely, if the husband is legally qualified to testify (free, Muslim, just) and the wife is a slave, disbeliever, or previously punished for qadhf, or she is a minor, insane, or a known fornicator, then the husband is not subjected to hadd and li'an does not occur. The reasoning is that li'an is only for cases where both spouses are eligible to testify and the accusation could be serious. The Hanafi school holds that li'an is a last resort to avoid hadd.

Key Terms
لعان (li'an): Mutual imprecation between spouses where they swear oaths to confirm or deny adultery.
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of adultery or fornication without four witnesses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a free Muslim husband accuses his slave wife of adultery without witnesses, what is the ruling?
A) He must perform li'an.
B) He receives hadd for qadhf.
C) He cannot perform li'an but is not punished.
D) The couple is divorced immediately.

Key Takeaway
Li'an is a conditional substitute for hadd, available only when both spouses are legally eligible to testify.
