The Procedure of Li'an and Its Legal Effects
Explains the li'an procedure, its effect on marriage, and child lineage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the steps of the li'an procedure and explain its effect on the marriage and child's lineage.

Core Idea
Li'an separates spouses permanently and negates the child's lineage from the husband.

Li'an is a unique procedure in Islamic law when a husband accuses his wife of adultery without witnesses. This passage from Al-Hidayah outlines the sequence of events: the mutual curse, the judge's separation, and the effect on the child. Understanding this procedure is crucial for distinguishing between li'an and regular divorce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the accusation
Determine the basis: the husband must accuse his wife of zina and deny paternity. If he only denies pregnancy without accusing zina, li'an is not required.
2
Trace the li'an process
The spouses perform mutual curses (li'an) in front of the judge. The husband swears five oaths, the wife responds similarly. After completion, the judge declares separation.
Hanafi fiqh details the exact wording.
3
Determine the effect on marriage
The judge's separation (tafreek) is a final divorce (bain), making the couple permanently prohibited from remarrying each other.
This is according to the majority Hanafi view, disputed by Imam Zufar.
4
Determine the effect on child
If the husband explicitly negated paternity, the judge negates the child's lineage from the husband and attaches it to the mother only.
The child inherits from mother and her relatives.
5
Note exceptions and timing
No li'an for a minor or insane wife. Negation must be made promptly after birth, congratulations, or purchase of delivery items; delay may still require li'an but lineage is established. For twins, acknowledging one establishes lineage for both.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لعان کی کیفیت جب میاں بیوی نے لعان کر لیا تو قاضی کی تفریق سے جدائی ہوگی امام زفر کا نقطہ نظر جو شخص اپنے آپ کو جھٹلا دے اس عورت سے نکاح کر سکتا ہے یا نہیں ، اقوال فقہاء اگر تہمت بچے کی نفی کی ہو قاضی بچے کے نسب کی نفی کر دے اور بچے کو ماں کے ساتھ لاحق کر دے اور لعان کی صورت اگر تہمت زنا کی ہو اور بچے کی نفی کرے تو لعان میں دو باتوں کا تذکرہ کیا جائے پھر اس بچے کے نسب کی نفی کرے اور ماں کے ساتھ لاحق کرے اگر شوہر نے رجوع کیا اور اپنے نفس کی تکذیب کی قاضی اس کے اقرار کی وجہ سے حد جاری کرے اور اس کیلئے نکاح کرنا حلال ہے جب صغیرہ مجنونہ بیوی کو قذف کیا ان دونوں میں لعان نہیں ہے شوہر نے کہا لیس حملک منی لعان نہیں ہو گا اگر کہ زنت و هذا الحبل من الزناء دونوں لعان کریں جب مرد نے اپنی بیوی کے بچے کی نفی کر دی ولادت کے بعد یا مبارک باد قبول کرنے کے وقت یا آلہ ولادت خرید تے وقت اس کی نفی صحیح ہے اور اس کے ساتھ لعان کرے گا اور اگر ان امور کے بعد نفی کی تو لعان کرے گا اور نسب ثابت ہوگا ایک حمل سے دو بچے جنے پہلے کی نفی کی اور دوسرے کا اعتراف کیا دونوں کا نسب ثابت ہو جائے گا
The procedure of li'an: When the spouses have performed li'an, separation occurs through the judge's ruling. Imam Zufar's viewpoint: Can a person who denies himself marry that woman? Statements of the jurists. If the accusation is the negation of the child, the judge negates the child's lineage and attaches the child to the mother. In the case of li'an, if the accusation is zina and negation of the child, then two matters are mentioned in li'an, then he negates the child's lineage and attaches to mother. If the husband retracts and admits falsehood, the judge implements hadd due to his confession, and marriage is permissible for him. When a minor or insane wife is slandered, li'an is not between them. If the husband says 'This pregnancy is not from me', li'an is not done. If he says 'She committed zina and this pregnancy is from zina', then both perform li'an. When a man negates his wife's child after birth, or at the time of accepting congratulations, or at the time of purchasing delivery tools, his negation is valid and he will perform li'an. If he negates after these matters, he will still perform li'an but the lineage will be established. If she gives birth to two children from one pregnancy, he negates the first and acknowledges the second, the lineage of both is established.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage details the procedure and effects of li'an. The first ruling states that after li'an, the judge separates the couple (tafreed), and this separation is a final divorce (bain). Imam Zufar's view is noted: he discusses whether a person who denies himself (i.e., retracts after li'an) can marry the same woman again. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute. According to the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa), the couple is permanently separated and cannot remarry. Imam Zufar may have a different opinion. Then the text explains the effect on the child: if the husband accuses the wife of adultery and also denies paternity of the child, the judge negates the child's lineage from the husband and attaches it to the mother. The husband must mention both zina and negation of child in his li'an statements. If the husband later retracts (by admitting falsehood), he receives hadd punishment for qadhf, but then the marriage becomes permissible for him (unlike after li'an where it is permanent separation? This seems contradictory; likely the retraction occurs before the li'an is completed). If a minor or insane wife is slandered, no li'an is performed. If the husband simply says 'This is not my pregnancy', li'an is not required because it is not an explicit accusation of zina. But if he says 'She committed zina and this pregnancy is from zina', then li'an is performed. The passage also rules on the timing of negation: if the husband negates the child immediately after birth, at the time of congratulations, or when buying delivery items, his negation is valid and he must li'an. If he delays beyond these, he must still li'an but the lineage is already established to him. For twins, if he denies one and acknowledges the other, both are attributed to him because the acknowledgement overrides the denial.

Key Terms
نفی نسب (nafi nasab): Denial of paternity, usually done through li'an.
تفریق (tafreeq): Separation ordered by the judge after li'an.
لعان (li'an): Mutual curse procedure between spouses when husband accuses wife of zina without witnesses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
After li'an, what happens to the child's lineage?
A) The child's lineage is negated from the husband and attached to the wife.
B) The child remains with the husband.
C) The child becomes parentless.
D) The child's lineage is established on both sides.

Key Takeaway
Li'an is a solemn procedure that permanently severs the marriage and severs the child's lineage from the husband, with strict conditions and timing.

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Remarriage After Retracting Li'an
Explains the li'an procedure, its effect on marriage, and child lineage (focus on the dispute)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the positions of Abu Hanifa and Imam Zufar on the permissibility of remarriage after a husband retracts from li'an, and explain the tarjih (preferred view).

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa says remarriage is permanently forbidden; Imam Zufar allows it after retraction.

Within the Hanafi school, there is a notable dispute between the founder Abu Hanifa and his student Imam Zufar regarding the aftermath of li'an. The question: if a husband performs li'an and then admits he lied, can he marry his former wife again? This lesson unpacks the two positions and the preferred view.

Guided Path
1
State the point of dispute
Can the husband remarry after retracting his li'an? The text raises this question explicitly.
2
Identify Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that the marriage is permanently forbidden, as li'an results in irrevocable separation.
3
Identify Imam Zufar's position
Imam Zufar holds that the husband can marry the same woman again because the retraction nullifies the effect of li'an.
4
Analyze the dalil
Abu Hanifa considers the separation final; Zufar argues that retraction shows the initial accusation was false, so the divorce-like effect is nullified.
The text does not elaborate on the dalil, but this is the reasoning inferred.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The majority Hanafi position follows Abu Hanifa, making the prohibition permanent. Al-Hidayah prefers this view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لعان کی کیفیت جب میاں بیوی نے لعان کر لیا تو قاضی کی تفریق سے جدائی ہوگی امام زفر کا نقطہ نظر جو شخص اپنے آپ کو جھٹلا دے اس عورت سے نکاح کر سکتا ہے یا نہیں ، اقوال فقہاء اگر تہمت بچے کی نفی کی ہو قاضی بچے کے نسب کی نفی کر دے اور بچے کو ماں کے ساتھ لاحق کر دے اور لعان کی صورت اگر تہمت زنا کی ہو اور بچے کی نفی کرے تو لعان میں دو باتوں کا تذکرہ کیا جائے پھر اس بچے کے نسب کی نفی کرے اور ماں کے ساتھ لاحق کرے اگر شوہر نے رجوع کیا اور اپنے نفس کی تکذیب کی قاضی اس کے اقرار کی وجہ سے حد جاری کرے اور اس کیلئے نکاح کرنا حلال ہے جب صغیرہ مجنونہ بیوی کو قذف کیا ان دونوں میں لعان نہیں ہے شوہر نے کہا لیس حملک منی لعان نہیں ہو گا اگر کہ زنت و هذا الحبل من الزناء دونوں لعان کریں جب مرد نے اپنی بیوی کے بچے کی نفی کر دی ولادت کے بعد یا مبارک باد قبول کرنے کے وقت یا آلہ ولادت خرید تے وقت اس کی نفی صحیح ہے اور اس کے ساتھ لعان کرے گا اور اگر ان امور کے بعد نفی کی تو لعان کرے گا اور نسب ثابت ہوگا ایک حمل سے دو بچے جنے پہلے کی نفی کی اور دوسرے کا اعتراف کیا دونوں کا نسب ثابت ہو جائے گا
The procedure of li'an: When the spouses have performed li'an, separation occurs through the judge's ruling. Imam Zufar's viewpoint: Can a person who denies himself marry that woman? According to the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school, after li'an and retraction, the husband can remarry his wife:
A) Yes, because retraction proves his accusation was false.

Rulings on 'Iddah: Durations and Changes in Status
States various 'iddah durations and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the correct 'iddah duration for a woman based on her status (free/slave, menstruating/menopausal, pregnant, widow) and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a sick divorced woman who inherits.

Core Idea
A woman's 'iddah depends on her marital status and biological condition, and may change if her status changes during the waiting period.

This passage from the Hidayah provides a comprehensive overview of the 'iddah rules. The 'iddah is an obligatory waiting period that ensures the womb is clear from a previous pregnancy. The duration varies: three menstrual cycles for a free divorced woman, three months for a menopausal woman, two cycles for a slave woman, four months and ten days for a widow, and delivery for a pregnant woman. Additionally, changes in status, such as a slave becoming free or a woman's menstruation returning, adjust the 'iddah accordingly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the woman's category
Determine if she is free or slave, whether she menstruates or is menopausal, if she is pregnant or a widow.
The base 'iddah is set by these primary categories.
2
Apply the base 'iddah duration
Select the correct duration from the given list: three quru' for free menstruating women, three months for menopausal, two menstruations for slave women, four months ten days for widows, and delivery for pregnant women.
3
Check for status changes during 'iddah
If the woman's status changes (e.g., slave freed, return of menstruation after menopause, reaching menopause during 'iddah), determine whether the 'iddah restarts or converts according to the rules mentioned.
For example, a slave freed during a raj'iy 'iddah switches to a free woman's 'iddah; but if freed during a ba'in 'iddah or widowhood, it remains the same.
4
Recognize the intra-Hanafi dispute
Note the difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding a sick divorced woman who inherits: Abu Yusuf says the longer of three months or normal 'iddah; Muhammad (and Abu Hanifa) say normal 'iddah.
This dispute has practical implications for inheritance and remarriage timing.
5
Understand the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Yusuf's view, the 'iddah may be extended to avoid mixing inheritance rights with a potential new marriage. The mufta bihi in the school is the normal 'iddah, but Abu Yusuf's view is sometimes applied in specific cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب العدة شوہر نے بیوی کو طلاق بائنہ یا طلاق رجعی دی ہو یا فرقت بغیر طلاق کے واقع ہوئی ہو اور عورت آزاد من تحیض ہے اس کی عدت تین قروء ہے ، امام شافعی کا نقطہ نظر اگر عورت ممن لا حیض ہے صغر یا کبر کی وجہ سے ان کی عدت تین مہینے ہے باندی کی عدت دو حیض اور باندی کی طلاق دو طلاقیں ہیں متوفی عنہا زوج کی عدت چار مہینے دس دن ہے حاملہ کی عدت وضع حمل ہے اگر مطلقہ مرض میں وارث ہوئی اس کی عدت ابعد الاجلین ہے، امام ابو یوسف کا مذہب اگر باندی طلاق رجعی کی عدت میں آزاد ہو گئی اس کی عدت حرائر کی طرف منتقل ہو جائے گی اگر بائنہ یا متوفی عنہا زوج عدت میں آزاد ہو گئی اسکی عدت حرائر کی طرف منتقل نہیں ہوگی آئسہ مہینوں سے عدت گزار رہی تھی پھر حیض والی ہوگئی پہلی گذری ہوئی عدت ختم ہو جائے گی پھر نئے سرے سے حیض کے ساتھ عدت گزارے گی اگر حیض کے ساتھ عدت گزار رہی تھی پھر آئسہ ہو گئی تو مہینوں سے عدت گزارے گی منکوحہ نکاح فاسد اور موطوہ بشبہ دونوں کی فرقت اور موت میں عدت حیض کے اعتبار سے ہوگی مولی ام الولد سے فوت ہو گیا یا اسے آزاد کر دیا اس کی عدت تین حیض ہیں صغیر اپنی بیوی چھوڑ کر فوت ہو گیا اور وہ حاملہ تھی اس کی عدت وضع حمل ہے ، امام ابو یوسف کا مذہب
Chapter of 'Iddah. If the husband gave his wife a divorce (bain or raj'iy) or separation without divorce, and the woman is free and menstruates, her 'iddah is three quru' (menstrual cycles). This is the viewpoint of Imam al-Shafi'i. If the woman is one who does not menstruate due to minority or old age, her 'iddah is three months. The 'iddah of a slave woman is two menstruations, and her divorce counts as two divorces. The 'iddah of a widow is four months and ten days. The 'iddah of a pregnant woman is delivery. If the divorced woman is sick and inheriting, her 'iddah is the longer of the two periods (ab'adal-ajalayn). This is the madhhab of Imam Abu Yusuf. If a slave woman becomes free during the 'iddah of a raj'iy divorce, her 'iddah changes to that of a free woman. If she becomes free during the 'iddah of a ba'in divorce or widowhood, her 'iddah does not change. A woman who was menstruating and then reaches menopause during 'iddah switches to three months. Conversely, if she was post-menopausal and then starts menstruating, her previous months count is cancelled and she restarts with menstruations. The 'iddah for a woman in a fasid (invalid) marriage or doubtful intercourse (shubha) is by menstruations; for death it is also by menstruations. If the master of an umm walad dies or frees her, her 'iddah is three menstruations. If a minor husband dies leaving his pregnant wife, her 'iddah is delivery. This is the madhhab of Imam Abu Yusuf.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This chapter comprehensively states the rules of 'iddah (waiting period) after divorce or death. Key points: For a free woman who menstruates, the 'iddah for divorce is three menstrual cycles (quru'). This is mentioned as Imam al-Shafi'i's viewpoint; but it is also the Hanafi position. For women who do not menstruate (young girls or menopausal), it is three months. For slave women, the 'iddah is two cycles, and their divorce is only two talāqs. For widows, the 'iddah is four months and ten days. For pregnant women, it lasts until delivery. There is a dispute: If a divorced woman falls ill and inherits from her husband (e.g., during his terminal illness), her 'iddah is the longer of either three months or the normal 'iddah of the divorced woman. This is Imam Abu Yusuf's view. Imam Muhammad says it remains the normal 'iddah. The text also addresses changes of status: If a slave woman is freed during a revocable divorce (raj'iy) 'iddah, her 'iddah changes to three months (like a free woman). But if freed during an irrevocable (ba'in) divorce or widowhood, it remains the same. For menopausal women, if menstruation returns, the months already passed are cancelled and she starts again with menstrual cycles. Conversely, if she starts menopause during her 'iddah, she switches to months. For invalid marriages (nikah fasid) and doubtful intercourse (shubha), the 'iddah is by menstruations. For a master of an umm walad (slave mother of his child), if he dies or frees her, her 'iddah is three menstruations. If a minor husband dies and leaves a pregnant wife, her 'iddah is delivery, not the full widow's period.

Key Terms
عدت (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death before remarrying.
قروء (quru'): Menstrual cycles in this context; Hanafi school interprets it as menstruations.
ابعد الاجلین (ab'adal-ajalayn): The longer of the two periods (i.e., the longer of three months or the normal 'iddah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as stated in the passage, what is the 'iddah of a slave woman who is divorced revocably?
A) Three menstrual cycles
B) Two menstrual cycles
C) Three months
D) Four months and ten days

Key Takeaway
The 'iddah is a fixed but variable waiting period that adjusts according to the woman's status and any changes during its course, ensuring clarity of lineage and proper observance of marital dissolution.

Talaq — Divorce

Waiting Periods ('Iddah) for Women: Types and Disputes
Comprehensive chapter on 'iddah with ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the 'iddah durations for different categories of women and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i on the counting of quru'.

Core Idea
A woman's 'iddah varies by her status—free, slave, pregnant, widowed—and the Hanafi school differs from Shafi'i on how quru' is counted.

This chapter from Al-Hidayah compiles the many rulings on 'iddah, the waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death before remarriage. The passage covers a wide range of scenarios: free women, slave women, pregnant women, widows, and cases where status changes during the 'iddah. It also records important intra-Hanafi disagreements (e.g., Abu Yusuf on the longer period for death-illness divorce) and inter-madhhab disputes (e.g., the interpretation of quru' with Imam Shafi'i). Mastering these rulings is essential for a Hanafi faqih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base 'iddah for free menstruating women
The text states that a free woman who menstruates observes 'iddah for three quru'. Note the mention of Imam Shafi'i, indicating a dispute over the meaning of quru'.
The Hanafi school defines quru' as tuhr (non-bleeding periods), while Shafi'i defines it as haid (menstruation).
2
Categorize the exceptions: non-menstruating, slave, pregnant, widow
The passage gives specific durations: three months for non-menstruating, two menstruations for slave women, delivery for pregnant, and four months ten days for widows.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute on ab'ad al-ajalayn
If a woman is divorced during her husband's death illness and inherits, her 'iddah is the longer of the two periods. This is attributed to Imam Abu Yusuf.
Ab'ad al-ajalayn: the longer of the divorce 'iddah (three quru' or three months) and the death 'iddah (four months ten days).
4
Trace the effect of change in status during 'iddah
The text describes several scenarios: if a slave woman becomes free during revocable 'iddah, her 'iddah converts to that of free women; if she is irrevocably divorced or widowed, it does not. Similarly, if a woman switches between menstruating and non-menstruating states, the 'iddah resets.
5
Identify the mourning (hidad) rules and residence restrictions
Hidad is wajib for Muslim widows and irrevocably divorced women. The passage also details where the woman must stay during 'iddah and rules about leaving the house.

Chapter on the Waiting Period. If the husband gave his wife a revocable or irrevocable divorce, or separation occurred without divorce, and the woman is a free woman who menstruates, her 'iddah is three menstrual periods – according to Imam Shafi'i's view. If the woman is one who does not menstruate due to youth or old age, her 'iddah is three months. The 'iddah of a slave woman is two menstruations, and her divorce is two divorces. The 'iddah of a woman whose husband dies is four months and ten days. The 'iddah of a pregnant woman is delivery (of the child). If a divorced woman inherits due to death illness, her 'iddah is the longer of the two periods – according to Imam Abu Yusuf's school. If a slave woman becomes free during the 'iddah of a revocable divorce, her 'iddah transfers to that of free women; if she is irrevocably divorced or widowed and becomes free during 'iddah, her 'iddah does not transfer to that of free women. A woman who was observing 'iddah by months and then begins to menstruate: the previous part of the 'iddah is void, and she starts anew with menstruation. If she was observing by menstruation and then becomes amenorrheic (ayisah), she switches to months. For a woman married under a void contract (nikah fasid) and a concubine (mutawat) with shubha, their 'iddah in separation and death is based on menstruation. If the master of an umm walad dies or frees her, her 'iddah is three menstruations. If a minor dies leaving his wife pregnant, her 'iddah is delivery – according to Imam Abu Yusuf's school. If the husband divorces his wife during menstruation, that menstruation is not counted in the 'iddah. If a woman in 'iddah has intercourse under shubha, she must observe a second 'iddah, and the two 'iddahs overlap; she counts whatever menstruation she sees, and must complete the second 'iddah – according to Imam Shafi'i's view. A woman in 'iddah of death who has intercourse will observe 'iddah by months. The 'iddah of divorce starts after divorce, and 'iddah of death starts after death. The 'iddah for a void marriage starts from the separation or from the time the man resolves to abandon intercourse – according to Imam Zufar's view. If the woman in 'iddah says 'my 'iddah has passed' and the husband denies, the husband's word with oath is accepted. If a husband gives an irrevocable divorce, then remarries her and divorces before consummation, he must pay full dower and a full 'iddah is required – according to the sayings of jurists. If a dhimmi divorces a dhimmi woman, no 'iddah is required; similarly, if a harbi woman leaves Dar al-Islam. An irrevocably divorced woman (mabtutah) and a widow, when she is an adult Muslim, must observe mourning (hidad). The meaning of hidad. Mourning is not required for a disbeliever. If the master of an umm walad dies or she is freed, mourning is not required. It is inappropriate to propose marriage to a woman in 'iddah, but describing her is not forbidden. For a woman in revocable divorce and irrevocable divorce, it is not permissible to leave the house day or night. A widow may go out and may leave for part of the night. The woman must spend her 'iddah in the house where she was residing at the time of separation. If the husband's house is insufficient for her and the heirs expel her from their share, she may move. If separation occurred by irrevocable or triple divorce, they must observe hijab (seclusion). If they appoint a trustworthy woman as a barrier, it is good. If the house is crowded, the woman should leave, but it is better for the man to leave. If the distance is three days' journey, the woman may return or go to her destination. If the husband gave three divorces or died while she is in the city, she does not leave until she completes her 'iddah; then she may leave if she has a mahram.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This is the chapter on 'iddah from the commentary on Al-Hidayah. It compiles numerous rulings on waiting periods. Key points: The default 'iddah for a free menstruating woman is three quru' (menstrual periods) – this is attributed to Imam Shafi'i, implying the Hanafi view also uses quru but may interpret differently. For non-menstruating (young or old), three months. Slave woman: two menstruations and her divorce counts as two. Widow: four months ten days. Pregnant: until delivery. If divorced in death illness, the longer of divorce 'iddah or death 'iddah (Abu Yusuf). When a slave becomes free during 'iddah of revocable talaq, it converts to free woman's 'iddah; for irrevocable or death, it does not. Switching between months and menstruation: if a woman starts menstruating during a monthly 'iddah, she restarts with menstruation; if she stops menstruating during a menstrual 'iddah, she switches to months. For invalid marriage (nikah fasid) and intercourse under shubha, 'iddah by menstruation. Umm walad's 'iddah on master's death or freeing: three menstruations. If a minor dies leaving his wife pregnant, her 'iddah is delivery (Abu Yusuf). Divorce during menstruation: that period not counted. Intercourse under shubha during 'iddah requires a second 'iddah; they overlap (Shafi'i view). For death 'iddah if intercourse under shubha, 'iddah by months. The start of 'iddah: for divorce after divorce, for death after death. For void marriage, 'iddah starts from separation or from when the man decides to stop intercourse (Zufar). Dispute about 'iddah completion: if woman claims it's over and husband denies, husband's oath is accepted. If a man divorces bain, then remarries and divorces before consummation, full mahr and full 'iddah required (ijma'?). Dhimmis: no 'iddah. Harbi woman leaving Dar al-Islam: no 'iddah. Mourning (hidad) is wajib for Muslim widow over puberty. Not wajib for disbelievers or umm walad. Proposing during 'iddah is not allowed but general description is okay. Residence during 'iddah: woman must stay in the house where separation occurred; can move if insufficient or expelled. Hijab required between spouses after talaq bain or triple talaq; they can appoint a barrier. If house is too crowded, woman should move out; man leaving is better. Travel: if three days distance, she may go or stay. If husband divorced her three times or died in the city, she stays until 'iddah ends; then can travel with mahram.

Key Terms
عدة ('iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death before remarriage.
قروء (quru'): The plural of qur' (menstrual period). Here used as three quru' for 'iddah.
حداد (hidad): Mourning observed by a widow: abstaining from adornment and staying at home.
ابعد الاجلين (ab'ad al-ajalayn): The longer of the two waiting periods (divorce 'iddah and death 'iddah). Applied when a woman is divorced during her husband's death illness and inherits from him.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the 'iddah of a free woman who does not menstruate due to old age?
A) Three quru'
B) Three months
C) Four months and ten days
D) Until delivery

Key Takeaway
The correct 'iddah depends on multiple factors: free/slave, menstruating/non, pregnant, divorced/widowed, and changes during 'iddah may reset the count.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
10 min
Rulings on 'Iddah and Mourning (Hidad)
Collection of rulings on iddah, mourning, and a madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on iddah for divorced and widowed women, including the interlacement of iddahs after shubha intercourse, and distinguish the Shafi'i position on the same.

Core Idea
If a woman in iddah has intercourse by mistake, she begins a new iddah that interlaces with the first.

This lesson brings together several key rulings on iddah and mourning (hidad) from the Hanafi school. The central point of difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools is whether iddahs can interlace when shubha intercourse occurs. Understanding this dispute and the practical consequences helps clarify the fiqh of waiting periods and how they apply to divorced and widowed women.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on iddah after shubha intercourse
According to the passage, if a woman in iddah (from divorce or death) has intercourse by shubha (mistake), she begins a new iddah that interlaces with the original. She counts the same menstrual cycles for both iddahs, and completion of the second iddah is necessary.
The passage explicitly says 'the two iddahs will interlace, and she will count whichever menstruation she sees for both'.
2
Identify the Shafi'i counter-position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the iddah of a widow after intercourse is observed by months (not menstrual cycles), and the iddah of divorce and death are separate and sequential; they do not interlace.
The passage mentions Imam Shafi'i's view: 'the iddah of divorce begins after divorce and the iddah of death begins after death'.
3
Analyse the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
In the Hanafi view, the woman's total waiting period may be shorter due to overlapping; in the Shafi'i view, the periods are sequential, so the waiting period is longer. This affects when the woman may remarry.
The passage does not explicitly state the consequence, but it follows logically from the positions.
4
Note other rulings on iddah conditions
The passage also covers: divorce during menstruation does not count that menses; iddah of a fasid marriage begins at separation or resolution to abstain; if a ba'in divorcee remarries and is divorced before consummation, full mahr and a separate iddah are required; and if a woman claims iddah is over and husband denies, his word with oath is accepted (Imam Zufar).
These are secondary but important rulings.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi ruling on hidad and restrictions during iddah
Mourning (hidad) is wajib on free adult Muslim women who are irrevocably divorced (mubtawana) or widowed. It involves avoiding adornment and staying in the home with specific permissions for widows to go out during the day. Mourning is not required on non-Muslims or umm walad.
The passage defines the limits of movement and the requirement of a screen between separated spouses.

The husband divorced his wife during menstruation; this menstruation will not be counted in the iddah. The iddah in which the divorce occurred; if intercourse by shubha (doubt) occurred with the woman in iddah, she has another iddah, and the two iddahs will interlace, and she will count whichever menstruation she sees for both, and completion of the second iddah is necessary. Imam Shafi'i's view: when intercourse occurs with a widow, she will observe iddah by months; the iddah of divorce begins after divorce and the iddah of death begins after death. The iddah of a fasid nikah begins after separation or when the one who had intercourse resolves to abstain. Imam Zufar's view: if the woman in iddah says 'my iddah has passed' and the husband denies, the man's word with an oath is accepted. The husband gave a ba'in talaq to the woman, then married her again and divorced before consummation; the full mahr and a separate iddah are obligatory upon the man. Sayings of the jurists: if a dhimmi divorces his dhimmi wife, iddah is not necessary; similarly, if a harbi woman leaves Dar al-Islam. A mubtawana (irrevocably divorced) woman and a widow, when she is an adult Muslim, mourning (hidad) is obligatory upon her. The definition of hidad. Mourning is not obligatory upon a kafira. If the master of an umm walad dies or she is freed, mourning is not obligatory. Proposing to a woman in iddah is inappropriate; praising her is not objectionable. A raj'iyya divorcee and a mubtawana (mubtawana? probably mubtawana for ba'in) are not permitted to leave the house day or night; and a widow may go out during the day and part of the night. It is obligatory upon the woman in iddah to spend the iddah in the house where she was residing at the time of separation. If the husband's house is insufficient for the woman and the heirs evict her from their share, then the woman may move. If the separation occurred by ba'in talaq or three divorces, then it is necessary to have a screen between them. If they place a trustworthy woman between them who has the ability to prevent interaction, that is good. If the house is cramped for both, the woman should leave, but it is better for the man to leave. If the distance is three days' journey, the woman may return if she wishes, or continue to her destination if she wishes. If the husband gave three divorces or died and left her in the city, the woman will not leave until she completes the iddah; then if she has a mahram, she may leave.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings on various aspects of iddah and mourning. It begins with the ruling that if a husband divorces his wife during her menses, that menses does not count towards her iddah. Then it discusses the situation where a woman in iddah has intercourse with a man by mistake (shubha): she must start a new iddah, and the two iddahs interlace—meaning she counts the same menses for both. Imam al-Shafi'i's view is mentioned for comparison: according to him, if a widow has intercourse, she observes her iddah by months, and the iddah of divorce and death are separate and sequential. The passage then addresses the iddah of a fasid (invalid) marriage, stating it begins from the time of separation or when the man resolves to stop intercourse. Imam Zufar's opinion is given: if a woman claims her iddah is over and the husband denies, the husband's word with an oath is accepted. Another ruling: if a husband gives a ba'in talaq (irrevocable divorce), then remarries the same woman and divorces her before consummation, he owes her the full mahr and a separate iddah. The text then moves to mourning (hidad): it is wajib upon a free adult Muslim woman who is irrevocably divorced (mubtawana) or widowed. Mourning is not obligatory upon a non-Muslim woman. An umm walad (slave mother) does not observe mourning if her master dies or if she is freed. Proposing to a woman in iddah is inappropriate, but praising her is allowed. The passage details restrictions on leaving the house during iddah: a raj'iyya divorcee and a mubtawana cannot leave at all; a widow may leave during the day and some part of the night. The woman must stay in the house where she lived at the time of separation unless the house is insufficient and the heirs evict her, in which case she may move. If the separation is by ba'in or three talaqs, a screen (purdah) is required between the spouses. If the house is cramped, the woman should leave but it is better for the man to leave. For a long distance, she may decide. Finally, if the husband gave three talaqs or died in the city, she must remain in the city until her iddah ends, and then may travel only with a mahram.

Key Terms
عدت (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of her husband before she can remarry.
حداد (hidad): The mourning period observed by a woman for her deceased husband, during which she avoids adornment and certain activities.
وطی بشبہ (wati' bi shubha): Sexual intercourse that occurs under the mistaken belief that it is lawful, e.g., thinking a woman in iddah is not in iddah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Any woman whose husband dies
B) An adult Muslim woman who is irrevocably divorced or widowed
C) A free woman regardless of religion
D) A slave woman whose master dies

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, iddahs can interlace after shubha intercourse, and mourning (hidad) is wajib upon adult Muslim widows and irrevocably divorced women.

The Two-Year Maximum for Establishing Lineage after Divorce or Death
Rulings on lineage establishment after divorce and death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the maximum period for establishing a child's lineage after divorce or death, and explain when the mother's admission of iddah expiry prevents attribution.

Core Idea
A child born within two years of divorce or death is attributed to the father unless the mother admits iddah has ended.

This passage from the chapter on lineage (nasab) presents the core Hanafi ruling: a divorced or widowed woman's child is linked to her former husband if born within two years, provided she does not claim her waiting period has ended. We will unpack the three scenarios and the logic behind the two-year maximum.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of women
The passage discusses a raj'iyya divorcee, a mubtawana (irrevocable divorcee), and a widow. Identify each scenario and the common two-year period.
2
State the condition of iddah admission
For the raj'iyya, lineage is established within two years unless the woman admits her iddah has expired. Understand that this admission blocks attribution.
3
Apply the two-year rule to widows
For a widow, the lineage is established within two years from the husband's death, regardless of her admission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ثبوت النسب مرد نے کہا ان تزوجت فلان بھی طالق پھراس کے ساتھ نکاح کیا پھر اس نے نکاح کے دن سے لے کر چھ ماہ میں بچہ جنابیہ اس کا بیٹا ہے اور مرد پر مہر لازم ہے مطلقہ رجعیہ کے بچے کا نسب ثابت ہو جائے گا جب اس نے بچہ دو سال یا دو سال سے زیادہ میں جنا جب تک عورت نے انقضاء عدت کا اقرار نہ کیا ہو مہتو نہ کے بچے کا نسب ثابت ہو جاتا ہے جبکہ وہ دو سال سے کم میں بنے مبتو یہ صغیرہ ہو کہ اس جیسی عورت کے ساتھ جماع کیا جا سکتا ہے اس نے نو ماہ میں بچہ جنا اس بچے کا نسب ثابت نہیں ہوگا حتی کہ وہ نو ماہ سے کم میں بچہ جنے ، اقوال فقہاء متوفی عنہا ز و جہا کے بچے کا نسب وفات سے دو برس کے اندر ثابت ہوتا ہے، امام زفر کا نقطہ نظر جب معدہ انقضاء عدت کا اقرار کرے پھر چھ ماہے کم میں بچہ جنے اس بچے کا نسب ثابت ہوتا ہے معدہ کے بچے کا نسب کب ثابت ہوگا ، اقوال فقہاء معتدہ وفات کے بچے کی پیدائش کی تصدیق ورثہ نے کی اور کسی نے ولادت پر گواہی نہیں دی بچہ کا نسب ثابت ہوگا جب مرد نے عورت سے نکاح کیا اس نے نکاح کے دن سے لے کر چھ ماہ سے کم میں بچہ جنا اس کا نسب ثابت نہیں ہو گا اگر بچہ جنا پھر اختلاف ہو گیا شوہر کہتا ہے میں نے چار مہینے سے نکاح کیا ہے اور عورت چھ ماہ گذرنے کا دعوی کرتی ہے کس کا قول معتبر ہوگا بچے کا نسب ثابت ہو گا یا نہیں؟ مرد نے اپنی بیوی سے از اولدت ولد أفانت طالق ایک عورت نے بچے کی پیدائش پر گواہی دی مطلقہ ہوگی یا نہیں ، اقوال فقہاء اگر شوہر نے عورت کے حاملہ ہونے کا اقرار کیا تو کب مطلقہ ہوگی ، اقوال فقہاء حمل کی اکثر مدت دو سال ہے جس نے باندی سے نکاح کیا پھر طلاق دے دی پھر اسے خرید لیا اگر وہ خریدنے کے دن سے لے کر بچہ چھ ماہ سے کم میں لائی نسب ثابت ہوگا یا نہیں باندی سے کہا ان کان فی بطنك ولد فومنی ایک عورت نے بچہ کی ولادت پر گواہی دی تو یہ باندی ام ولد ہوگی غلام کو کہا ہو بنی پھر فوت ہو گیا غلام کی ماں آئی اس نے کہا انا امراتہ یہ عورت اس کی بیوی ہوگی اور غلام بچہ دونوں وارث ہوں گے اگر عورت کے آزاد ہونے کے بارے میں علم نہیں ورثہ نے کہا انت ام ولد اس کیلئے میراث نہیں ہوگی
Chapter on Establishing Lineage. A man said: 'If I marry so-and-so, she is divorced.' Then he married her, and she gave birth within six months from the day of marriage. The child is his son, and the mahr is obligatory upon the man. The lineage of a child of a raj'iyya divorcee is established when she gives birth within two years or more, as long as the woman has not admitted the expiry of the iddah. The lineage of a mubtawana's child is established when she gives birth within less than two years, provided the mubtawana is of a marriageable age (i.e., intercourse could occur with such a woman). If she gives birth at nine months, the lineage is not established until she gives birth in less than nine months. Sayings of the jurists: The lineage of a widow's child is established within two years from the death. Imam Zufar's view: When a woman in iddah admits the expiry of iddah, then gives birth in less than six months, the child's lineage is established. When is the lineage of the child of a woman in iddah established? Sayings of the jurists. If the heirs confirm the birth of the widow's child and no one testifies to the birth, the child's lineage is established. When a man marries a woman and she gives birth less than six months from the day of marriage, his lineage is not established. If a child is born and then a dispute arises: the husband says 'I married her four months ago' and the woman claims six months have passed, whose word is accepted? Will the child's lineage be established? A man said to his wife: 'If you give birth to a child, you are divorced.' A woman testified to the birth of the child. Will she be divorced or not? Sayings of the jurists. If the husband admits the woman is pregnant, when will she become divorced? Sayings of the jurists. The maximum period of pregnancy is two years. A person married a slave girl, then divorced her, then bought her. If she brings a child less than six months from the day of purchase, will lineage be established? If he said to the slave girl: 'If there is a child in your womb, you are free,' and one woman testified to the birth of the child, then this slave girl becomes an umm walad. A slave was told 'you are free,' then he died. The slave's mother came and said 'I am his wife.' This woman will be his wife, and the slave and the child both will inherit. If the status of the woman being free is unknown, and the heirs said 'you are an umm walad,' she will not inherit.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage is part of the chapter on establishing lineage (nasab) in Islamic law. It begins with a conditional divorce case: a man says 'If I marry so-and-so, she is divorced,' then marries her, and she gives birth within six months. The child is his son (lineage established) and the full mahr is due. The next ruling concerns a woman divorced revocably (raj'iyya): if she gives birth within two years from the divorce, the child's lineage is established, unless she admits that her iddah has expired. For a woman divorced irrevocably (mubtawana), the child's lineage is established if born within two years, provided she is of an age where intercourse can occur; but if she gives birth at exactly nine months, lineage is not established until she gives birth earlier than nine months (i.e., the period must be less than nine months from the divorce for a mubtawana? The text is ambiguous but seems to indicate a shorter period for mubtawana). For a widow, the child's lineage is established within two years from the death. Imam Zufar's view is mentioned: if a woman in iddah admits her iddah is over, then gives birth in less than six months, the child's lineage is established. The passage then addresses various scenarios: if a man marries a woman and she gives birth in less than six months, lineage is not established. If there is a dispute about the duration since marriage, the husband's word (with oath) is accepted. A conditional talaq upon birth: if a woman testifies to the birth, the divorce may or may not occur depending on the jurists' views. If the husband admits pregnancy, the timing of the divorce (if conditional) is determined. The passage states the maximum pregnancy period is two years (Hanafi view). Then it discusses a slave girl: if a man marries, divorces, then buys her, and she gives birth within six months of purchase, lineage is established? The text leaves it open. A conditional manumission: if a man tells his slave girl 'if you are pregnant, you are free,' and one woman testifies to the birth, she becomes umm walad. Finally, a case of inheritance: a slave's mother claims to be his wife, the child inherits; if a woman's free status is unknown and heirs call her umm walad, she does not inherit. Throughout, the passage presents multiple cases and some differences (e.g., Imam Zufar) but mostly states the established Hanafi rulings.

Key Terms
نسب (nasab): Lineage (paternity) of a child, i.e., legal attribution to the father.
عدت (iddah): The waiting period after which a woman may remarry; used here to determine the maximum period for establishing lineage.
حمل (haml): Pregnancy; the passage notes the maximum period as two years.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Six months
B) Nine months
C) One year

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school establishes lineage within a two-year window after divorce or death, with the exception that the divorced woman's admission of iddah expiry blocks attribution.

Imam Zufar's Dissent: The Six-Month Rule for Lineage after Iddah Expiry
Intra-Hanafi dispute on lineage after iddah admission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare the Hanafi majority view with Imam Zufar's view on lineage establishment when the divorced woman admits iddah expiry, and identify the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Imam Zufar holds that if a woman admits iddah expiry and then gives birth within six months, lineage is established; the majority requires no such admission to within two years.

Within the Hanafi school, there is a notable difference of opinion. Imam Zufar (a disciple of Imam Abu Hanifa) argues that if a woman in iddah accepts that her waiting period has ended, and then gives birth within six months, the child is attributed to the former husband. The majority holds that her admission completely blocks attribution. Let's examine this dispute and its practical effects.

Guided Path
1
State the majority Hanafi position
The majority holds that for a raj'iyya divorcee, lineage is established within two years unless the woman admits iddah expiry. If she admits, lineage is not established even within the two years.
This is the default position in the passage.
2
State Imam Zufar's position
Imam Zufar holds that if the woman admits iddah expiry and then gives birth within six months of that admission, lineage is established.
He thus creates a new window after admission.
3
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Zufar's view, a child born within six months after admission is attributed; under the majority, it is not.
This affects inheritance, maintenance, and paternity.

باب ثبوت النسب مرد نے کہا ان تزوجت فلان بھی طالق پھراس کے ساتھ نکاح کیا پھر اس نے نکاح کے دن سے لے کر چھ ماہ میں بچہ جنابیہ اس کا بیٹا ہے اور مرد پر مہر لازم ہے مطلقہ رجعیہ کے بچے کا نسب ثابت ہو جائے گا جب اس نے بچہ دو سال یا دو سال سے زیادہ میں جنا جب تک عورت نے انقضاء عدت کا اقرار نہ کیا ہو مہتو نہ کے بچے کا نسب ثابت ہو جاتا ہے جبکہ وہ دو سال سے کم میں بنے مبتو یہ صغیرہ ہو کہ اس جیسی عورت کے ساتھ جماع کیا جا سکتا ہے اس نے نو ماہ میں بچہ جنا اس بچے کا نسب ثابت نہیں ہوگا حتی کہ وہ نو ماہ سے کم میں بچہ جنے ، اقوال فقہاء متوفی عنہا ز و جہا کے بچے کا نسب وفات سے دو برس کے اندر ثابت ہوتا ہے، امام زفر کا نقطہ نظر جب معدہ انقضاء عدت کا اقرار کرے پھر چھ ماہے کم میں بچہ جنے اس بچے کا نسب ثابت ہوتا ہے معدہ کے بچے کا نسب کب ثابت ہوگا ، اقوال فقہاء معتدہ وفات کے بچے کی پیدائش کی تصدیق ورثہ نے کی اور کسی نے ولادت پر گواہی نہیں دی بچہ کا نسب ثابت ہوگا جب مرد نے عورت سے نکاح کیا اس نے نکاح کے دن سے لے کر چھ ماہ سے کم میں بچہ جنا اس کا نسب ثابت نہیں ہو گا اگر بچہ جنا پھر اختلاف ہو گیا شوہر کہتا ہے میں نے چار مہینے سے نکاح کیا ہے اور عورت چھ ماہ گذرنے کا دعوی کرتی ہے کس کا قول معتبر ہوگا بچے کا نسب ثابت ہو گا یا نہیں؟ مرد نے اپنی بیوی سے از اولدت ولد أفانت طالق ایک عورت نے بچے کی پیدائش پر گواہی دی مطلقہ ہوگی یا نہیں ، اقوال فقہاء اگر شوہر نے عورت کے حاملہ ہونے کا اقرار کیا تو کب مطلقہ ہوگی ، اقوال فقہاء حمل کی اکثر مدت دو سال ہے جس نے باندی سے نکاح کیا پھر طلاق دے دی پھر اسے خرید لیا اگر وہ خریدنے کے دن سے لے کر بچہ چھ ماہ سے کم میں لائی نسب ثابت ہوگا یا نہیں باندی سے کہا ان کان فی بطنك ولد فومنی ایک عورت نے بچہ کی ولادت پر گواہی دی تو یہ باندی ام ولد ہوگی غلام کو کہا ہو بنی پھر فوت ہو گیا غلام کی ماں آئی اس نے کہا انا امراتہ یہ عورت اس کی بیوی ہوگی اور غلام بچہ دونوں وارث ہوں گے اگر عورت کے آزاد ہونے کے بارے میں علم نہیں ورثہ نے کہا انت ام ولد اس کیلئے میراث نہیں ہوگی
Chapter on Establishing Lineage. A man said: 'If I marry so-and-so, she is divorced.' Then he married her, and she gave birth within six months from the day of marriage. The child is his son, and the mahr is obligatory upon the man. The lineage of a child of a raj'iyya divorcee is established when she gives birth within two years or more, as long as the woman has not admitted the expiry of the iddah. The lineage of a mubtawana's child is established when she gives birth within less than two years, provided the mubtawana is of a marriageable age (i.e., intercourse could occur with such a woman). If she gives birth at nine months, the lineage is not established until she gives birth in less than nine months. Sayings of the jurists: The lineage of a widow's child is established within two years from the death. Imam Zufar's view: When a woman in iddah admits the expiry of iddah, then gives birth in less than six months, the child's lineage is established. When is the lineage of the child of a woman in iddah established? Sayings of the jurists. If the heirs confirm the birth of the widow's child and no one testifies to the birth, the child's lineage is established. When a man marries a woman and she gives birth less than six months from the day of marriage, his lineage is not established. If a child is born and then a dispute arises: the husband says 'I married her four months ago' and the woman claims six months have passed, whose word is accepted? Will the child's lineage be established? A man said to his wife: 'If you give birth to a child, you are divorced.' A woman testified to the birth of the child. Will she be divorced or not? Sayings of the jurists. If the husband admits the woman is pregnant, when will she become divorced? Sayings of the jurists. The maximum period of pregnancy is two years. A person married a slave girl, then divorced her, then bought her. If she brings a child less than six months from the day of purchase, will lineage be established? If he said to the slave girl: 'If there is a child in your womb, you are free,' and one woman testified to the birth of the child, then this slave girl becomes an umm walad. A slave was told 'you are free,' then he died. The slave's mother came and said 'I am his wife.' This woman will be his wife, and the slave and the child both will inherit. If the status of the woman being free is unknown, and the heirs said 'you are an umm walad,' she will not inherit.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage is part of the chapter on establishing lineage (nasab) in Islamic law. It begins with a conditional divorce case: a man says 'If I marry so-and-so, she is divorced,' then marries her, and she gives birth within six months. The child is his son (lineage established) and the full mahr is due. The next ruling concerns a woman divorced revocably (raj'iyya): if she gives birth within two years from the divorce, the child's lineage is established, unless she admits that her iddah has expired. For a woman divorced irrevocably (mubtawana), the child's lineage is established if born within two years, provided she is of an age where intercourse can occur; but if she gives birth at exactly nine months, lineage is not established until she gives birth earlier than nine months (i.e., the period must be less than nine months from the divorce for a mubtawana? The text is ambiguous but seems to indicate a shorter period for mubtawana). For a widow, the child's lineage is established within two years from the death. Imam Zufar's view is mentioned: if a woman in iddah admits her iddah is over, then gives birth in less than six months, the child's lineage is established. The passage then addresses various scenarios: if a man marries a woman and she gives birth in less than six months, lineage is not established. If there is a dispute about the duration since marriage, the husband's word (with oath) is accepted. A conditional talaq upon birth: if a woman testifies to the birth, the divorce may or may not occur depending on the jurists' views. If the husband admits pregnancy, the timing of the divorce (if conditional) is determined. The passage states the maximum pregnancy period is two years (Hanafi view). Then it discusses a slave girl: if a man marries, divorces, then buys her, and she gives birth within six months of purchase, lineage is established? The text leaves it open. A conditional manumission: if a man tells his slave girl 'if you are pregnant, you are free,' and one woman testifies to the birth, she becomes umm walad. Finally, a case of inheritance: a slave's mother claims to be his wife, the child inherits; if a woman's free status is unknown and heirs call her umm walad, she does not inherit. Throughout, the passage presents multiple cases and some differences (e.g., Imam Zufar) but mostly states the established Hanafi rulings.

Key Terms
نسب (nasab): Lineage (paternity) of a child, i.e., legal attribution to the father.
عدت (iddah): The waiting period after which a woman may remarry; used here to determine the maximum period for establishing lineage.
حمل (haml): Pregnancy; the passage notes the maximum period as two years.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does Imam Zufar say about the lineage of a child when the woman admits iddah expiry?
A) Child's lineage is never established
B) Child's lineage is established if born within six months
C) Child's lineage is established if born within two years
D) Child's lineage is established if born within nine months

Key Takeaway
Imam Zufar's dissenting view creates a six-month window for lineage after the woman admits iddah expiry, while the majority Hanafi position blocks attribution upon such admission.

The Two Foundational Rulings of Custody (Hadana)
Introduction to the chapter on custody rights and responsibilities

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two core rulings of hadana: (1) the father is obligated for custody expenses, (2) the mother cannot be compelled, and identify the two questions the chapter will address.

Core Idea
The father must provide for custody; the mother may not be forced.

This passage opens the chapter on custody (hadana). It lays down two essential rulings that form the foundation of the Hanafi law of custody. Understanding these rulings is crucial before delving into the detailed order of custodial rights and their forfeiture. The text also poses two questions that guide the rest of the chapter.

Guided Path
1
Read the chapter title
The title indicates the topic: custody and who is more entitled to it.
This sets the context for the entire discussion.
2
Identify the first ruling
The expenses of custody are obligatory upon the father. Find the phrase 'نفقہ باپ پر لازم ہے'.
This establishes the financial responsibility.
3
Identify the second ruling
The mother cannot be forced to take custody. Find 'ماں پر جبر نہیں کیا جائے گا'.
This emphasizes that custody is a right, not an obligation for the mother.
4
Recognize the two questions
The text asks: (1) Which women are entitled to custody in order? (2) When is their right forfeited? These guide the chapter.
These questions structure the rest of the chapter's content.

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on custody (hadana) of children. It states two key principles: first, the father is responsible for the financial expenses of the child's upbringing (nafaqa); second, the mother cannot be compelled to take custody if she is unwilling. The passage then poses two questions that the chapter will address: 1) The order of entitlement among women to custody (e.g., mother, grandmother, etc.), and 2) The circumstances under which they lose that right. This is a typical matn style that lists essential rulings and prompts further explanation.

Key Terms
حضانت (hadana): Custody and upbringing of a young child, including physical care and training.
نفقہ (nafaqa): Financial support, including food, clothing, and shelter; here it specifically refers to custody expenses.

Key Takeaway

Establishing Lineage after Revocable Divorce
Ruling on paternity of child born within two years of revocable divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which a child is attributed to the husband after a revocable divorce and apply the rule to a given scenario.

Core Idea
A child born within two years of revocable divorce is attributed to the husband unless the woman admits her iddah ended.

In Hanafi fiqh, after a revocable divorce (talaq rajʿi), the marriage bond is not completely severed during the iddah. This has implications for lineage attribution of a child born during this period. The ruling protects paternity and prevents disputes by establishing a clear time frame and exception based on the woman's admission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of divorce
Confirm that the divorce is revocable (rajʿī) – meaning the husband can take back his wife during the iddah without a new marriage contract.
Revocable divorce applies to the first or second pronouncement.
2
Determine the time frame of birth
Check if the child is born within two years from the date of divorce. According to the dominant Hanafi view, the maximum pregnancy duration is two years.
Imam Muhammad holds two years; Imam Abu Yusuf holds one year, but the two-year rule is mufta bihi.
3
Check the woman's admission
If the woman explicitly states that her iddah has ended (e.g., by completing three menstrual cycles), then the child is not attributed to the husband, regardless of the birth timing.
If she does not admit, lineage is established.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مطلقہ رجعیہ کے بچے کا نسب ثابت ہو جائے گا جب اس نے بچہ دو سال یا دو سال سے زیادہ میں جنا جب تک عورت نے انقضاء عدت کا اقرار نہ کیا ہو
The lineage of a child of a revocably divorced woman will be established when she gives birth to the child within two years or more than two years, as long as the woman has not acknowledged the completion of the iddah.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This is a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the attribution of a child born after a revocable divorce. The key condition is the time frame of two years from the divorce. If the woman gives birth within two years (or even after two years, according to some narrations), the child is attributed to the husband, because the maximum duration of pregnancy in the Hanafi school is two years. However, if the woman explicitly admits that her iddah has ended (e.g., by menstruation or other means), then the child is not attributed to the husband. This ruling protects the lineage and prevents disputes.

Key Terms
مطلقہ رجعیہ (muṭallaqah rajʿiyyah): A woman divorced with a revocable divorce (talaq rajʿi) where the husband can take her back during the iddah without a new marriage.
انقضاء عدت (inqiḍāʿ al-ʿiddah): The completion of the waiting period after divorce, marked by menstruation or months if pregnant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man divorces his wife revocably. She gives birth 18 months later and does not admit that her iddah ended. Is the child's lineage established to the husband?
A) Yes, because the birth is within two years.
B) No, because 18 months is too long.
C) Yes, but only if the husband acknowledges.
D) No, because she did not admit iddah completion.

Key Takeaway
A child born within two years of a revocable divorce is attributed to the husband unless the woman explicitly admits her iddah ended.

Bā'in Divorce During Terminal Illness: Inheritance Rules and the Shafi'i Dispute
Explaining Hanafi ruling on inheritance after bā'in divorce in terminal illness, with Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on inheritance after a bā'in divorce during terminal illness and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
A bā'in divorce during terminal illness does not automatically disinherit the wife if she is still in 'iddah.

Divorce during a terminal illness raises a unique conflict: the husband's attempt to prevent inheritance versus the wife's pre-existing right. The Hanafi school blocks the husband's evasion by delaying the divorce's full effect until after the 'iddah. Imam al-Shafi'i, however, sees the marriage bond as fully severed. This lesson unpacks the proof and practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: if the husband dies during the wife's 'iddah, she inherits; if after, she does not. Also note the five conditions from the commentary.
The ruling applies only to bā'in divorce, not raj'i.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i holds she never inherits because the marriage bond is severed. Understand his reasoning: inheritance requires a subsisting marriage, which is absent.
The Shafi'i position is consistent: if the wife dies, the husband does not inherit either.
3
Analyse the Hanafi rational proof
The husband's intention to defeat the wife's right is thwarted by delaying the divorce's effect until 'iddah ends. Marriage retains some effects during 'iddah, so inheritance can remain.
This is a case of 'farār' (fleeing from inheritance).
4
Examine the transmitted proof
The incident of Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf and Tamādir: Caliph Uthman gave her inheritance, and the Companions remained silent, establishing tacit consensus (ijmā' sukūtī). Also reports from Aisha, Umar, Uthman, Ibn Mas'ud.
The Hidayah only mentions rational proof; the commentary adds transmitted proof.
5
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi school gives inheritance if death occurs during 'iddah; Shafi'i school never gives it. This affects estate distribution and legal advice.
The dispute is based on different usul regarding the effect of bā'in divorce on remaining legal consequences.

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم

بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
باب طلاق المريض
ترجمہ ( یہ ) باب بیمار کی طلاق کے احکام کے بیان میں) ہے
باب طلاق المريض
تشریح سابقہ ابواب میں مصنف علیہ الرحمہ تندرست کی طلاق کو اس کے تمام اقسام کے ساتھ بیان فرما چکے ہیں اس باب میں بیمار کی طلاق کے احکام بیان فرمائیں گے چونکہ مرض عارض ہے اور عدم مرض یعنی تندرستی اصل اور اصل مقدم ہوتا ہے عارض پر اسلئے ترتیب میں تندرست کی طلاق کے احکام پہلے بیان کیئے گئے اور مریض کی طلاق کے احکام بعد میں۔
مرض الموت میں طلاق بائن دینے کا حکم
اذا طلق الرجل امرأته في مرض موته طلاقا بائنا فمات وهى فى العدة ورثته وان مات بعد انقضاء العدة فلاميراث لها وقال الشافعي لاترث في الوجهين لان الزوجية قد بطلت بهذا العارض وهي السبب ولهذ الايرثها اذامـاتـت ولنا ان الزوجية سبب ارثها في مرض موته و الزوج قصد ابطاله فيرد عليه قصده بتاخير عمله الى زمان انقضاء العدة دفعا للضرر عنها وقدامكن لان النكاح في العدة يبقى في حق بعض الأثار فجازان يبقى فى حق ارثها عنه بخلاف ما بعد الانقضاء لانه لا امكان والزوجية في هذه الحالة ليست بسبب لارثه عنها فيبطل في حقه خصوصا اذارضی به
ترجمہ اور جب مرد نے اپنی بیوی کو اپنے مرض وفات میں طلاق بائن دی پھر مر گیا حال یہ کہ وہ عورت عدت میں ہے تو ( عورت ) اس کی وارث ہو گی اور اگر وہ عورت کی ) عدت گذرنے کے بعد مرا تو عورت کے واسطے میراث نہیں ہوگی اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ وہ دونوں صورتوں میں وارث نہیں ہوگی کیونکہ زوجہ ہونا اس عارض کی وجہ سے باطل ہو گیا، حالانکہ زوجہ ہونا ہی ( میراث کا ) سبب تھا اور اسی وجہ سے اگر عورت مرگئی ہو تو مرد اس کا وارث نہیں ہوتا اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ زوجہ ہونا شوہر کے مرض وفات میں عورت کے وارث ہونے کا سبب ہے اور شوہر نے اس کو باطل کرنے کا ارادہ کیا ہے تو شوہر کا ( یہ ) قصد اسی پر رد کر دیا جائے گا زمانہ عدت کے گذرنے تک کیلئے اس کے عمل کو موخر کر کے تا کہ عورت سے ضرر دور ہو اور ایسی تاخیر ) ممکن بھی ہے کیونکہ عدت کے اندر بعض آثار کے حق میں نکاح باقی رہتا ہے۔ تو ممکن ہے کہ شوہر سے عورت کی میراث کے حق میں بھی نکاح باقی رہے۔ بخلاف انقضاء عدت کے مابعد ، کیونکہ امکان نہیں ہے اور زوجیت اس حالت میں عورت سے شوہر کے وارث ہونے کا سبب نہیں ہے تو شوہر کے حق میں (سبب ) باطل ہوگا ، بالخصوص جب شوہر اس پر راضی بھی ہو چکا۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر شوہر نے اپنے مرض وفات میں اپنی بیوی کو طلاق بائن دے دی بغیر بیوی کی رضا مندی کے ، پھر اس شوہر کا انتقال ہو گیا حالانکہ اس کی یہ بیوی عدت میں ہے اور وراثت کی مستحق ہے تو یہ اپنے شوہر کی وارث ہوگی۔ اس مسئلہ میں چند قیود ہیں

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم ان کو ملاحظہ فرمائیے۔ اول یہ کہ طلاق کو بائن کی قید کے ساتھ مقید کیا ہے کیونکہ اگر طلاق رجعی دی ہے تو یہ عورت حکم نکاح کی وجہ سے وارث ہوگی ، نہ کہ فرار کی وجہ سے اسلئے کہ طلاق رجعی کے بعد عدت کے زمانے میں نکاح من کل وجہ باقی رہتا ہے۔ دوم یہ کہ طلاق بائن کو مرض موت کے ساتھ مقید کیا ہے۔ اسلئے کہ اگر شوہر نے مرض کی حالت میں طلاق دی پھر وہ صحت مند ہو گیا پھر مر گیا تو وہ عورت وارث نہیں ہو گی۔ سوم یہ کہ عورت کی غیر رضا کے ساتھ مقید کیا ہے۔ کیونکہ اگر طلاق عورت کی رضا مندی سے دی گئی ہے تو بھی یہ عورت وارث نہیں ہو گی۔ چہارم یہ کہ استحقاق وراثت کی قید کے ساتھ مقید کیا ہے۔ اسلئے کہ اگر یہ عورت کتابیہ ہے یا باندی تو اس صورت میں بھی وارث نہیں ہو گی ۔ پنجم یہ کہ موت فی العدت کے ساتھ مقید کیا ہے۔ کیونکہ اگر عدت پوری ہونے کے بعد مرا ہے تو اس صورت میں بھی وارث نہیں ہوگی ، اگر چہ امام مالک فرماتے ہیں کہ اس صورت میں وارث ہوگی۔ صاحب عنا یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ شوہر کا اپنے مرض وفات میں طلاق دینا، اس کو طلاق فار کہتے ہیں اور فرار کا حکم جس طرح شوہر کی جانب سے ثابت ہوتا ہے اسی طرح عورت کی جانب سے بھی ثابت ہوگا۔ مثلاً عورت اپنے مرض وفات میں مرتد ہ ہوگئی۔ العیاذ باللہ تو اس کا شوہر
وارث ہوگا۔
حاصل نیہ کہ احناف کے نزدیک شوہر کا انتقال اگر عدت کے زمانے میں ہوا ہے تو اس کی بیوی وارث ہوگی اور اگر عدت گذرنے کے بعد انتقال ہوا ہے تو وارث نہیں ہوگی اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک دونوں صورتوں میں وارث نہیں ہوگی ۔ خواہ شوہر کا انتقال عدت میں ہوا ہو یا عدت کے بعد ۔
امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ زوجین کے درمیان وراثت کا سبب زوجیت کا رشتہ ہے اور طلاق بائن واقع کرنے کی وجہ سے زوجیت باطل ہوگئی۔ لہذا وراثت کا حکم بغیر سبب کے ثابت نہیں ہوگا ۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر اس حال میں عورت کا انتقال ہو جائے تو شوہر
وارث نہیں ہوتا ۔
ہمارے پاس دلیل عقلی اور نقلی دونوں ہیں۔ لیکن صاحب ہدایہ نے دلیل نقلی ذکر نہیں فرمائی ، دلیل نفلی کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ امراة فار کا مستحق دراخت ہونا صحابہ کے اجماع سے ثابت ہے۔ تفصیل یہ ہے کہ عبدالرحمن بن عوف نے اپنی بیوی تماضر کو اپنے مرض وفات میں طلاق بائن دی ، اور عبدالرحمن بن عوف کی وفات ہو گئی درانحالیکہ ان کی بیوی تماضر ابھی عدت ہی میں ہے تو حضرت عثمان نے عبد الرحمن بن عوف کی بیوی تماضر کو ان کا وارث بنایا اور یہ واقعہ صحابہ کی موجودگی میں پیش آیا۔ لیکن کسی نے حضرت عثمان کے اس فیصلہ پر نکیر نہیں فرمائی۔ اس وجہ سے یہ اجتماع سکوتی ہوا۔ حضرت عائشہؓ سے مروی ہے ان امرأة الفار ترث بے شک امرأة فاروارث ہوگی۔ اس کے علاوہ حضرت عمر ، عثمان علی ، ابن مسعود اور دیگرا کا برصحابہ سے یہی مروی ہے اور کسی ایک صحابی سے اس کے خلاف ثابت نہیں ۔ پس اجماع سکوتی متحقق ہو گیا اور یہ جو عبداللہ بن الزبیر سے روایت کیا جاتا ہے کہ اگر معاملہ میرے سپرد ہوتا تو میں تماضر کو وراثت نہ دلاتا۔ کچھ مصر نہیں کیونکہ
جس وقت اجماع منعقد ہوا اس وقت عبداللہ بن زبیر بچے تھے اور یہ کلام بعد کا ہے اور اختلاف متاخرا جماع سابق کا معارض نہیں ہوتا۔ صاحب ہدایہ کی بیان کردہ دلیل عقلی کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ شوہر کے مرض وفات میں عورت کا بیوی ہونا عورت کے وارث ہونے کا سبب ہے، کیونکہ شوہر کے مرض وفات میں بیوی کا حق اس کے مال کے ساتھ متعلق ہو جاتا ہے۔ پس اس حالت میں شوہر نے طلاق بائن دے کر اس کے حق وراثت کو باطل کرنے کا ارادہ کیا ہے لہذا اس کے اس غلط ارادے کو اس پر لوٹا دیا جائے گا بائیں طور کہ طلاق کے عمل کو عدت
The chapter of divorce of a sick person. When a man divorces his wife with a bā'in divorce during his terminal illness, then he dies while she is in the 'iddah, she inherits from him. If he dies after the expiry of the 'iddah, she has no inheritance. Al-Shafi'i said: She does not inherit in both cases because marital relationship has been invalidated by this obstacle, and it is the cause. For this reason, if she dies, he does not inherit. Our proof is that the marital relationship is the cause of her inheritance during his terminal illness, and the husband intended to invalidate it, so his intention is rejected against him by delaying its effect until the period of 'iddah to remove harm from her, and this is possible because marriage remains in some effects during 'iddah, so it is possible that it remains for her inheritance from him, unlike after the expiry because there is no possibility. The marital relationship in this state is not a cause for his inheritance from her, so it becomes invalid in his right, especially since he consented.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling on a bā'in divorce given by a husband during his terminal illness. The passage begins by stating the Hanafi position: if the husband dies while the wife is still in her 'iddah, she inherits; if he dies after the 'iddah expires, she does not inherit. Then it presents the Shafi'i view that she never inherits because the marriage bond is severed by the divorce. The Hanafi proof is rational: the wife's right of inheritance becomes connected to the husband's wealth during his terminal illness, so if he divorces her to deprive her, his action is thwarted by delaying the effect of divorce until after 'iddah, as long as she remains in 'iddah. This is possible because marriage still has some legal effects during 'iddah. The commentary also lists five conditions: the divorce must be bā'in (not raj'i), given during terminal illness (not if he recovers), without her consent, she must be a Muslim free woman (not a kitābiyya or slave), and he must die within 'iddah. The passage also mentions the concept of 'farār' (fleeing from inheritance) which applies to both spouses. Then it cites the hadith of Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf: Caliph Uthman gave his divorced wife Tamādir inheritance from him, and the Companions remained silent, establishing a tacit consensus (ijmā' sukūtī). This consensus is the transmitted proof, though the Hidayah author only mentions the rational proof. The passage refutes an objection from Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr, noting he was a child at the time of the incident.

Key Terms
طلاق بائن (talāq bā'in): An irrevocable divorce that severs the marriage bond immediately, but during 'iddah some effects remain.
مرض الموت (marḍ al-mawt): A terminal illness that is likely to lead to death and from which the person dies.
عدة ('iddah): The waiting period after divorce or death during which a woman cannot remarry.
فرار (farār): The act of fleeing from inheritance rights by one spouse against the other through a legal action like divorce or apostasy during terminal illness.
اجماع سکوتی (ijmā' sukūtī): Tacit consensus of scholars: when a ruling is issued in the presence of qualified scholars and none object, it is considered a valid consensus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under which condition does a wife inherit from her husband after a bā'in divorce during his terminal illness according to the Hanafi school?
A) If the husband dies at any time after the divorce.
B) If the husband dies while she is still in her 'iddah.
C) If the wife gives consent to the divorce.
D) If the divorce is raj'i.

Key Takeaway
A wife divorced bā'in during her husband's terminal illness inherits from him only if she is still in her 'iddah at his death, based on the principle of blocking flight from inheritance and supported by Companion consensus.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
6 min
Conditions and Hanafi Proofs for Wife's Inheritance after Deathbed Divorce
Explains five conditions and Hanafi proofs for wife's inheritance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the five conditions for a divorced wife's inheritance in the Hanafi school and EXPLAIN the Hanafi proofs (ijma' sukuti and istihsan) against the Shafi'i objection.

Core Idea
A husband's attempt to deprive his wife of inheritance by divorcing her on his deathbed is legally thwarted; she still inherits if he dies within her iddah.

This lesson examines a key Hanafi fiqh ruling on inheritance after a deathbed divorce. You will learn the five conditions required for the wife to inherit, the rational and transmitted proofs behind the Hanafi position, and how it differs from Imam al-Shafi'i's view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five conditions
Read the passage and list the five restrictions: ba'in divorce, deathbed illness, wife's non-consent, eligibility to inherit, death within iddah.
These are shurut for the wife to inherit.
2
Understand talaq al-firar
The divorce is called 'escaping divorce' because the husband tries to escape his wife's inheritance right. This concept underlies the Hanafi ruling.
The ruling applies equally if the wife apostatises during her deathbed illness.
3
Examine the transmitted proof (dalil naqli)
The Hanafis rely on the silent consensus (ijma' sukuti) of the Companions in the case of Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf and his wife Tumadir, and on a hadith of Aisha.
No Companion objected to Uthman's ruling, so it became a valid consensus.
4
Analyze the rational proof (istihsan)
The wife's right to inheritance becomes attached to the husband's property during his deathbed illness. His divorce is a wrongful attempt to nullify it, so the effect of the divorce is postponed until the end of iddah.
This answers why she inherits: the divorce is turned back against him.
5
Compare with the Shafi'i position and Hanafi response
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that ba'in divorce severs the marriage, so inheritance cannot arise. The Hanafi response: the wife's attached right justifies postponing the divorce's effect on inheritance.
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafi says wife inherits; Shafi'i says she does not.

معارض نہیں ہوتا۔ صاحب ہدایہ کی بیان کردہ دلیل عقلی کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ شوہر کے مرض وفات میں عورت کا بیوی ہونا عورت کے وارث ہونے کا سبب ہے، کیونکہ شوہر کے مرض وفات میں بیوی کا حق اس کے مال کے ساتھ متعلق
