مؤخر کر دیا گیا تا کہ عورت سے حرمانِ وراثت کا ضرر دور ہو۔ و قد امکن سے ایک سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ اگر طلاق کے عمل کو مؤخر کرنے کا سبب عورت سے ضرر کو دور کرنا ہے تو اس حکم میں مدخول بہا اور غیر مدخول بہا قبل انقضاء العدت اور بعد انقضاء العدت سب برابر ہونی چاہیں ، حالانکہ ایسا نہیں، کیونکہ غیر مدخول بہا کو اگر مرض وفات میں طلاق دی اور پھر مر گیا تو یہ غیر مدخول بہا بھی وارث نہیں ہوگی اور اسی طرح اگر عدت گذرنے کے بعد مرا ہے تو مدخول بہا بھی مستحق وراثت نہیں ہوگی ۔ جواب بلاشبہ طلاق کے عمل کو مؤخر کرنے کا سبب عورت سے ضرر کو دور کرنا ہے لیکن طلاق کے عمل کو اسی حد تک مؤخر کیا جا سکتا ہے جس حد تک مؤخر کرنا ممکن ہو اور چونکہ عدت کے ختم ہونے تک طلاق کے عمل کو مؤخر کرنا ممکن ہے کیونکہ عدت میں من وجہ نکاح باقی رہتا ہے۔ اس وجہ سے عدت کے ختم ہونے تک طلاق کے عمل کو مؤخر کر دیا گیا۔ اور چونکہ عدت گذر جانے کے بعد نکاح بالکل باقی نہیں رہتا من وجہ اور نہ من کل وجہ ۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ عدت کے بعد تک طلاق کے عمل کو مؤخر کرنا ممکن نہیں ہے۔ اس وجہ سے ما بعد العدت طلاق کے عمل کو مؤخر نہیں کیا گیا اور چونکہ غیر مدخول بہا پر عدت واجب نہیں ، لہذا اس کے حق میں بھی طلاق کے عمل کو مؤخر نہیں کیا جا سکتا۔ والزوجية في هذه الحالة سے امام شافعی کے قیاس ولهذا لا يرثها اذا ماتت کا جواب ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ شوہر کے مرض وفات کی حالت میں اس کا شوہر ہونا عورت سے میراث پانے کا سبب نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ شوہر کے مرض وفات میں عورت کا حق اس کے مال کے ساتھ متعلق ہوتا ہے۔ نہ کہ مرد کا حق عورت کے مال کے ساتھ ، لہذا مرد کے حق میں سبب میراث باطل ہو جائے گا۔ خاص طور سے جب شوہر اس کو طلاق دے کر سبب میراث باطل کرنے پر راضی بھی ہو گیا۔
Chapter on the Divorce of the Sick. First: Divorce is restricted to ba'in because if it is raj'i, the wife inherits due to the marriage tie, not due to escape, since after raj'i divorce the marriage remains in all respects during the iddah. Second: Ba'in divorce is restricted to deathbed illness because if he divorced while ill then recovered then died, she does not inherit. Third: It is restricted to the wife's non-consent because if she consented, she does not inherit. Fourth: It is restricted to eligibility for inheritance because if she is a kitabiyya or slave, she does not inherit. Fifth: It is restricted to death during the iddah because if he died after the iddah, she does not inherit, although Imam Malik says she would. The author of 'Inayah says: A husband divorcing during his deathbed illness is called talaq al-firar (escaping divorce), and the ruling of escape applies from the husband's side as well as the wife's. For example, if the wife becomes an apostate during her deathbed illness, then her husband inherits from her. In summary, according to the Hanafis, if the husband dies during the iddah, his wife inherits; if after the iddah, she does not. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, she does not inherit in either case, whether death occurs in iddah or after. Imam al-Shafi'i's evidence is that the cause of inheritance between spouses is the marital bond, and ba'in divorce nullifies it, so inheritance cannot be established without cause. Therefore if the wife dies in such state, the husband does not inherit. We have both rational and transmitted proofs. However, the author of Hidayah did not mention the transmitted proof. The transmitted proof is that a woman divorced by escape (imra'at al-far) inherits, established by the consensus of the Companions. The details: Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf gave his wife Tumadir a ba'in divorce during his deathbed illness, then he died while she was in iddah. Uthman made Tumadir his heir, and this happened in the presence of the Companions without any objection. This constitutes silent consensus. Aisha narrated: 'Indeed, the woman divorced by escape inherits.' Additionally, this is reported from Umar, Uthman, Ali, Ibn Mas'ud and other senior Companions, and no contrary report from any Companion is established. Thus silent consensus is confirmed. As for the narration from Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr that 'if the matter were left to me, I would not give Tumadir inheritance,' it is not considered because at the time consensus was established, he was a child, and his later opinion does not oppose the earlier consensus. The rational proof presented by the author of Hidayah is that the wife's status as wife during the husband's deathbed illness is the cause of her inheritance, because her right becomes attached to his property. So when the husband gives a ba'in divorce intending to nullify her right, his wrong intention is turned back against him such that the divorce is postponed until the end of the iddah to remove the harm of deprivation from her. This answers the objection from the phrase 'and it is possible' (wa qad amkan). The objection: if postponement is to remove harm, then all women (whether consummated or not, before or after iddah) should be equal, but they are not. Response: postponement is only possible to the extent it is possible. It is possible to postpone until the end of iddah because during iddah the marriage remains from one aspect. After iddah it does not, so postponement is not possible. Since iddah is not obligatory for an unconsummated wife, postponement is not possible for her. This answers Shafi'i's analogy based on the phrase 'and therefore he does not inherit from her if she dies' (wa li hadha la yarithuha idha maatat). The response: during the husband's deathbed illness, his being a husband is not a cause for him to inherit from her, because her right is attached to his property, not his right to hers. Therefore his cause for inheritance is nullified, especially since he consented to nullify that cause by divorcing her.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hadaya opens the chapter on divorce during deathbed illness (marad al-mawt) and establishes the Hanafi position that a wife divorced with a ba'in (irrevocable) divorce during her husband's terminal illness inherits from him if he dies within her iddah. The commentator first lists five conditions for this inheritance: (1) the divorce must be ba'in, not raj'i, because raj'i divorce does not sever the marriage; (2) the divorce must occur during the husband's deathbed illness, not if he recovers; (3) the wife must not have consented, because if she asked for the divorce, she is considered to have waived her right; (4) the wife must be eligible to inherit (not a non-Muslim or slave); (5) the husband must die within the iddah. If he dies after the iddah, she does not inherit, although Imam Malik disagrees. The commentator then explains the concept of 'talaq al-firar' (escape divorce), where the husband tries to deprive his wife of inheritance. He then contrasts the Hanafi position with Imam Shafi'i, who holds that the wife never inherits because ba'in divorce destroys the marital bond. The Hanafis provide two proofs: a transmitted proof (naqli) based on the silent consensus (ijma' sukuti) of the Companions, illustrated by the case of Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf and his wife Tumadir, and a rational proof (aqli) based on istihsan: the wife's right to inheritance becomes attached to her husband's property during his deathbed illness, so his attempt to nullify it through divorce is thwarted by postponing the divorce's effect until the end of the iddah. The passage then answers objections, including why the ruling does not apply to unconsummated wives or after the iddah (because postponement is only possible while the marriage persists in some form), and why the husband does not inherit if the wife dies during the iddah (because his right is not attached to her property in the same way).

Key Terms
طلاق بائن (talaq ba'in): Irrevocable divorce that severs the marital bond immediately; the husband cannot take her back except with a new marriage.
عدت (iddah): Waiting period after divorce or death, during which the woman cannot remarry.
مرض موت (marad al-mawt): Deathbed illness: a serious illness from which the person dies, and which prevents him from managing his affairs normally.
اجماع سکوتی (ijma' sukuti): Silent consensus: when some scholars issue a ruling and others remain silent, indicating approval.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, under which of the following conditions does a wife inherit from her husband if he divorced her during his deathbed illness?
A) She was given a raj'i divorce and he died after her iddah ended.
B) She was given a ba'in divorce with her consent and he died within her iddah.
C) She was given a ba'in divorce without her consent and he died within her iddah, and she is eligible to inherit.
D) She was given a ba'in divorce without her consent and he died after her iddah.

Key Takeaway
If a husband divorces his wife on his deathbed, she inherits if he dies within her iddah because of the attached right to his property, based on istihsan and silent consensus.

Talaq — Divorce

Effect of Wife's Request or Consent on Inheritance in Deathbed Divorce
Rulings on inheritance when wife requests or consents to deathbed divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state whether a wife inherits from her deathbed-divorced husband based on whether she requested a ba'in or raj'i divorce, and explain the legal reasoning (talil) for the difference.

Core Idea
A wife who consents to a ba'in divorce forfeits inheritance; but if she requests a raj'i divorce, she retains her right because the marriage persists.

In Hanafi fiqh, a divorce pronounced on the deathbed is normally considered effective, but the wife's inheritance right is preserved if the marriage is still legally intact at the time of death. This lesson focuses on how the wife's own action—whether she requests or consents to the divorce—affects that preservation. The key distinction lies between revocable (raj'i) and irrevocable (ba'in) divorce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios of non-inheritance
The passage lists three cases where the wife does not inherit: (1) she directly asks for three divorces, (2) the husband gives her the option to choose and she chooses herself, (3) she initiates khula'. In all these, the divorce is ba'in (irrevocable) and the wife consented.
2
Identify the one scenario of inheritance
If the wife asks specifically for a raj'i (revocable) divorce, and the husband gives three divorces (which are actually ba'in), she still inherits. The reason is that her request was for a type of divorce that does not end the marriage completely.
The husband's action of giving three divorces is ba'in, but the wife's request was for raj'i, so her intention was not to nullify her right.
3
Understand the legal cause (talil)
The law postpones the effect of divorce to protect the wife's inheritance right. By consenting to a ba'in divorce, she waives that protection. Asking for a raj'i divorce does not waive it because raj'i divorce does not sever the marriage tie.
The talil is based on the wife's consent to nullify her right.
4
Apply to a new scenario
Given a hypothetical: A dying husband tells his wife 'I divorce you thrice' after she says 'give me a final divorce.' She inherits? No, because her request was for a ba'in divorce (final/irrevocable).
The key is whether the wife's request/consent was for a ba'in or raj'i divorce.

Source Text

ترجمہ اور اگر (شوہر نے) عورت کے کہنے سے اس کو تین طلاقیں دے دیں ، یا اپنی عورت سے کہا اختیار کر تو ۔ پس عورت نے اپنے نفس کو اختیار کر لیا یا عورت نے شوہر سے خلع کر لیا پھر شوہر مر گیا حالانکہ وہ عورت عدت میں ہے، تو وہ شوہر کی وارث ن ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ عورت (خود) اپنے حق میراث کو باطل کرنے پر راضی ہو گئی۔ حالانکہ مؤخر کرنا اس کے حق کی وجہ سے تھا اور اگر عورت نے کہا مجھے طلاق رجعی دے دے۔ پس شوہر نے اس کو تین طلاقیں دے دیں تو عورت اس کی وارث ہوگی۔ اسلئے کہ طلاق رجعی نکاح کو زائل نہیں کرتی۔ پس یہ عورت طلاق رجعی کا سوال کرنے کی وجہ سے اپنا حق باطل کرنے پر راضی ہونے والی نہیں ہوگی۔
تشریح ۔ اس عبارت میں تین صورتیں بیان کی گئی ہیں۔
1) عورت نے اپنے شوہر سے تین طلاقوں کا سوال کیا۔ شوہر نے اس کو اپنے مرض وفات میں تین طلاقیں دے دیں۔
And if he divorces her three times at her command, or said to her 'choose' and she chose herself, or she khula'd from him, then he died while she is in iddah, she does not inherit from him, because she consented to the nullification of her right, and the postponement was for her right. But if she said 'divorce me a raj'i divorce' and he divorced her three times, she inherits from him, because raj'i divorce does not remove the marriage, so she is not consenting to the nullification of her right by her request. Translation: And if (the husband) gives her three divorces at her instruction, or said to his wife 'choose', so she chose herself, or the wife khula'd from him, then the husband died while she is in iddah, she will not be his heir, because the wife (herself) consented to nullify her right to inheritance. The postponement was because of her right. And if the wife said 'give me a raj'i divorce', and the husband gave her three divorces, then the wife inherits from him, because raj'i divorce does not remove the marriage. So she is not consenting to nullify her right by requesting raj'i divorce. Explanation: In this passage, three scenarios are mentioned: 1) The wife requested three divorces from her husband, and the husband gave them to her during his deathbed illness.

Commentary
This passage presents the matn (core text) from Al-Hidayah concerning three specific scenarios where the wife's involvement in the divorce affects her inheritance. The ruling is clear: if the wife actively seeks or consents to a ba'in divorce (by asking for three divorces, choosing herself after being given the option, or initiating khula'), then she does not inherit, regardless of whether the husband dies within her iddah. The reason is that the law's postponement of the divorce's effect was designed to protect her right, but by consenting to the divorce, she implicitly waives that protection. Conversely, if she asks for a raj'i (revocable) divorce, and the husband gives her three divorces (which are actually ba'in because three count as ba'in), she still inherits because her request was for a revocable divorce, which does not sever the marriage entirely. Her intention was not to nullify her right. The commentator then begins to explain the first scenario in detail, noting that there are three scenarios in the passage.

Key Terms
طلاق رجعی (talaq raj'i): Revocable divorce: the husband can take back his wife without a new marriage during the iddah.
خلع (khula'): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation paid to the husband, typically ending the marriage irrevocably.
اختیار (ikhtiyar (option)): Choosing oneself: when the husband gives the wife the option to choose herself (divorce), and she does so.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A wife on her husband's deathbed initiates khula' by offering compensation. The husband accepts and divorces her. He dies while she is in iddah. Does she inherit?
A) Yes, because khula' is a type of divorce that does not affect inheritance.
B) No, because khula' is a ba'in divorce and she consented to nullify her right.
C) Yes, because the divorce was initiated by the wife, so it is not valid on deathbed.
D) No, because any divorce on deathbed invalidates inheritance.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a wife who consents to a ba'in divorce on the deathbed forfeits inheritance; but if she requests a raj'i divorce, she retains her right because the marriage persists in a revocable state.

Talaq — Divorce

Wife's Consent to Divorce During Terminal Illness: Inheritance Forfeiture
Ruling on inheritance when wife requests divorce, uses option, or khul' in husband's terminal illness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios where a wife forfeits inheritance upon divorce during her husband's terminal illness and the one scenario where she retains it, and explain the rationale based on her consent.

Core Idea
Consent to divorce annuls inheritance right; asking for revocable divorce does not.

Divorce during terminal illness raises a conflict between the wife's right to inherit and the husband's interest in preventing fraud. The Hanafi school resolves this by examining the wife's consent: if she initiates or accepts the divorce, she forfeits her inheritance; if she merely asks for a revocable divorce, she retains it. This lesson dissects the four scenarios from the Hidayah and the legal reasoning (talil) behind each.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Four Scenarios
Read the passage carefully and list each case mentioned: (1) wife requests three divorces, (2) husband gives option and wife chooses herself, (3) wife obtains khul', (4) wife asks for revocable divorce but receives three.
2
Determine the Inheritance Ruling
For each scenario, state whether the wife inherits or not. Note that the first three result in no inheritance; the fourth results in inheritance.
The exception is when the wife asks only for revocable divorce.
3
Extract the Legal Principle
The text states the reason: 'she consented to annulment of her right'. Identify how each scenario demonstrates consent: explicit request, choosing separation, and paying compensation all indicate willingness to end the marriage.
Consent can be explicit or implied by action.
4
Apply the Principle to the Exception
Explain why asking for revocable divorce does not constitute consent to annulment. Since revocable divorce does not dissolve the marriage during iddah, the wife's request does not aim at final separation, so her inheritance right remains intact.
The marriage continues in some aspects during revocable iddah.
5
Evaluate the Talil (Reasoning)
The ruling is based on the idea that postponing the divorce effect was for her benefit; when she voluntarily abandons that benefit, protection is removed. Recognize this as a form of qiyas or istihsan rooted in the principle of consent.
This reasoning prevents the wife from defrauding heirs by initiating divorce but still claiming inheritance.

ترجمہ اور اگر (شوہر نے) عورت کے کہنے سے اس کو تین طلاقیں دے دیں ، یا اپنی عورت سے کہا اختیار کر تو ۔ پس عورت نے اپنے نفس کو اختیار کر لیا یا عورت نے شوہر سے خلع کر لیا پھر شوہر مر گیا حالانکہ وہ عورت عدت میں ہے، تو وہ شوہر کی وارث نہ ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ عورت (خود) اپنے حق میراث کو باطل کرنے پر راضی ہو گئی۔ حالانکہ مؤخر کرنا اس کے حق کی وجہ سے تھا اور اگر عورت نے کہا مجھے طلاق رجعی دے دے۔ پس شوہر نے اس کو تین طلاقیں دے دیں تو عورت اس کی وارث ہوگی۔ اسلئے کہ طلاق رجعی نکاح کو زائل نہیں کرتی۔ پس یہ عورت طلاق رجعی کا سوال کرنے کی وجہ سے اپنا حق باطل کرنے پر راضی ہونے والی نہیں ہوگی۔

Translation: And if (the husband) gives her three divorces at her request, or he said to his wife 'choose', so the wife chose herself, or the wife khul'ed from her husband, then the husband dies while that woman is in 'iddah, then she will not inherit from her husband. And if the woman said 'give me a revocable divorce,' then the husband gave her three divorces, then the woman will inherit from him. Because revocable divorce does not remove the marriage. So this woman, by asking for revocable divorce, she was not consenting to annulment of her right.

Explanation: This passage mentions three cases: 1) The woman asked her husband for three divorces. The husband gave her three divorces during his terminal illness. 2) The husband gave his wife the option during his terminal illness. The wife chose herself. 3) The woman khul'ed from her husband during his terminal illness. The ruling for these three cases is that if this husband dies and the woman is in 'iddah, then this woman will not inherit from her husband. The proof is that in these three cases, the woman consented to annul her right (because in the first case, the woman herself requested three divorces; in the second case, she chose herself and thus committed separation, which is evidence of consent; and in the third case, she made wealth obligatory upon herself through khul' to achieve separation. This is also evidence of consent. And the divorce action was postponed because of the woman's right. So when the woman herself consented to annul her right, then protecting her right is not obligatory for others. And if the woman asked her husband for revocable divorce, but the husband gave her three divorces during his terminal illness, then this woman will inherit from him. The proof is that revocable divorce does not remove the marriage, so it will not be said that this woman, by asking for revocable divorce, consented to annul her right.

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hidayah on the inheritance rights of a wife divorced during her husband's terminal illness. The matn states three scenarios where the wife does not inherit: (1) she requests three divorces, (2) the husband gives her the option and she chooses separation, (3) she obtains khul'. In all these, the wife is deemed to have consented to forfeiting her inheritance, which was otherwise protected by postponing the divorce's effect until after the iddah. The fourth scenario shows that if the wife merely asks for a revocable divorce (talaq raj'i), she still inherits because revocable divorce does not dissolve the marriage during iddah, so her request does not indicate consent to loss of inheritance. The commentary (tashrih) elaborates on the proof: the wife's explicit or implied consent nullifies the need to protect her right. The reasoning is based on the principle that the postponement of divorce's effect was for her benefit; when she voluntarily abandons that benefit, the protection is removed.

Key Terms
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): The terminal illness of the husband during which special divorce and inheritance rulings apply to prevent fraud against heirs.
طلاق رجعي (talaq raj'i): A revocable divorce that does not dissolve the marriage during the iddah period, allowing the husband to take back his wife without a new contract.
خلع (khul'): A divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation, resulting in a permanent separation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which scenario does a wife inherit from her husband who dies during his terminal illness?
A) She asked for three divorces and he gave them.
B) He gave her the option and she chose herself.
C) She khul'ed from him.
D) She asked for revocable divorce but he gave her three.

Key Takeaway
A wife's consent to divorce during her husband's terminal illness forfeits her inheritance, but asking for revocable divorce does not, as it does not dissolve the marriage.

Husband's Acknowledgment to Divorced Wife During Terminal Illness: The Tuhma Dispute
Ruling on husband's acknowledgment/will to wife after confirming divorce in health, with intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the validity of a husband's acknowledgment or will to a wife he claims to have divorced in health, and explain how the principle of tuhma (suspicion) governs the dispute.

Core Idea
Suspicion of collusion (tuhma) limits a terminally ill husband's gift to his divorced wife, but the extent of limitation splits the Hanafi school.

When a husband in terminal illness claims he divorced his wife in health and she confirms, then he acknowledges a debt or makes a will for her, is the gift fully valid? Abu Hanifa and his two disciples disagree because of the potential for collusion. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the practical consequences for the wife's entitlement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize the two scenarios discussed: (1) husband claims divorce in health, wife confirms, then acknowledgment/will; (2) husband divorces by wife's command during illness, then acknowledgment/will.
The central legal issue is whether the wife is treated as a stranger or still subject to suspicion.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and reasoning
Abu Hanifa rules that the wife takes the lesser of the acknowledged amount/will and her inheritance. His reasoning: potential collusion (tuhma) exists because the wife might prefer divorce to enable larger gifts, and spouses may conspire to defraud other heirs.
He distinguishes between the amount equal to inheritance (no tuhma) and any excess (tuhma).
3
State Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's position and reasoning
The Sahibayn hold that the acknowledgment/will is fully valid. Their reasoning: once the divorce and iddah are confirmed, the wife becomes a stranger (ajnabiyya), eliminating tuhma. Evidence: he can marry her sister, his testimony for her is accepted, and zakat can be given to her.
They argue that tuhma only attaches to marriage and kinship, not to a stranger.
4
Note Zufar's exception in the second scenario
Zufar agrees with Abu Hanifa in the first scenario but differs in the second: when divorce was at the wife's request during illness, he says she takes the full amount because inheritance was annulled by her request, removing the impediment.
This shows the diversity within the Hanafi school even on the same facts.
5
Apply the principle of tuhma to determine the operative position
The text does not give explicit tarjih, but the structure and detailed defense of Abu Hanifa suggest his view is the mufta bihi. The key is to recognize that tuhma is a legal presumption that can limit dispositions in terminal illness.
Later Hanafi fatwa authorities (e.g., Ibn Abidin) generally adopt Abu Hanifa's position in this case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان قال لها في مرض موته كنت طلقتك ثلثا فى صحتى وانقضت عدتک فصدقته ثم اقرلها بدین او اوصى لها بوصية فلها الاقل من ذلك ومن الميراث عند ابي حنيفة وقال ابويوسف و محمد یجوز اقراره ووصيته وان طلقها ثلثا في مرضه بامرها ثم اقرلها بدين او اوصى لها بوصية فلها الاقل من ذلك ومن الميراث في قولهم جميعا الا على قول زفر فان لها جميع ما اوصى وما اقربه لان الميراث لما بطل بسوالهازال المانع من صحة الاقرار و الوصية وجه قولهما فى المسألة الأولى انهما لما تصاد قاعلى الطلاق وانقضاء العدة صارت اجنبية عنه حتى جازله ان يتزوج اختها فانعدمت التهمة الاترى انه تقبل شهادته لها و يجوز وضع الزكوة بخلاف المسالة الثانية لان العدة باقية وهى سبب التهمة والحكم يدار على دليل التهمة و لهذايدار على النكاح والقرابة ولاعدة في المسألة الاولى ولابي حنيفة في المسألتين ان التهمة قائمة لان المرأه قد تختار الطلاق لينفتح باب الاقرار والوصية عليها فيزيد حقها والزوجان قديتو اضعان على الاقرار بالفرقة وانقضاء العدة ليبرها الزوج بماله زيادة على ميراثها وهذه التهمة فى الزيادة فرددناها ولاتهمة في قدر الميراث فصححناه ولا مواضعة عادة فى حق الزكوة والتزوج والشهادة فلا تهمة في حق هذه الاحكام
And if he says to her in his terminal illness: 'I divorced you three times in my health and your iddah ended,' and she confirms him, then he acknowledges a debt to her or makes a will for her, then she takes the lesser of that and the inheritance according to Abu Hanifa. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: his acknowledgment and will are valid. And if he divorces her three times in his illness by her command, then he acknowledges a debt to her or makes a will for her, then she takes the lesser of that and the inheritance in all their sayings, except according to Zufar, for according to him she takes all that he willed and acknowledged because since inheritance was annulled by her request, the impediment to the validity of acknowledgment and will is removed. The proof of their (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's) view in the first issue is that when they both affirm the divorce and the end of the iddah, she becomes a stranger to him such that it is permitted for him to marry her sister, so suspicion (tuhma) is eliminated. Do you not see that his testimony for her is accepted and it is permissible to give zakat to her? Unlike the second issue because the iddah remains, which is the cause of suspicion, and the ruling is based on the evidence of suspicion. Therefore it is based on marriage and kinship, and there is no iddah in the first issue. And Abu Hanifa's view in both issues is that suspicion exists because the woman might choose divorce to open the door of acknowledgment and will in her favor to increase her right, and the two spouses may collude in affirming separation and end of iddah so that the husband may give her wealth in addition to her inheritance. This suspicion is regarding the increase, so we reject it, but there is no suspicion regarding the amount of the inheritance, so we affirm it. And there is normally no collusion regarding zakat, marriage, and testimony, so there is no suspicion regarding those rulings.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about a husband in terminal illness who claims he divorced his wife in health and that her iddah ended. If she confirms, then he acknowledges a debt or makes a will for her. Abu Hanifa rules she takes the lesser of the acknowledged amount/will and her inheritance, based on the possibility of collusion (tuhma) to increase her share. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say the acknowledgment and will are fully valid because the wife is now a stranger (no iddah, no marriage), eliminating suspicion; they argue that if the divorce and iddah are confirmed, she is like any non-relative, so testimony and zakat are permissible. Abu Hanifa counters that collusion is still possible because the wife may prefer divorce to enable larger gifts. Zufar differs in the second case (where divorce was by her command during illness), allowing full acknowledgment. The text explains the reasoning behind each position, emphasizing the role of suspicion (tuhma) in determining validity.

Key Terms
تہمة (tuhma): Suspicion of collusion or fraud between the spouses to deprive other heirs of their rightful shares.
اقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment of a debt or obligation owed to someone; in this context, by the husband to his wife.
وصية (wasiyya): Will or bequest made by the deceased, limited to one-third of the estate unless heirs consent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because she is still an heir and a will to an heir is invalid.
B) Because there is tuhma (suspicion of collusion) regarding any amount exceeding her inheritance.
C) Because the husband did not actually divorce her.
D) Because the wife requested the divorce, so she forfeits her right.

Key Takeaway
The principle of tuhma restricts a terminally ill person's gifts to a spouse even after divorce, limiting them to the inheritance amount unless collusion is impossible.

Inheritance of Wife Who Initiates Divorce During Husband's Death Illness
Ruling on three cases where wife loses inheritance, with exception for raj'i talaq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the three cases where a wife loses inheritance when she initiates divorce during her husband's death illness, and EXPLAIN the exception for revocable divorce.

Core Idea
A wife who consents to nullify her inheritance right by initiating divorce loses it, except in revocable divorce.

This passage from the Hidayah addresses a delicate scenario: a wife seeks divorce during her husband's terminal illness, and the husband dies during her iddah. Does she inherit? The ruling hinges on her consent to nullify her right. We will examine the three cases where she does not inherit and the one exception that preserves her right.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three cases
List the three scenarios where the wife initiates divorce: (1) husband gives her an option and she chooses divorce, (2) she performs khula', (3) she requests three divorces. Note that in each, the wife takes active steps to end the marriage.
These cases share the element of the wife's consent to separation.
2
Understand the legal reasoning
The proof (dalil) for denying inheritance is that the wife consented to nullify her right. Since the divorce was delayed only because of her right, her consent removes that protection. Grasp the principle: one who willingly forfeits a right cannot later claim it.
Consent is inferred from her actions: choosing herself, paying khula', or requesting three divorces.
3
Learn the exception
If the wife asks for a revocable divorce (talaq raj'i) and the husband gives three divorces, she still inherits. Why? Because revocable divorce does not dissolve the marriage immediately; it only becomes irrevocable after iddah. Thus, her request for raj'i is not consent to nullify her inheritance.
Raj'i talaq preserves the marital bond during iddah, so the wife's right to inheritance remains intact.
4
Apply the rule to new scenarios
Test your understanding: Would a wife who asks for a ba'in (irrevocable) divorce inherit? According to the logic, if she seeks irrevocable separation, she consents to nullify her rights, so she would not inherit.
The principle extends: any action that shows willingness to forfeit inheritance leads to deprivation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب طلاق المريض (۲) شوہر نے اپنے مرض وفات میں اپنی بیوی کو اختیار دیا۔ بیوی نے اپنے نفس کو اختیار کر لیا۔ )، عورت نے اپنے شوہر کے مرض وفات میں اس سے ضلع کیا۔ ان تین صورتوں کا حکم یہ ہے کہ اگر یہ شوہر مر گیا اور عورات عدت میں ہے تو یہ عورت اپنے شوہر کی وارث نہیں ہوگی۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ ان تینوں صورتوں میں عورت اپنے حق کو باطل کرنے پر راضی ہو گئی (اسلئے کہ پہلی صورت میں عورت نے خود تین طلاقوں کی درخواست کی ہے اور دوسری صورت میں اپنے نفس کو اختیار کر کے فرقت کا ارتکاب کیا ہے جو دلیل رضا ہے اور تیسری صورت میں خلع کے ذریعہ اپنے اوپر مال لازم کیا ہے تا کہ فرقت حاصل ہو جائے۔ یہ بھی رضا مندی کی دلیل ہے۔ اور طلاق کے عمل کو مؤخر کیا گیا تھا عورت کے حق کی وجہ سے۔ پس جب عورت ہی اپنے حق کو باطل کرنے پر راضی ہوگئی تو دوسروں پر بھی اس کے حق کی حفاظت لازم نہیں رہی۔ اور اگر عورت نے اپنے شوہر سے طلاق رجعی مانگی مگر شوہر نے اس کو اپنے مرض وفات میں تین طلاقین دیں تو یہ عورت اس کی وارث ہوگی ۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ طلاق رجعی نکاح کو زائل نہیں کرتی، لہذا یہ نہیں کہا جائے گا کہ یہ عورت طلاق رجعی کا سوال کر کے اپنے حق کو باطل کرنے پر راضی ہوگئی ہے۔
Chapter of Divorce of the Sick Person. (2) Husband gave his wife an option during his death illness. She chose herself. A woman performed khula' from her husband during his death illness. The ruling for these three cases is that if this husband dies and the woman is in iddah, this woman will not be an heir of her husband. The proof is that in all three cases, the woman consented to nullify her right (because in the first case, she herself requested three divorces; in the second case, by choosing herself she committed separation, which is evidence of consent; and in the third case, through khula' she made wealth obligatory upon herself to obtain separation. This is also evidence of consent. The divorce action was delayed because of the woman's right. So when the woman herself consented to nullify her right, it is no longer necessary for others to protect her right. And if a woman asked her husband for a revocable divorce (talaq raj'i) but the husband gave her three divorces during his death illness, then this woman will be his heir. The proof is that revocable divorce does not nullify the marriage; therefore, it cannot be said that this woman, by requesting revocable divorce, consented to nullify her right.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage states the ruling for three scenarios where a wife initiates divorce during her husband's death illness: (1) husband gives her an option and she chooses herself (meaning she opts for divorce), (2) she performs khula' (ransom divorce), (3) she asks for three divorces. In all three, if the husband dies while she is still in iddah, she does not inherit from him. The legal reason (illa) is that she willingly consented to nullify her right to inheritance by seeking the divorce. However, there is an exception: if she asks for a revocable divorce (talaq raj'i) and the husband gives three divorces, she still inherits because revocable divorce does not dissolve the marriage immediately; it only becomes irrevocable after iddah. Therefore, her consent to raj'i divorce is not considered consent to nullify her inheritance right.

Key Terms
طلاق رجعی (talaq raj'i): A revocable divorce that does not dissolve the marriage immediately, allowing the husband to take the wife back during the iddah without a new nikah.
عدت (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of her husband before she can remarry.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) She requests a revocable divorce (raj'i) and the husband gives three divorces.
B) She performs khula' during the husband's death illness.
C) She is divorced by the husband in health without her request.
D) The husband gives her an option in health and she chooses divorce.

Key Takeaway
A wife who consents to nullify her inheritance right by initiating divorce during husband's death illness loses inheritance, unless the divorce is revocable (raj'i).

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Confession and Bequest to Divorced Wife During Death Illness
Intra-Hanafi dispute on confession/bequest to divorced wife during marad al-mawt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of a husband's confession or bequest to his divorced wife during death illness, and analyze how the presence or absence of suspicion (tuhma) affects the rulings in two distinct scenarios.

Core Idea
When iddah expires, she becomes a stranger, eliminating suspicion; when iddah remains or collusion is possible, suspicion restricts the amount to the lesser of confession and inheritance.

This lesson unpacks a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute about the validity of a sick man's financial dealings with his divorced wife. The core issue is whether the separation was genuine (eliminating suspicion of collusion) or manipulated to bypass inheritance rules. Understanding the reasoning of each imam will sharpen your ability to apply the principle of tuhma in similar cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Scenario 1: The husband claims he divorced his wife in health and her iddah has expired; she confirms. Then he confesses a debt or makes a bequest to her. Scenario 2: The husband divorces her three times at her request during his death illness, then confesses or bequeaths.
The critical difference is whether the wife's request triggered the divorce and whether the iddah has ended.
2
State the positions of the Hanafi imams
Abu Hanifa: In both scenarios, the wife gets the lesser of the confessed/bequeathed amount and her inheritance share. Abu Yusuf & Muhammad (Sahibayn): In scenario 1, the confession/bequest is fully valid; in scenario 2, they agree with Abu Hanifa. Zufar: In scenario 2, the full amount is due.
Note the agreement among Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn in scenario 2.
3
Understand the concept of tuhma (suspicion)
Tuhma is the legal presumption that a sick person may collude with an heir to deprive other heirs of their rightful shares. It restricts the validity of confessions and bequests in favor of heirs.
Tuhma is not applied when the recipient is a stranger (ajnabiyyah) — someone who does not inherit.
4
Analyze the reasoning of each imam
Sahibayn argue that in scenario 1, the wife becomes a stranger when the iddah expires; thus no tuhma. In scenario 2, iddah remains, so tuhma persists. Abu Hanifa holds that tuhma exists in both because the couple could collude to create a false claim of prior divorce. Zufar argues that since the wife's request nullified her inheritance, the obstacle to validity is removed.
Each position hinges on when tuhma is deemed present.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Under Abu Hanifa, the wife can never exceed her inheritance share. Under Sahibayn, she can get more if the divorce was before the death illness and iddah expired. Under Zufar, she can get the full amount even if divorced at her request during illness.
The difference is most stark in scenario 2.

کے حق میں قبول کر لی جائے گی اور ( مرد کو اپنے مال کی زکوۃ اس عورت کو دینا جائز ہے۔ برخلاف دوسرے مسئلہ کے، کیونکہ عدت باقی ہے اور یہی تہمت کا سبب تھی اور حکم کا مدار تہمت کی دلیل پر ہے اور اسی وجہ سے نکاح اور قرابت پر حکم کا مدار ہے اور پہلے مسئلہ میں عدت (باقی ) نہیں رہی اور امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل دونوں مسئلوں میں یہ ہے کہ تہمت موجود ہے۔ کیونکہ عورت بھی ( اس غرض سے ) طلاق کو اختیار کر لیتی ہے تا کہ اقرار اور وصیت کا دروازہ اس پر کھل جائے۔ پھر اس کا حق زیادہ ہو جائے اور شوہر بیوی کبھی دونوں فرقت کے اقرار اور عدت کے گذر جانے پر اتفاق کر لیتے ہیں، تاکہ شوہر ا سپر اپنے مال کے ساتھ اس کے حصہ میراث پر بڑھا کر تبرع کرے اور یہ تہمت (صرف) زیادتی میں ہے اس وجہ سے ہم نے زیادتی کورد کر دیا اور میراث کی مقدار میں کوئی تہمت نہیں لہذا ہم نے ( میراث کی مقدار کو ) صحیح رکھا اور عادتاز کوۃ اور تزوج اور گواہی کے حق میں اتفاق نہیں کیا جاتا۔ پس ان احکام کے حق میں تہمت ( معتبر نہیں۔ تشریح اس عبارت میں دو مسئلے زیر بحث ہیں: (1) شوہر نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا میں صحت کے زمانے میں تجھے طلاقیں دے چکا اور تیری عدت بھی پوری ہو گئی ۔ عورت نے اپنے شوہر کی تصدیق کر دی پھر اس کے بعد شوہر نے اس عورت کیلئے کچھ قرضہ کا اقرار کیا ، مثلاً کہا کہ میرے ذمہ اس کا ایک ہزار روپیہ ہے۔ یا اس عورت کیلئے اپنے مال مسترد کہ میں سے کچھ مال کی وصیت کر دی۔ عورت نے اپنے شوہر سے اس کے مرضِ وفات میں تین طلاقیں طلب کیں ، اس نے اس کو تین طلاقیں دے دی۔ پھر عدت میں اس عورت کیلئے کچھ قرضہ کا اقرار کیا یا کچھ مال کی وصیت کی۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ان دونوں صورتوں میں حکم یہ ہے کہ جس قدر مال کا اقرار کیا گیا ہے یا وصیت کی ہے اس سے اور اس کے حصہ میراث سے جو کم ہے وہ دیا جائے گا۔ اگر مال مقر بہ اور مال وصیت کم ہے تو وہ دے دیا جائے اور اگر حصہ میراث کم ہے تو یہ دے دیا جائے اور امام زفر کے نزدیک جس مقدار کا اقرار کیا ہے یا وصیت کی ہے عورت کو وہ دیا جائے گا۔ یہ مقدار حصہ میراث سے کم ہو یا زیادہ۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک پہلے مسئلہ میں وہ حکم And if he said to her during his death illness, 'I divorced you three times in my health and your iddah has expired,' and she confirmed him, then he confessed a debt to her or made a bequest to her, then she gets the lesser of that and the inheritance according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: his confession and bequest are valid. And if he divorced her three times in his illness at her command, then confessed a debt to her or made a bequest to her, then she gets the lesser of that and the inheritance according to all of them except on the saying of Zufar: for her is all that he bequeathed and all that he confessed, because when the inheritance is nullified by her request, the obstacle to the validity of confession and bequest is removed. The justification of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) in the first case is that when they both agree on the divorce and the expiration of the iddah, she becomes a stranger to him such that it becomes permissible for him to marry her sister, so the suspicion (tuhma) is eliminated. Do you not see that his testimony is accepted for her and it is permissible to give zakat to her? Contrary to the second case, because the iddah remains and it is the cause of suspicion, and the ruling revolves around the evidence of suspicion. For this reason, the ruling revolves around marriage and kinship, and there is no iddah in the first case. And for Abu Hanifa in both cases, the suspicion exists because the woman may choose divorce so that the door of confession and bequest opens for her and her right increases, and the two spouses sometimes agree on the confession of separation and expiration of iddah so that the husband may give her his wealth exceeding her inheritance. This suspicion is only in the increase, so we reject the increase, and there is no suspicion regarding the amount of inheritance, so we correct it. And there is no customary collusion regarding zakat, marriage, and testimony, so there is no suspicion regarding these rulings. Translation: And if the husband said to the woman during his death illness, 'I divorced you three times in my health and your iddah has passed,' so the woman confirmed his statement, then (the husband) confessed a debt for that woman or the husband made some bequest for her, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, for that woman, whatever is less from that confession or bequest and from her share of inheritance, she gets that. And Imam Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said that the sick person's confession and bequest are valid. And if the husband during death illness gave three divorces to the woman at her request, then confessed some debt for that woman or made some bequest for her, then by agreement (this is the ruling) that for the woman, whatever is less from that confession of debt or bequest and from the share of inheritance, she gets that. Except on the saying of Imam Zufar, because (according to Imam Zufar) whatever he bequeathed and whatever he confessed, she will get it entirely. Because when due to the woman's request for divorce, her inheritance became void, the obstacle to the validity of confession and bequest was removed. The justification of the Sahibayn in the first case is that when the husband and wife agreed on the divorce and the passing of the iddah, this woman became a stranger to him such that it became permissible for the husband to marry her sister. So suspicion has been eliminated. Do you not see that the man's testimony will be accepted in favor of this woman, and (the man) is allowed to give his zakat to this woman? Contrary to the second case, because the iddah remains and that was the cause of suspicion, and the ruling revolves around the evidence of suspicion, and for this reason the ruling revolves around marriage and kinship. And in the first case, the iddah does not remain. And the proof of Imam Abu Hanifa in both cases is that suspicion exists. Because the woman also (for this purpose) chooses divorce so that the door of confession and bequest opens for her, then her right increases. And sometimes both husband and wife agree on the confession of separation and passing of iddah so that the husband may grant her with his wealth exceeding her share of inheritance, and this suspicion is (only) in the increase, so we rejected the increase, and there is no suspicion in the amount of inheritance, so we kept the inheritance correct. And customarily, there is no agreement regarding zakat, marriage, and testimony, so suspicion is not considered in these rulings. Explanation: In this passage, two cases are under discussion: (1) The husband said to his wife, 'I divorced you in the time of health and your iddah has completed.' The woman confirmed her husband, then after that the husband confessed some debt for this woman, for example, he said that she has one thousand rupees due from me. Or he made a bequest of some wealth from his estate for this woman. (2) The woman asked her husband for three divorces during his death illness, he gave her three divorces. Then during the iddah, he confessed some debt for this woman or made a bequest of some wealth. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, in both cases, the ruling is that whichever is less from the amount of confessed wealth or bequest and from her share of inheritance, that will be given. If the confessed amount and bequest wealth is less, that will be given; if the share of inheritance is less, that will be given. And according to Imam Zufar, the woman will be given the amount that he confessed or bequeathed, whether that amount is less or more than the share of inheritance. And according to the Sahibayn, in the first case, the ruling is what Imam Zufar said, and in the second case, what Imam Abu Hanifa said. Imam Zufar's proof is that for this woman, for the validity of confession and bequest, being an heir was an obstacle. But in the first case, due to confirming the husband's statement, and in the second case, due to requesting divorce, her inheritance became void. Therefore, the obstacle to the validity of confession and bequest
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of a husband's confession of debt or bequest to his wife after a divorce that occurred during his death illness. Two scenarios are analyzed: (1) The husband claims he divorced her in health and her iddah expired; she confirms. Then he confesses a debt or makes a bequest to her. (2) The husband divorces her three times at her request during his death illness, then confesses or bequeaths. The disagreement among Hanafi imams centers on the presence of suspicion (tuhma) of collusion. Abu Hanifa holds that in both cases, the wife may be conspiring with the husband to increase her entitlement beyond her inheritance share, so she receives only the lesser of the confessed/bequeathed amount and her inheritance. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) differentiate: in the first scenario, since the iddah has expired, she becomes a stranger (ajnabiyyah), eliminating suspicion, so the confession/bequest is fully valid. In the second scenario, iddah remains, so suspicion exists, and they agree with Abu Hanifa. Zufar argues that in the second scenario, since the wife's request for divorce nullified her inheritance, the obstacle to valid confession/bequest is removed, so she receives the full amount. The text then provides the reasoning of each side. Abu Hanifa maintains that suspicion persists because the couple could agree on a false claim of prior divorce to enable greater bequest. The Sahibayn argue that when iddah is absent, the wife is a stranger, and thus no suspicion applies, as evidenced by the permissibility of marriage to her sister, acceptance of testimony, and giving zakat.

Key Terms
اقرار (iqrar): Confession or acknowledgment of a debt or right in favor of another person.
تہمت (tuhma): Suspicion of collusion or fraud, particularly in financial dealings between a sick person and an heir.
اجنبیہ (ajnabiyyah): A stranger, i.e., a woman who is not a mahram and with whom marriage is permissible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the second scenario (divorce at wife's request during death illness), which imam holds that the wife receives the full amount of the confession or bequest?
A) Abu Hanifa
B) Abu Yusuf and Muhammad
C) Zufar
D) All of them

Key Takeaway
The validity of a confession or bequest to a divorced wife during death illness depends on the presence of suspicion (tuhma), which is determined by whether the iddah has expired and whether collusion is plausible.

Talaq — Divorce
advanced
10 min
Dispute on Acknowledgment and Bequest by a Sick Man After Claimed Divorce
Intra-Hanafi dispute on acknowledgment/bequest validity during death illness after divorce.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and Zufar on the validity of a sick man's acknowledgment/bequest for his wife after divorce, and apply the concept of tuhmah to determine the operative ruling.

Core Idea
Tuhmah (suspicion of collusion) limits what a sick husband can give his divorced wife via acknowledgment or bequest.

This lesson explores a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute about whether a husband's debt acknowledgment or bequest made during his death illness for his wife is fully valid or limited when the wife either confirms a prior divorce or asks for divorce. The central legal concept is tuhmah (suspicion of collusion) and how it interacts with the wife's inheritance rights and iddah. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply principles of equity and evidentiary reasoning in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
First case: husband claims he divorced in health, wife confirms, then he makes an acknowledgment/bequest. Second case: wife asks for three divorces during husband's death illness, he gives them, then during iddah he makes an acknowledgment/bequest.
2
State each imam's ruling
Abu Hanifa: in both cases, wife gets the lesser of acknowledged/bequeathed amount and inheritance share. Sahibayn: in case one (iddah passed), wife gets full amount; in case two (iddah remains), wife gets lesser. Zufar: in both cases, wife gets full amount.
The Sahibayn's view is a middle position.
3
Analyze the reasoning: tuhmah and iddah
Abu Hanifa: tuhmah exists in both because the divorce agreement itself could be a ruse. Sahibayn: iddah is the evidence of tuhmah; if iddah has passed, no tuhmah. Zufar: once inheritance right is removed, no impediment remains.
Tuhmah is inferred from custom and possibility of collusion.
4
Identify the operative ruling (mufta bihi)
Later Hanafi authorities prefer the Sahibayn's view: in case one (iddah passed), wife receives full; in case two (iddah pending), wife receives the lesser.
Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah gives tarjih to Sahibayn.

زائل ہو گیا اور جب مانع زائل ہو گیا تو عورت کیلئے شوہر کا اقرار کرنا اور وصیت کرنا صحیح ہوا۔ اسلئے شوہر کے مرجانے کے بعد عورت مال کی اس مقدار کی مستحق ہوگی، جس کا اس کیلئے اقرار کیا گیا ہے یا وصیت کی ہے، خواہ یہ مقدار حصہ میراث سے کم ہو یا زائد۔ پہلے مسئلہ میں صاحبین کے قول کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب زوجین نے وقوع طلاق اور عدت کے گذر جانے پر اتفاق کر لیا، تو یہ عورت اس سے اجنبیہ ہو گئی ، وارث نہیں رہی۔ چنانچہ شوہر اگر اس کی بہن سے ابھی نکاح کرنا چاہے تو شرعاً درست ہے۔ پس احد الوزثہ کو آخر پر ترجیح دینے کی تہمت دور ہو گئی۔ چنانچہ آپ غور کریں کہ مرد کی گواہی اس عورت کے حق میں جائز ہے اور مرد کا اس عورت کو اپنے مال کی زکوۃ دینا بھی جائز ہے۔ پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ یہ عورت اس سے اجنبیہ ہو گئی ہے، لہذا اس مرد کا اقرار اور وصیت اس عورت کیلئے اسی طرح درست ہے۔ جس طرح دوسرے اجانب کیلئے بر خلاف دوسرے مسئلہ کے کیونکہ اس میں تہمت کا اثر ہے اور تہمت کا اثر اس وجہ سے ہے کہ ابھی عدت باقی ہے اور عدت ہی تہمت کا سبب ہے تفصیل یہ ہے کہ احد الورثہ کو آخر پر تر بی دینے کی تہت امر باطن ہے اور چونکہ امر باطن کی حقیقت مطلع ہونا ناممکن ہے۔ اسلئے حکم کا مدار امر باطن نہیں ہوتا، بلکہ اس کی دلیل ہوتی ہے اور یہاں تہمت کی دلیل اس کی عدت ہے۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ عدت کے موجود ہونے سے تہمت موجود ہے اور تہمت کی وجہ سے اقرار اور وصیت جائز نہیں ہے۔ لہذا عدت اگر موجود ہو تو اقرار اور وصیت جائز نہیں ہوں گے۔ اسی وجہ سے نکاح اور قرابت پر حکم کا مدار ہے۔ چنانچہ تہمت کی وجہ سے احد الزوجین کی شہادت آخر کے حق میں قبول نہیں کی جائے گی اور نہ قرابت اولاد میں سے ایک کی دوسرے کے حق میں اور پہلے مسئلہ میں انقضاء عدت پر زوجین سے اتفاق کر لینے کی وجہ سے عدت ہی باقی نہ رہی۔ لہذا دلیل تہمت بھی نہیں پائی گئی۔ اس وجہ سے ہم نے کہا کہ پہلے مسئلہ میں اس عورت کیلئے شوہر کا اقرار اور وصیت جائز ہے۔ دونوں مسئلوں میں امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ تہمت موجو! ۔۔ دوسرے مسئلہ میں بالاتفاق تہمت موجود ہے۔ اور اول میں اگر واقعی طلاق مان لی جائے تب بھی تہمت موجود ہے کیونکہ عورت کبھی اس غرض سے طلاق کو اختیار کر لیتی ہے تا کہ اقرار اور وصیت کا دروازہ اس پر کھل جائے۔ پھر اس کا حق اقرار یا وصیت کے ذریعہ میراث سے بڑھا دیا جائے ۔ خلاصہ یہ کہ شوہر نے اس کو اس وجہ سے طلاق نہیں دی کہ اس کو جدائی کی ضرورت تھی۔ بلکہ منشاء یہ ہے کہ عورت کو زیادہ مال مل جائے ، جو ترکہ سے نہیں ملتا تھا اور اس میں وارثوں کا نقصان اظہر من الشمس ہے پس یہی تہمت ہے اور یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ واقع میں طلاق ہی نہ ہو، بلکہ زوجین نے اس بات پر اتفاق کر لیا ہے کہ طلاق بھی واقع ہوگئی اور عدت بھی گزر گئی اور اس اتفاق سے مقصد یہ ہے کہ شوہر اپنی اس بیوی کو اس کے حصہ میراث سے زیادہ دے کر اس پر تبرع اور احسان کرنا چاہتا ہے۔ بایں طور کہ اس کیلئے قرضہ کا اقرار کرے یا وصیت کر دے۔ حاصل یہ کہ یہ تہمت صرف زیادتی میں ہے۔ لہذا ہم نے زیادتی کو رد کر دیا اور میراث کی مقدار میں کوئی تہمت نہیں اس وجہ سے ہم نے میراث کی مقدار کو سی رکھا اورحکم دیا کہ اقرار اور وصیت سے اور میراث کی مقدار سے جو کم ہو عورت کو وہ دلایا جائے۔ یعنی اگر میراث کی مقدار، اقرار اور وصیت سے کم ہے تو میراث کی مقدار دلائی جائے گی اور اگر مال مقر بہ اور وصیت کی مقدار کم ہے تو چونکہ وہ اپنے حق میں اس پر راضی ہو چکی اس واسطے اس کو یہی دلایا جائیگا۔ ولا مواضعة عادة سے صاحبین کا قول الا ترى انه تقبل شهادته لها كا جواب ہے ۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ میراث کے حق میں یہ اتفاق عادتا جاری ہے تو اس میں تہمت ہے مگر دوسرے احکام میں عادتا یہ اتفاق جاری نہیں ہے بلکہ ایک گونہ حماقت ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ کون سی دانشمندی ہے کہ بیوی کے موافق گواہی دینے کیلئے یا اس کی بہن سے شادی کرنے کیلئے باز کوۃ دینے کیلئے طلاق اور انقضاء عدت
Chapter: Divorce of the Sick Person. Ashraf al-Hidaya, Urdu commentary of Hidayah, volume five. Then if the woman confirmed his statement, then (the husband) made an acknowledgment of debt for that woman (against himself) or the husband made some bequest for her, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, for that woman, from that acknowledgment or bequest and from her share of inheritance, whichever is less will be given. And Imam Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said that the sick person's acknowledgment and bequest are valid. And if the husband in his death illness gave three divorces to the woman at her request, then made an acknowledgment of some debt for that woman or made some bequest for her, then by default (the ruling is) that for the woman, from that acknowledgment of debt or bequest and from the inheritance share, whichever is less will be given, except according to Imam Zufar, because (according to Imam Zufar) whatever bequest was made and whatever acknowledgment was made, she will receive the full amount, because when due to the woman's asking for divorce, her inheritance was invalidated, the impediment to the validity of acknowledgment and bequest was removed. In the first case, the reason for the Sahibayn's statement is that when the husband and wife agreed on the occurrence of divorce and the passing of the iddah, this woman became a stranger to him, so much so that it became permissible for the husband to marry her sister (immediately). Thus the suspicion (tuhmah) is eliminated. Do you not see that the man's testimony in favor of this woman would be accepted, and (the man) is permitted to give her his zakat from his wealth. Contrary to the second case, because the iddah remains and this was the cause of suspicion, and the ruling is based on the evidence of suspicion, and for this reason the ruling is based on marriage and kinship. And in the first case, the iddah did not remain. And Imam Abu Hanifa's proof in both cases is that suspicion exists, because the woman also chooses divorce with this motive, so that the door of acknowledgment and bequest opens for her, then her right increases. And sometimes the husband and wife both agree on the acknowledgment of separation and the passing of iddah, so that the husband may bestow upon her with his wealth exceeding her inheritance share, and this suspicion is only in the excess. For this reason we rejected the excess, and there is no suspicion in the amount of inheritance, so we kept the amount of inheritance correct. And customarily, agreement is not made for zakat, marriage, and testimony. So for these rulings, suspicion is not considered. Explanation: In this phrase, two cases are under discussion: (1) The husband said to his wife, 'I divorced you during health and your iddah has also completed.' The woman confirmed her husband, then after that the husband made an acknowledgment of some debt for this woman, for example he said, 'I owe her one thousand rupees.' Or he made a bequest of some property for this woman from his estate. (2) The woman asked her husband for three divorces during his death illness, he gave her three divorces. Then during the iddah he made an acknowledgment of some debt for this woman or made a bequest of some property. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, in both these cases the ruling is that whatever amount of property was acknowledged or bequeathed, and whatever her inheritance share is, whichever is less will be given. If the acknowledged amount and bequeathed amount is less, then that will be given; if the inheritance share is less, then that will be given. And according to Imam Zufar, the amount that was acknowledged or bequeathed will be given to the woman, whether this amount is less or more than the inheritance share. And according to the Sahibayn, in the first case the ruling is that which Imam Zufar stated, and in the second case that which Imam Abu Hanifa stated. Imam Zufar's proof is that for the validity of acknowledgment and bequest for this woman, her being an heir was an impediment. But in the first case, due to confirming the husband's statement, and in the second case, due to asking for divorce, her inheritance became invalid. Therefore the impediment to the validity of acknowledgment and bequest was removed, and when the impediment was removed, the husband's acknowledgment and bequest for the woman became valid. Hence after the husband's death, the woman will be entitled to the amount of property that was acknowledged or bequeathed for her, whether this amount is less or more than the inheritance share. In the first case, the proof for the Sahibayn's statement is that when the spouses agreed on the occurrence of divorce and the passing of iddah, this woman became a stranger to him, no longer an heir. Consequently, if the husband wants to marry her sister now, it is legally permissible. So the suspicion of giving preference to one heir over another was removed. Consider that the man's testimony in favor of this woman is permissible, and the man giving his zakat to this woman is also permissible. Thus it is established that this woman has become a stranger to him, therefore the man's acknowledgment and bequest for this woman are valid just as for other strangers, contrary to the second case because in it the effect of suspicion remains, and the effect of suspicion is because the iddah still remains, and the iddah itself is the cause of suspicion. The detail is that the suspicion of giving preference to one heir over another is an internal matter, and since it is impossible to know the reality of an internal matter, the ruling is not based on the internal matter itself but on its evidence. And here the evidence of suspicion is her iddah. Thus it is established that with the existence of iddah, suspicion exists, and due to suspicion, acknowledgment and bequest are not valid. Therefore if iddah exists, acknowledgment and bequest will not be valid. For this reason, rulings are based on marriage and kinship. Consequently, due to suspicion, the testimony of one spouse is not accepted in favor of the other, nor the testimony of one offspring in favor of another. And in the first case, due to the spouses agreeing on the completion of iddah, the iddah did not remain, therefore the evidence of suspicion was also not found. For this reason we said that in the first case, the husband's acknowledgment and bequest for this woman are valid. In both cases, Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that suspicion exists... In the second case, by consensus suspicion exists. And in the first, even if the divorce is accepted as real, still suspicion exists because sometimes the woman chooses divorce with this motive, so that the door of acknowledgment and bequest opens for her, then her right is increased through acknowledgment or bequest over inheritance. The summary is that the husband did not divorce her because he needed separation, but the intention is that the woman should get more wealth, which she could not get from the estate, and in this the loss to other heirs is clearer than the sun. So this is the suspicion. And there is also a possibility that in reality there was no divorce, but the spouses agreed that the divorce occurred and the iddah passed, and the purpose of this agreement is that the husband wants to bestow upon this woman more than her inheritance share, by making an acknowledgment of debt or bequest for her. The conclusion is that this suspicion is only in the excess. Therefore we rejected the excess, and there is no suspicion in the amount of inheritance, so we kept the amount of inheritance correct, and ruled that from the acknowledgment and bequest and from the inheritance amount, whichever is less will be given to the woman. That is, if the inheritance amount is less than the acknowledged and bequeathed amount, then the inheritance amount will be given; and if the acknowledged amount and bequeathed amount are less, then since she has agreed to that regarding her right, she will be given that. And the statement of the Sahibayn 'Do you not see that his testimony in her favor is accepted' is a response from custom. The gist of the response is that this agreement is customarily prevalent regarding inheritance, so there is suspicion in it, but in other rulings this agreement is not customarily prevalent, rather it is a kind of foolishness. Because what wisdom is there in divorcing and completing iddah for the sake of giving testimony in favor of the wife, or marrying her sister, or giving zakat...
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning rulings on a husband's debt acknowledgment or bequest made during his death illness for a wife who either confirms a prior divorce or asks for divorce. The commentary explains two distinct cases and the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), and Imam Zufar. The central legal concept is tuhmah (suspicion of collusion to deprive other heirs). In the first case, the husband claims he divorced his wife in health and she confirms, then makes an acknowledgment or bequest. In the second case, the wife asks for three divorces during the husband's death illness, he gives them, then during her iddah he makes an acknowledgment or bequest. Abu Hanifa holds that in both cases, the wife receives the lesser of the acknowledged/bequeathed amount and her inheritance share, because tuhmah exists: the agreement could be a ruse to give her more. The Sahibayn distinguish: in the first case, since the spouses agree that iddah has passed, the wife is a stranger (no inheritance right), so no tuhmah — the acknowledgment/bequest is fully valid (like Zufar). In the second case, iddah remains, tuhmah exists, so the ruling follows Abu Hanifa. Imam Zufar holds that in both cases, the acknowledgment/bequest is fully valid because the wife's inheritance right is eliminated (in the first by confirming the divorce, in the second by asking for it), so no impediment remains. The commentary then provides the reasoning of each imam, focusing on the role of iddah as the evidence of tuhmah and the fact that agreement on inheritance is customary but not for other matters like testimony or zakat.

Key Terms
تہمت (tuhmah): Suspicion or expectation of collusion between the husband and wife to deprive other heirs, inferred from circumstances such as acknowledgment or bequest during death illness.
صاحبین (Sahibayn): Refers to Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two principal students of Abu Hanifa.
عدت (iddah): The waiting period a divorced woman must observe before remarrying; its duration indicates whether the divorce is real or collusive.
اقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment of a debt or right, which in the context of a sick person is subject to scrutiny for suspicion of collusion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the second case (wife asks for three divorces during husband's death illness, then husband makes an acknowledgment during iddah), what is the ruling according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad)?
A) The wife receives the full acknowledged amount regardless of inheritance share.
B) The wife receives the lesser of the acknowledged amount and her inheritance share.
C) The acknowledgment is invalid and the wife receives nothing.
D) The wife receives one-third of the estate.

Key Takeaway
The Sahibayn's differentiated view—full validity when iddah has passed, limited when iddah remains—is the mufta bihi, balancing tuhmah and formal impediments.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
15 min
Tuhmah in Divorce: Iqrar and Wasiyyah for the Wife
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tuhmah in iqrar/wasiyyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding tuhmah in iqrar/wasiyyah after divorce, and apply the ruling to a scenario involving marad al-mawt.

Core Idea
Tuhmah (suspicion) can invalidate a husband's favor to his divorced wife when it exceeds her inheritance share.

This passage delves into a classic intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). The issue arises when a husband divorces his wife during a fatal illness (marad al-mawt) and then makes an acknowledgment (iqrar) or bequest (wasiyyah) in her favor. The central question is whether the suspicion of collusion (tuhmah) to deprive other heirs renders such acts invalid. By working through this dispute, you will sharpen your ability to analyze legal reasoning based on underlying motives and evidentiary customs.

Guided Path
1
State the Issue and the Two Positions
Identify the factual scenario: a husband in marad al-mawt divorces his wife, and after the divorce (with or without 'iddah ending), he makes an iqrar or wasiyyah in her favor that exceeds her inheritance share. The two positions are: (1) Abu Hanifa holds tuhmah remains, so the excess is invalid; (2) Sahibayn hold tuhmah is removed if 'iddah has ended, so the act is fully valid.
The dispute hinges on whether the divorce is a genuine separation or a ruse to favor the wife.
2
Identify Abu Hanifa's Position and His Dalil
Abu Hanifa argues that tuhmah exists in both cases (whether 'iddah ended or not) because the wife may have consented to the divorce specifically to enable the husband to give her more than her inheritance. The continued existence of tuhmah is evidenced by the fact that the couple's agreement on the divorce and 'iddah is itself suspicious; it could be fabricated. Therefore, any iqrar or wasiyyah exceeding the inheritance share is invalid, and the woman receives the lesser of the two amounts.
Abu Hanifa's reasoning relies on the prevalence of such collusion in practice.
3
Identify the Sahibayn's Position and Their Dalil
The Sahibayn argue that if the 'iddah has ended and both spouses agree on the divorce and the passage of 'iddah, then the woman becomes a stranger to the husband (not an heir). Therefore, the suspicion of preferring one heir over another disappears. She is like any other non-heir, so the iqrar or wasiyyah should be fully valid, without any cap. They support this by noting that the husband can testify for her, give her zakat, and even marry her sister—all actions that would be forbidden if tuhmah remained.
Sahibayn emphasize the objective removal of the impediment (the 'iddah ending).
4
Analyze the Hanafi Response and Thamarah al-Khilaf
The text presents a rebuttal to Sahibayn's argument: the agreement on divorce and 'iddah is not customary in matters like testimony or marriage; it would be foolish to go to such lengths for those purposes. Hence, in those matters the agreement is taken as genuine, and no tuhmah applies. But in the context of iqrar/wasiyyah, such collusion is common, so tuhmah persists. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is clear: under Abu Hanifa, the woman gets the lesser of the acknowledged amount or inheritance share; under Sahibayn, she gets the full acknowledged amount or bequest.
This shows how the same external evidence (agreement) is evaluated differently based on customary practice (urf).
5
Apply the Ruling to a New Scenario
Take a scenario: A terminally ill husband divorces his wife, and after the 'iddah ends, he acknowledges a debt of $100,000 to her. Her inheritance share would be $50,000. According to Abu Hanifa, she gets only $50,000 because the excess is void due to tuhmah. According to Sahibayn, she gets the full $100,000. In a fatwa, the mufti may lean towards one view depending on strength of evidence and local custom.
This illustrates the real-world impact of the dispute.

باب طلاق المريض
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو بدایہ جلد پنجم زائل ہو گیا اور جب مانع زائل ہو گیا تو عورت کیلئے شوہر کا اقرار کرنا اور وصیت کرنا صحیح ہوا۔ اسلئے شوہر کے مرجانے کے بعد عورت مال کی اس مقدار کی مستحق ہوگی، جس کا اس کیلئے اقرار کیا گیا ہے یا وصیت کی ہے، خواہ یہ مقدار حصہ میراث سے کم ہو یا زائد۔ پہلے مسئلہ میں صاحبین کے قول کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب زوجین نے وقوع طلاق اور عدت کے گذر جانے پر اتفاق کر لیا، تو یہ عورت اس سے اجنبیہ ہو گئی ، وارث نہیں رہی۔ چنانچہ شوہر اگر اس کی بہن سے ابھی نکاح کرنا چاہے تو شرعاً درست ہے۔ پس احد الوزثہ کو آخر پر ترجیح دینے کی تہمت دور ہو گئی۔ چنانچہ آپ غور کریں کہ مرد کی گواہی اس عورت کے حق میں جائز ہے اور مرد کا اس عورت کو اپنے مال کی زکوۃ دینا بھی جائز ہے۔ پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ یہ عورت اس سے اجنبیہ ہو گئی ہے، لہذا اس مرد کا اقرار اور وصیت اس عورت کیلئے اسی طرح درست ہے۔ جس طرح دوسرے اجانب کیلئے بر خلاف دوسرے مسئلہ کے کیونکہ اس میں تہمت کا اثر ہے اور تہمت کا اثر اس وجہ سے ہے کہ ابھی عدت باقی ہے اور عدت ہی تہمت کا سبب ہے تفصیل یہ ہے کہ احد الورثہ کو آخر پر تر بی دینے کی تہت امر باطن ہے اور چونکہ امر باطن کی حقیقت مطلع ہونا ناممکن ہے۔ اسلئے حکم کا مدار امر باطن نہیں ہوتا، بلکہ اس کی دلیل ہوتی ہے اور یہاں تہمت کی دلیل اس کی عدت ہے۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ عدت کے موجود ہونے سے تہمت موجود ہے اور تہمت کی وجہ سے اقرار اور وصیت جائز نہیں ہے۔ لہذا عدت اگر موجود ہو تو اقرار اور وصیت جائز نہیں ہوں گے۔
اسی وجہ سے نکاح اور قرابت پر حکم کا مدار ہے۔ چنانچہ تہمت کی وجہ سے احد الزوجین کی شہادت آخر کے حق میں قبول نہیں کی جائے گی اور نہ قرابت اولاد میں سے ایک کی دوسرے کے حق میں اور پہلے مسئلہ میں انقضاء عدت پر زوجین سے اتفاق کر لینے کی وجہ سے عدت ہی باقی نہ رہی۔ لہذا دلیل تہمت بھی نہیں پائی گئی۔ اس وجہ سے ہم نے کہا کہ پہلے مسئلہ میں اس عورت کیلئے شوہر کا اقرار اور وصیت جائز ہے۔ دونوں مسئلوں میں امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ تہمت موجو! ۔۔ دوسرے مسئلہ میں بالاتفاق تہمت موجود ہے۔ اور اول میں اگر واقعی طلاق مان لی جائے تب بھی تہمت موجود ہے کیونکہ عورت کبھی اس غرض سے طلاق کو اختیار کر لیتی ہے تا کہ اقرار اور وصیت کا دروازہ اس پر کھل جائے۔ پھر اس کا حق اقرار یا وصیت کے ذریعہ میراث سے بڑھا دیا جائے ۔ خلاصہ یہ کہ شوہر نے اس کو اس وجہ سے طلاق نہیں دی کہ اس کو جدائی کی ضرورت تھی۔ بلکہ منشاء یہ ہے کہ عورت کو زیادہ مال مل جائے ، جو ترکہ سے نہیں ملتا تھا اور اس میں وارثوں کا نقصان اظہر من الشمس ہے پس یہی تہمت ہے اور یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ واقع میں طلاق ہی نہ ہو، بلکہ زوجین نے اس بات پر اتفاق کر لیا ہے کہ طلاق بھی واقع ہوگئی اور عدت بھی گزر گئی اور اس اتفاق سے مقصد یہ ہے کہ شوہر اپنی اس بیوی کو اس کے حصہ میراث سے زیادہ دے کر اس پر تبرع اور احسان کرنا چاہتا ہے۔ بایں طور کہ اس کیلئے قرضہ کا اقرار کرے یا وصیت کر دے۔ حاصل یہ کہ یہ تہمت صرف زیادتی میں ہے۔ لہذا ہم نے زیادتی کو رد کر دیا اور میراث کی مقدار میں کوئی تہمت نہیں اس وجہ سے ہم نے میراث کی مقدار کو سی رکھا اورحکم دیا کہ اقرار اور وصیت سے اور میراث کی مقدار سے جو کم ہو عورت کو وہ دلایا جائے۔ یعنی اگر میراث کی مقدار، اقرار اور وصیت سے کم ہے تو میراث کی مقدار دلائی جائے گی اور اگر مال مقر بہ اور وصیت کی مقدار کم ہے تو چونکہ وہ اپنے حق میں اس پر راضی ہو چکی اس واسطے اس کو یہی دلایا جائیگا۔ ولا مواضعة عادة سے صاحبین کا قول الا ترى انه تقبل شهادته لها كا جواب ہے ۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ میراث کے حق میں یہ اتفاق عادتا جاری ہے تو اس میں تہمت ہے مگر دوسرے احکام میں عادتا یہ اتفاق جاری نہیں ہے بلکہ ایک گونہ حماقت ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ کون سی دانشمندی ہے کہ بیوی کے موافق گواہی دینے کیلئے یا اس کی بہن سے شادی کرنے کیلئے باز کوۃ دینے کیلئے طلاق اور انقضاء عدت پر اتفاق کر لیں پس ان احکام کے حق میں یہی سمجھا جائے گا کہ طلاق اور انقضاء عدت کا اقرار واقعی ہے۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ ان احکام میں کوئی تہمت نہیں ہے۔ واللہ اعلم
Chapter of Divorce of the Sick Person. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu Commentary on al-Hidayah Volume Five. ... and when the impediment is removed, the husband's acknowledgment and bequest for the woman became valid. ... After the husband's death, the woman is entitled to the amount acknowledged or bequeathed, whether less or more than her inheritance share. In the first issue, the proof of the Sahibayn's opinion is that when the spouses agree on the occurrence of divorce and the passing of the 'iddah, then this woman becomes a stranger to him, not an heir. ... So the suspicion of preference for one of the heirs is removed. ... In the second issue, the effect of suspicion remains because the 'iddah still exists and 'iddah is the cause of suspicion. ... The proof of Imam Abu Hanifah in both issues is that suspicion exists ... In the second issue, suspicion exists by consensus. And in the first, even if the divorce is accepted as real, suspicion still exists because the woman may take the divorce with the motive that the door of acknowledgment and bequest opens for her. ... So we rejected the excess and kept the inheritance share; we ruled that the woman is given whichever is less: the acknowledged amount or the inheritance share. ... The Sahibayn's response ... They say that this agreement is not customary in other rulings; it is foolishness to agree on divorce and passing of 'iddah for testimony or marriage to her sister. So in those rulings, the agreement is considered real and no suspicion. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two disciples (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the validity of a husband's acknowledgment (iqrar) and bequest (wasiyyah) for his divorced wife when he is in marad al-mawt (fatal illness). The issue is whether the tuhmah (suspicion of collusion to deprive other heirs) prevents such iqrar/wasiyyah. The Sahibayn argue that if the 'iddah has ended and both agree, the woman is a stranger, so no tuhmah, hence iqrar/wasiyyah valid. Abu Hanifa argues that tuhmah persists because the divorce may be a pretext to give her more than her inheritance. The text then presents a compromise: the woman receives the lesser of the acknowledged amount or her inheritance share. The Sahibayn respond that such collusion is not customary in other matters like testimony or remarriage, so those are not affected. The passage thus illustrates the clash between Zähir (external evidence) and istihsān (juristic preference) in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
تہمت (tuhmah): Suspicion of collusion or bias that may affect the validity of a legal act like iqrar or testimony.
اقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment of a right or debt, here by the husband in favor of the wife.
وصیت (wasiyyah): Bequest made during illness to a person who is not an heir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why does tuhmah remain even if the couple agrees that 'iddah has ended?
A) Because the divorce might be a pretext to give her more than her inheritance share.
B) Because the wife is still an heir by law.
C) Because the couple's agreement is always invalid in such cases.
D) Because the 'iddah never truly ends.

Key Takeaway
In an intra-Hanafi dispute, Abu Hanifa holds that tuhmah (suspicion of collusion) persists after divorce during fatal illness and invalidates iqrar/wasiyyah exceeding the wife's inheritance share, while the Sahibayn hold that if 'iddah ends, the wife is a stranger and the iqrar/wasiyyah is fully valid.
