Firar in Marad al-Mawt: Conditions for Inheritance After Divorce in Life-Threatening Scenarios
Defines conditions for firar in various life-threatening situations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on firar for a husband besieged in a fort versus one who duels or faces execution, and apply the principle of predominance of safety or death to determine inheritance.

Core Idea
Firar is established only when death predominates; safety predominates in a fort, so the wife does not inherit.

In this lesson, we examine the classical Hanafi ruling on firar (escape from inheritance) when a husband divorces his wife during a life-threatening situation and later dies. The Hidayah passage presents three scenarios: besieged in a fort, in the battle line, and dueling or facing execution. The ruling differs based on whether safety or death is predominant. We will trace the legal reasoning (istihsan and qiyas) that underlies this distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is divorcing the wife during a life-threatening situation. The ruling varies: wife does not inherit if husband is besieged or in battle line; she does inherit if he duels or is brought for execution.
Note the two distinct outcomes based on context.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is istihsan, which compares these situations to marad al-mawt (fatal illness) via qiyas. The underlying rationale is the attachment of the wife's right to the husband's property when death is probable.
The dalil is not an explicit text but a rational extension.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The key effective cause (illa) is the predominance of death (ghalabah al-halak) versus safety (ghalabah al-salamah). In a fort or army, safety is predominant; in a duel or execution, death is predominant.
This distinction is critical for applying the rule to new cases.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools may have different rules for firar; Hanafis use istihsan. The ruling as stated is mufta bihi within the Hanafi school.
Cross-madhhab ikhtilaf exists, but this passage presents the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وہ شخص جو قلعہ میں محصور ہو یا صف قتال میں ہو اور عورت کو تین طلاقیں دیں عورت وارث نہیں ہوگی اور اگر وہ شخص کسی مرد سے مقابلہ کیلئے نکلا یا پیش کیا تا کہ قصاص یار جسم میں قتل کیا جائے پس وہ اسی وجہ سے مرایا قتل کیا گیا تو عورت وارث ہوگی
قال ومن كان محصورا اوفى صف القتال فطلق امرأته ثلثالم ترثه و ان كان قد بارز رجلا او قدم ليقتل في قصاص اور جم ورثت ان مات فى ذالك الوجه اوقتل واصله مابينا ان امرأة الفارترث استحسانا وانما يثبت حكم الفرار بتعلق حقها بماله وانما يتعلق بمرض يخاف منه الهلاك غالبا كما اذا كان صاحب الفراش وهو ان يكون بحال لا يقوم بحوائجه كما يعتاده الاصحاء وقديثبت حكم الفرار بما هو في معنى المرض في توجه الهلاك الغالب ومايكون الغالب منه السلامة لايثبت به حكم الفرار فالمحصور والذي في صف القتال الغالب منه السلامة لان الحصن لدفع باس العدو وكذا المنعة فلايثبت به حكم الفرار والذى بارز اوقدم ليقتل الغالب منه الهلاك فتحقق به الفرار ولهذا اخوات تخرج على هذا الحرف وقوله اذامات في ذالك الوجه اوقتل دليل على انه لا فرق بين ما اذامات بذلك السبب او بسبب اخر كصاحب الفراش بسبب المرض اذاقتل
ترجمہ اور جو شخص ( قلعہ ) میں محصور ہو یا وہ لڑائی کی صف میں ہو۔ پس اس نے اپنی بیوی کو تین طلاقیں دیدیں۔ ( پھر مرد مارا گیا) تو عورت اس کی وارث نہ ہوگی اور اگر وہ شخص کسی مرد سے مقابلہ کیلئے نکلا ، یا پیش کیا گیا تا کہ قصاص یا رحم میں قتل کیا جائے ۔ پس اگر وہ اس وجہ سے مرا یا قتل کیا گیا تو عورت وارث ہوگی اور اس کی اصل وہ ہے جو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں کہ ( طلاق دے کر میراث سے ) بھاگنے والے کی بیوی وارث ہوگی استحسانا اور بھگوڑے ہونے کا حکم اس وقت ثابت ہوگا ( جبکہ ) عورت کا حق اس کے مال کے ساتھ متعلق ہو جائے اور ( عورت کا حق شوہر کے مال کے ساتھ ) ایسے مرض سے متعلق ہوگا جس سے ہلاکت کا خوف غالب ہو جیسا کہ جب وہ صاحب فراش ہو۔ (اور جس مرض سے ہلاکت کا خوف غالب ہو ) ۔ وہ مریض ہے جو ایسی حالت میں ہو کہ تندرستوں کی طرح عادتاً اپنی ضروریات پوری نہیں کر سکتا اور کبھی فرار کا حکم ثابت ہو جاتا ہے۔ اس چیز سے جو غالب ہلاکت میں مرض الموت کے معنی میں ہو اور وہ امر جس سے سلامتی غالب ہے، اس سے فرار کا حکم ثابت نہیں ہوگا۔ پس جو شخص ( قلعہ ) میں محصور ہو اور لڑائی کی صف میں ہو اس سے سلامتی غالب ہے۔ کیونکہ قلعہ تو دشمن کا ضرر دور کرنے کیلئے ہوتا ہے اور ایسے ہی لشکر ۔ پس اس سے فرار کا حکم ثابت نہیں ہوگا اور جوشخص مقابلہ کیلئے نکلا یا آگے بڑھایا گیا تا کر قتل کیا جائے تو اس سے ہلاکت غالب ہے۔ لہذا اس سے فرار ( کا حکم ) متحقق ہوگا اور اس مسئلہ کے اور بھی نظائر ہیں جو اسی اصل پر نکالے جائیں گے اور امام محمد کا قول اذا مات فی ذالک الوجه او قتل اس بات پر دلیل ہے کہ کوئی فرق نہیں کہ اس سبب سے مرے یا دوسرے سبب سے مرے۔ جیسا کہ مرض کی وجہ سے صاحب فراش جب قتل کر دیا گیا۔
And the person who is besieged in a fort or is in the battle line and gives his wife three divorces, the wife will not inherit. And if the person emerged for a duel against a man or was brought to be executed in qisas or rujm (stoning), then if he dies or is killed due to that, the wife will inherit. He said: And the one who is besieged or in the battle line and divorces his wife thrice, she does not inherit. And if he fought a duel or was brought to be killed in qisas or stoning, then she inherits if he dies in that manner or is killed. The principle is what we explained: the wife of the 'far' (one who flees from inheritance) inherits by istihsan. The ruling of firar is established by the attachment of her right to his property, and that attachment occurs by a disease from which destruction is generally feared, as when he is bedridden (sahib al-firash). And the ruling of firar is established by that which is analogous to such disease in facing general destruction. And that from which safety is predominant, the ruling of firar is not established. So the besieged and the one in the battle line have safety predominant because the fort repels the enemy's harm, similarly the army. So firar is not established. And the one who dueled or was brought to be killed has destruction predominant, so firar is established. And this has other examples derived from this principle. And Imam Muhammad's saying 'when he dies in that manner or is killed' is evidence that there is no difference between dying from that cause or another cause, like the bedridden who is killed while ill.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the application of 'firar' (escape from inheritance) in various situations. The text first states the ruling: if a husband is besieged in a fort or in the battle line and divorces his wife three times, she does not inherit from him even if he dies. But if he emerges for a duel or is brought for execution (qisas or stoning), then she does inherit if he dies from that cause. The proof is based on istihsan, comparing these situations to marad al-mawt (fatal illness). The key principle is that firar is established only when death is generally feared (ghalabah al-halak). In a fort or army, safety is predominant (ghalabah al-salamah) because the fort protects. In a duel or execution, death is predominant. Imam Muhammad adds that it does not matter whether he dies directly from that cause or another; the ruling applies as long as the situation was one of probable death. This shows that the Hanafi school uses rational analogy (qiyas) based on the underlying cause of probable death.

Key Terms
فرار (firar): Escape from inheritance by divorcing the wife during fatal illness to deprive her of inheritance.
محصور (mahsūr): One who is besieged in a fort or similar, with safety likely.
صف القتال (saff al-qitāl): The battle line; a soldier in army formation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the wife of a besieged soldier not inherit if he divorces her and dies?
A) Because the divorce was valid and final.
B) Because safety is predominant in a fort.
C) Because the soldier intended to harm her.
D) Because the marriage was invalid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, firar is established only when death is the predominant outcome at the time of divorce, not when safety is likely.

Firar and Inheritance: Fortress vs. Battlefield
Explains the ruling on inheritance after divorce in cases of siege and battlefield with istihsan reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between situations where firar applies and where it does not, and state the Hanafi ruling on the wife's inheritance in each case.

Core Idea
The wife inherits only when death is predominant—not when safety is predominant, even if divorce occurs.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a nuanced scenario: a husband divorces his wife while in a life-threatening situation but then dies. The ruling depends on whether the circumstances make death likely or safety likely. The Hanafi school applies istihsan (equity) to protect the wife's inheritance when the husband's divorce appears to be a ploy to disinherit her, but only when death is the predominant expectation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage distinguishes between a person besieged in a fortress or in the battle line (safety predominant) and a person who steps out for single combat or is presented for execution (death predominant).
The key is the predominant outcome (ghalabat al-halakat vs. ghalabat al-salamah).
2
Apply the principle of firar
Firar is the husband's act of divorcing his wife to deprive her of inheritance when he is in a situation where death is likely. By istihsan, the wife inherits despite the divorce, overriding qiyas.
The basis (asl) is the established ruling that the wife of a fugitive inherits.
3
Define 'predominant fear of death'
The ruling attaches when the wife's right to inheritance is linked to the husband's wealth due to a condition from which destruction is predominantly feared (e.g., bedridden illness, sea storm).
This is broader than just fatal illness; any situation with predominant risk of death qualifies.
4
Analyze the fortress and battle line scenarios
In a fortress or battle line, safety is predominant because the fortress protects and the army provides mutual defense. Hence, firar is not established, and the wife does not inherit.
The ruling holds even if the husband dies later from unrelated causes.
5
Analyze the single combat and execution scenarios
When a person steps out to face an opponent or is led to execution, death is predominant. Firar is established, and the wife inherits if he dies from any cause during that situation.
Imam Muhammad confirms that the cause of death is irrelevant; only the predominant risk at the time of divorce matters.

ترجمہ اور جو شخص ( قلعہ ) میں محصور ہو یا وہ لڑائی کی صف میں ہو۔ پس اس نے اپنی بیوی کو تین طلاقیں دیدیں۔ ( پھر مرد مارا گیا) تو عورت اس کی وارث نہ ہوگی اور اگر وہ شخص کسی مرد سے مقابلہ کیلئے نکلا ، یا پیش کیا گیا تا کہ قصاص یا رحم میں قتل کیا جائے ۔ پس اگر وہ اس وجہ سے مرا یا قتل کیا گیا تو عورت وارث ہوگی اور اس کی اصل وہ ہے جو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں کہ ( طلاق دے کر میراث سے ) بھاگنے والے کی بیوی وارث ہوگی استحسانا اور بھگوڑے ہونے کا حکم اس وقت ثابت ہوگا ( جبکہ ) عورت کا حق اس کے مال کے ساتھ متعلق ہو جائے اور ( عورت کا حق شوہر کے مال کے ساتھ ) ایسے مرض سے متعلق ہوگا جس سے ہلاکت کا خوف غالب ہو جیسا کہ جب وہ صاحب فراش ہو۔ (اور جس مرض سے ہلاکت کا خوف غالب ہو ) ۔ وہ مریض ہے جو ایسی حالت میں ہو کہ تندرستوں کی طرح عادتاً اپنی ضروریات پوری نہیں کر سکتا اور کبھی فرار کا حکم ثابت ہو جاتا ہے۔ اس چیز سے جو غالب ہلاکت میں مرض الموت کے معنی میں ہو اور وہ امر جس سے سلامتی غالب ہے، اس سے فرار کا حکم ثابت نہیں ہوگا۔ پس جو شخص ( قلعہ ) میں محصور ہو اور لڑائی کی صف میں ہو اس سے سلامتی غالب ہے۔ کیونکہ قلعہ تو دشمن کا ضرر دور کرنے کیلئے ہوتا ہے اور ایسے ہی لشکر ۔ پس اس سے فرار کا حکم ثابت نہیں ہوگا اور جوشخص مقابلہ کیلئے نکلا یا آگے بڑھایا گیا تا کر قتل کیا جائے تو اس سے ہلاکت غالب ہے۔ لہذا اس سے فرار ( کا حکم ) متحقق ہوگا اور اس مسئلہ کے اور بھی نظائر ہیں جو اسی اصل پر نکالے جائیں گے اور امام محمد کا قول اذا مات فی ذالک الوجه او قتل اس بات پر دلیل ہے کہ کوئی فرق نہیں کہ اس سبب سے مرے یا دوسرے سبب سے مرے۔ جیسا کہ مرض کی وجہ سے صاحب فراش جب قتل کر دیا گیا۔

اس مسئلہ کی اصل ہم سابق میں بیان کر چکے کہ امراة فاراستحسانا وارث ہوگی نہ کہ قیا سا۔ وجہ استحسان اول باب میں بالتفصیل گذر چکی اور قیاس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ وراثت کا سبب موت کی وجہ سے نکاح کا ختم ہونا ہے اور چونکہ یہ شخص تین طلاقوں کے ذریعہ موت سے پہلے ہی نکاح کوختم کر چکا اسلئے وراثت کا سبب نہیں پایا گیا اور حکم بغیر سبب کے ثابت نہیں ہوتا۔ اس وجہ سے یہ عورت اپنے اس شوہر کی وارث نہیں ہوگی ۔
رہی یہ بات کہ فرار کا حکم کب ثابت ہوگا۔ سو اس بارے میں صاحب ہدایہ کی رائے یہ ہے کہ جس وقت عورت کا حق شوہر کے مال کے ساتھ متعلق ہو جائے تو فرار کا حکم ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ یعنی اس وقت اگر شوہر نے اپنی بیوی کو طلاق بائن دی تو یہ طلاق فار ہو گی اور عورت کا حق شوہر کے مال کے ساتھ اس وقت متعلق ہوتا ہے، جبکہ شوہر کسی ایسے مرض میں مبتلا ہو جائے کہ اس سے ہلاکت کا اندیشہ غالب ہو۔ مثلاً شوہر صاحب فراش ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے صاحب فراش کی تعریف کرتے ہوئے فرمایا ہے کہ وہ مریض تندرستوں کی طرح اپنی ضروریات پورا کرنے پر قادر ہو۔ مثلاً نماز کیلئے مسجد نہیں جا سکتا اور قضائے حاجت کیلئے جانے پر قدرت نہیں ۔ شمس الائمہ سرسی سے منقول ہے کہ فقیہ صاحب فراش اس وقت کہلائے گا جبکہ وہ مسجد جانے پر قادر نہ ہو اور بازاری جبکہ وہ دکان جانے پر قادر نہ ہو اور عورت جبکہ وہ چھت پر چڑھنے کی قدرت نہ رکھتی ہو۔
اور اگر مریض اندرون خانہ ضروریات کو پورا کر سکتا ہے۔ مثلا بیت الخلا جانا اور بیرون خانہ ضروریات پوری نہیں کر سکتا تو عام مشائخ بخارا کے نزدیک وہ مرض موت کے حکم میں ہے اور عام مشائخ بلخ کے نزدیک وہ تندرست کے حکم میں ہے۔ اور مشائخ متاخرین فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر بغیر دوسرے کی مدد کے تین قدم چلنے پر قادر ہے تو وہ تندرست کہلائے گا مگر یہ قول ضعیف ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ فرار کا حکم مرض میں منحصر نہیں بلکہ ہر وہ چیز جس سے ہلاکت کا خوف غالب ہو ۔ وہ مرض موت کے حکم میں اور اس سے فرار کا حکم ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ مثلا کشتی میں بحری سفر پر ہے اور پانی میں اس قدر طغیانی پیدا ہوگئی کہ ڈوبنے کا اندیشہ غالب

The chapter of the divorce of the sick person. They agree, so regarding these rulings, it will be considered that the admission of divorce and completion of 'iddah is real. So it is established that there is no accusation in these rulings. And Allah knows best. A person who is besieged in a fortress or in the battle line, and gave his wife three divorces, the wife will not inherit. But if that person came out to confront a man or was presented to be killed in retaliation or stoning, then if he died or was killed in that manner, the wife will inherit. He said: And whoever is besieged or in the battle line and divorces his wife three times, she does not inherit from him. And if he had faced a man or was presented to be killed in retaliation or stoning, she inherits if he dies in that manner or is killed. Its basis is what we explained that the wife of the fugitive inherits by istihsan. And the ruling of firar is only established by the attachment of her right to his wealth. And it only attaches by a disease from which destruction is feared predominantly, as when he is bedridden (sahib al-firash), which is that he is in a state where he cannot fulfill his needs as healthy people usually do. And the ruling of firar may be established by something that is in the meaning of disease in terms of predominant destruction. And that which is predominantly safe, the ruling of firar is not established by it. So the besieged and the one in the battle line, the predominant is safety because the fortress is to repel the enemy's harm, and similarly the army, so the ruling of firar is not established by it. And the one who came out to face or was presented to be killed, the predominant is destruction, so firar is realized by it. For this reason, its counterparts are derived on this principle. And his statement, 'If he dies in that manner or is killed,' is evidence that there is no difference between whether he dies by that cause or by another cause, like the bedridden one due to disease if he is killed. Translation: And the person who is besieged in a fortress or is in the battle line, then he gave his wife three divorces (then the man was killed), so the wife will not inherit from him. And if that person came out to confront a man, or was presented to be killed in retaliation or the body, then if he died or was killed due to that cause, the wife will inherit. And its basis is what we have explained that the wife of the one who flees (from inheritance) inherits by istihsan. And the ruling of being a fugitive is established when the wife's right is attached to his wealth. And (the wife's right to the husband's wealth) is attached by such a disease from which the fear of destruction is predominant, like when he is bedridden. (And the disease from which destruction is feared predominantly) is the patient who is in a state where he cannot fulfill his needs habitually like healthy people. And sometimes the ruling of firar is established by something that is in the meaning of deathly illness in terms of predominant destruction. And that matter from which safety is predominant, the ruling of firar is not established by it. So the person who is besieged in a fortress and in the battle line, from him safety is predominant, because the fortress is to repel the enemy's harm, and similarly the army. So the ruling of firar is not established by him. And the person who came out for confrontation or was brought forward to be killed, from him destruction is predominant, therefore firar is realized from him. And there are other similar cases to this issue that will be derived on this same principle. And Imam Muhammad's statement, 'If he dies in that manner or is killed,' is evidence that there is no difference whether he dies from this cause or from another cause, like the bedridden one due to disease if he is killed. Explanation: The case is that if a person is besieged in a fortress and the enemies have surrounded the fortress, or he is in the battle line. In such a state, that person gave his wife three divorces. Then that person died, so this wife will not inherit. And if a person came out of the battle line to confront the enemy for fighting, or was brought forward to be killed due to retaliation or stoning, then if he died from that cause or was killed by another cause, his wife will inherit. The basis of this issue we have explained earlier: the wife of the fugitive inherits by istihsan, not by qiyas. The reason for istihsan has passed in detail in the first chapter. And the reason for qiyas is that the cause of inheritance is the termination of marriage due to death, and since this person had already terminated the marriage through three divorces before death, the cause of inheritance is not found, and a ruling is not established without a cause. For this reason, this woman will not inherit from her husband. As for when the ruling of firar is established, the author of Hidayah's opinion is that when the wife's right is attached to the husband's wealth, then the ruling of firar is established. That is, if the husband gave his wife a bain divorce at that time, this divorce is firar. And the wife's right is attached to the husband's wealth when the husband is afflicted with such a disease that the fear of destruction from it is predominant, for example, the husband is bedridden. The author of Hidayah defined bedridden as: the patient is unable to fulfill his needs like healthy people, for example, cannot go to the mosque for prayer and cannot go to relieve himself. It is narrated from Shams al-Aimma al-Sarakhsi that a jurist is called bedridden when he cannot go to the mosque, a merchant when he cannot go to the shop, and a woman when she cannot climb the roof. And if the patient can fulfill indoor needs, e.g., go to the toilet, but cannot fulfill outdoor needs, then according to the general mashayikh of Bukhara, it is considered deathly illness, and according to the general mashayikh of Balkh, it is considered healthy. And the later mashayikh say that if he can walk three steps without assistance, he is considered healthy, but this saying is weak. The author of Hidayah says that the ruling of firar is not confined to illness; rather, everything from which the fear of destruction is predominant, it is in the ruling of deathly illness and the ruling of firar is established from it. For example, he is on a sea voyage in a ship and the water surges so much that the fear of drowning becomes predominant. In such a state, if he gives his wife a bain divorce, the ruling of firar is established. And if it is a condition upon which safety is predominant, then the ruling of firar is not established. So since the person who is besieged in a fortress and who is in the battle line, from him safety is predominant, therefore the ruling of firar is not established. The evidence for safety being predominant is that the fortress is to repel the enemy's harm, and the same ruling applies to the army. And the person who came out of the line for confrontation or was presented for execution, from him destruction is predominant, therefore the ruling of firar is established.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage from Bab Talaq al-Mareed of Al-Hidayah discusses the inheritance rights of a wife whose husband divorced her while in a life-threatening situation, differentiating between cases where safety is predominant and where death is predominant. The chapter begins with an earlier discussion about the validity of admitting divorce and completion of 'iddah, establishing that such admissions are real and not tainted by accusation. The core ruling is stated in the matn: If a man is besieged in a fortress or is in the battle line and gives his wife three divorces, she does not inherit from him. However, if he came out to face an opponent or was presented for execution (retaliation or stoning), she does inherit if he dies or is killed in that situation. The commentary explains that the basis (asl) for this ruling is the principle of firar (fleeing from inheritance). By istihsan (equity), the wife of a fugitive inherits, contrary to qiyas (analogy), which would deny inheritance because the marriage ended before death. The reason for istihsan is that the husband's action (divorce) is seen as a ploy to deprive the wife of her inheritance when he is in a situation where death is likely. The ruling of firar attaches when the wife's right to inheritance becomes linked to the husband's wealth, which occurs when the husband is in a condition from which death is predominantly feared—such as a fatal illness (marad al-mawt) or any circumstance with predominant risk of death. The definition of 'sahib al-firash' (bedridden) is given: someone who cannot perform basic needs independently, like going to the mosque or toilet. The text then applies this principle: In a fortress or battle line, safety is predominant because the fortress protects from the enemy, so no firar; but when one steps out for single combat or is presented for execution, death is predominant, so firar applies, and the wife inherits. Imam Muhammad's statement confirms that it does not matter if death occurs from that specific cause or another—like a bedridden patient who is killed. The Urdu commentary elaborates further, noting that the definition of marad al-mawt varies among Hanafi scholars: the mashayikh of Bukhara consider inability to go out as deathly, while those of Balkh consider it healthy if one can fulfill indoor needs. Later scholars (muta'akhkhirin) opine that one who can walk three steps without help is healthy, though this is considered weak. The author of Hidayah emphasizes that the ruling of firar is not limited to illness; any situation where death is predominantly feared (e.g., a storm at sea) triggers the same ruling. Thus, the distinction hinges on the predominance of safety vs. destruction.

Key Terms
فرار (firār): The act of a husband divorcing his wife while in a life-threatening situation to deprive her of inheritance.
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): A fatal illness from which death is predominantly feared, making the husband subject to rulings of inheritance protection for the wife.
صاحب الفراش (ṣāḥib al-firāsh): A person who is bedridden and unable to perform daily needs like going to the mosque or toilet.
محصور (maḥṣūr): A person besieged in a fortress or surrounded by enemies.
صف القتال (ṣaff al-qitāl): The battle line or rank of soldiers in combat.
مبارز (mubāriz): A person who steps forward from the battle line to engage in single combat with an opponent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in Al-Hidayah, what is the ruling on the wife's inheritance if the husband divorces her while he is in the battle line (saff al-qital) and then dies?
A) She inherits because the divorce is considered firar.
B) She does not inherit because safety is predominant in the battle line.
C) She inherits only if the husband was wounded in battle.
D) She inherits only if the divorce was revocable.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses the principle of firar and istihsan to grant the wife inheritance only when the husband's divorce occurs under a predominant risk of death, not when safety is the norm.

Divorce in Siege and Battle: When Does the Wife Inherit?
Ruling with proof: divorce in battle and inheritance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi distinction between safety-dominant and death-dominant situations to determine whether a wife inherits from a husband who divorced her during battle or siege.

Core Idea
A wife inherits from a husband who divorces during battle only if he actively faces death, not if he remains in safety.

This lesson examines a specific scenario from the Hidayah: a man divorces his wife while besieged in a fort or standing in a battle line, then dies. The surprising ruling is that she does not inherit if he stayed in the fort or line, but she does inherit if he came out to fight or was brought for qisas. This distinction rests on the concept of firar and the balance between safety and death.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The text presents two opposite rulings: one where the wife inherits (exit to fight) and one where she does not (remaining in fort/line). Distinguish the key difference: whether the husband was in a position of safety or actively facing death.
2
Understand the legal basis: istihsan vs. qiyas
The ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference), not qiyas. Qiyas would deny inheritance because the marriage ended before death, removing the cause of inheritance. Istihsan overrides to prevent the husband from evading inheritance via firar (escape).
3
Apply the concept of safety vs. death dominance
Determine which situations are considered safety-dominant (fort, battle line) and which are death-dominant (coming out to fight, being brought for qisas). This determines whether the divorce is a firar.
4
Trace the practical consequence
The wife's inheritance depends on whether the divorce was a firar (escape from inheritance) or not. If death is dominant, the divorce is firar and she inherits; if safety is dominant, she does not.
5
Note the analogy to other cases
The text mentions a pregnant woman in labor as an analogy: she is normally healthy, but when labor pains begin, she is like a sick person. Reflect on the principle of changing circumstances.

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کوئی شخص قلعہ میں محصور ہے اور دشمنوں نے قلعہ کو گھیر رکھا ہے یا لڑائی کی صف میں ہے۔ ایسی حالت میں اس شخص نے اپنی بیوی کو تین طلاقیں دے دیں۔ پھر اس شخص کی وفات ہوگئی تو اس کی یہ بیوی وارث نہیں ہوگی اور اگر کوئی شخص لڑائی کی صف سے نکل کر قتال کیلئے دشمن کے سامنے آیا یا کسی کو قصاص یار تم کی وجہ سے قتل کرنے کیلئے آگے بڑھایا گیا۔ پس اگر وہ اسی سبب سے مرگیا یا دوسرے سبب سے قتل کیا گیا تو اس کی بیوی وارث ہوگی۔
اس مسئلہ کی اصل ہم سابق میں بیان کر چکے کہ امراة فاراستحسانا وارث ہوگی نہ کہ قیا سا۔ وجہ استحسان اول باب میں بالتفصیل گذر چکی اور قیاس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ وراثت کا سبب موت کی وجہ سے نکاح کا ختم ہونا ہے اور چونکہ یہ شخص تین طلاقوں کے ذریعہ موت سے پہلے ہی نکاح کوختم کر چکا اسلئے وراثت کا سبب نہیں پایا گیا اور حکم بغیر سبب کے ثابت نہیں ہوتا۔ اس وجہ سے یہ عورت اپنے اس شوہر کی وارث نہیں ہوگی۔
رہی یہ بات کہ فرار کا حکم کب ثابت ہوگا۔ سو اس بارے میں صاحب ہدایہ کی رائے یہ ہے کہ جس وقت عورت کا حق شوہر کے مال کے ساتھ متعلق ہو جائے تو فرار کا حکم ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ یعنی اس وقت اگر شوہر نے اپنی بیوی کو طلاق بائن دی تو یہ طلاق فار ہو گی اور عورت کا حق شوہر کے مال کے ساتھ اس وقت متعلق ہوتا ہے، جبکہ شوہر کسی ایسے مرض میں مبتلا ہو جائے کہ اس سے ہلاکت کا اندیشہ غالب ہو۔ مثلاً شوہر صاحب فراش ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے صاحب فراش کی تعریف کرتے ہوئے فرمایا ہے کہ وہ مریض تندرستوں کی طرح اپنی ضروریات پورا کرنے پر قادر ہو۔ مثلاً نماز کیلئے مسجد نہیں جا سکتا اور قضائے حاجت کیلئے جانے پر قدرت نہیں۔ شمس الائمہ سرسی سے منقول ہے کہ فقیہ صاحب فراش اس وقت کہلائے گا جبکہ وہ مسجد جانے پر قادر نہ ہو اور بازاری جبکہ وہ دکان جانے پر قادر نہ ہو اور عورت جبکہ وہ چھت پر چڑھنے کی قدرت نہ رکھتی ہو۔
اور اگر مریض اندرون خانہ ضروریات کو پورا کر سکتا ہے۔ مثلا بیت الخلا جانا اور بیرون خانہ ضروریات پوری نہیں کر سکتا تو عام مشائخ بخارا کے نزدیک وہ مرض موت کے حکم میں ہے اور عام مشائخ بلخ کے نزدیک وہ تندرست کے حکم میں ہے۔ اور مشائخ متاخرین فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر بغیر دوسرے کی مدد کے تین قدم چلنے پر قادر ہے تو وہ تندرست کہلائے گا مگر یہ قول ضعیف ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ فرار کا حکم مرض میں منحصر نہیں بلکہ ہر وہ چیز جس سے ہلاکت کا خوف غالب ہو۔ وہ مرض موت کے حکم میں اور اس سے فرار کا حکم ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ مثلا کشتی میں بحری سفر پر ہے اور پانی میں اس قدر طغیانی پیدا ہوگئی کہ ڈوبنے کا اندیشہ غالب ہو گیا۔ پس ایسی حالت میں اگر اس شخص نے اپنی بیوی کو طلاق بائن دے دی تو فرار کاحکم ثابت ہو جائے گا۔
اور اگر ایسا عارض ہے کہ جس کے پیش آنے کے بعد سلامتی غالب ہے تو اس سے فرار کا حکم ثابت نہیں ہوگا۔ پس چونکہ جوشخص قلعہ میں محصور ہے اور جو لڑائی کی صف میں ہے اس سے سلامتی غالب ہے۔ اسلئے اس سے فرار کا حکم ثابت نہیں ہوگا۔ سلامتی کے غالب ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قلعہ دشمن کے ضرر کو دور کرنے کیلئے ہوتا ہے اور یہی حکم لشکر کا ہے۔ اور وہ شخص جو مقابلہ کیلئے صف سے باہر نکل کر آیا یا قتل کیلئے پیش کیا گیا تو اس سے ہلاکت غالب ہے۔ لہذا اس سے فرار کا حکم ثابت نہیں ہوگا۔
اور اس مسئلے کے اور بہت سے نظائر ہیں جو اسی اصول پر تخریج کیئے جائیں گے مثلاً حاملہ عورت تندرست کے مرتبہ میں ہے۔ پس اگر دردزہ شروع ہو گیا تو وہ مریض کے مانند ہوگی۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ امام محمد کا قول اذا مات في ذالك الوجه او قتل اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ ان دونوں میں کوئی فرق نہیں کہ وہ اسی سبب سے مرایا دوسرے سبب سے۔ مثلاً ایک شخص مرض کی وجہ سے صاحب فراش ہے اس کو قتل کر دیا گیا تو اس کی بیوی حکم فرار کی وجہ سے وارث ہوگی۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
Chapter on Divorce of the Sick. Explanation: If a person is besieged in a fort or in the battle line, and he gives his wife three divorces, then dies, his wife does not inherit. But if he comes out of the line to fight or is brought forward for qisas, and then dies from that cause or another, his wife inherits. The basis of this is that the woman inherits by istihsan, not by qiyas. The reason for istihsan has been detailed earlier. The reason for qiyas is that the cause of inheritance is the dissolution of marriage at death; here the marriage ended before death through divorce, so the cause is nonexistent. Thus, she does not inherit. As for when the ruling of firar applies: Sahib al-Hidayah says it applies when the wife's right attaches to the husband's wealth. That happens when the husband suffers from an illness where death is feared, e.g., he is bedridden. Sahib al-Hidayah defines bedridden as one who cannot fulfill his needs like a healthy person, e.g., cannot go to mosque or toilet. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi said a faqih is bedridden when unable to go to mosque, a shopkeeper when unable to go to his shop, a woman when unable to climb to the roof. If the patient can fulfill indoor needs but not outdoor, according to the scholars of Bukhara he is in marad al-mawt, but according to the scholars of Balkh he is healthy. Later scholars say if he can walk three steps without help, he is healthy, but this is weak. Sahib al-Hidayah says firar is not limited to illness; any situation where death is dominant is like marad al-mawt, e.g., on a ship in a storm. If a person in such a state gives a ba'in divorce, it is firar. If the situation is one where safety is dominant, like being in a fort or battle line, firar does not apply. The evidence that safety is dominant is that a fort is for protection. The person who goes out to fight faces death. There are many analogies; e.g., a pregnant woman is healthy, but when labor pains begin, she is like a sick person. Sahib al-Hidayah says Imam Muhammad's statement 'if he dies in that manner or is killed' indicates there is no difference whether he dies from that cause or another. For example, a bedridden person who is killed: his wife inherits due to firar. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling with proof from the commentary on the chapter of divorce of the sick. It begins with a specific scenario: a man in a siege or battle line divorces his wife thrice and then dies. The ruling is that the wife does not inherit. However, if the man exits the line to fight or is brought forward for qisas, and then dies, she does inherit. The text then explains the underlying principle: this ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference), not qiyas (analogy). Qiyas would say she does not inherit because the marriage ended before death, so the cause of inheritance is absent. But istihsan overrides this to prevent the husband from deliberately depriving the wife of inheritance by divorcing her when death is imminent. The passage then defines when the concept of 'firar' (escape from inheritance) applies: when the wife's right to inheritance has attached to the husband's wealth. This occurs when the husband is in marad al-mawt (a fatal illness where death is feared). The text provides a specific definition of being bedridden (sahib al-firash) as one who cannot perform normal activities like going to the mosque or toilet. Different scholarly opinions from Bukhara, Balkh, and later scholars are mentioned regarding the definition, with the later scholar's opinion being considered weak. Importantly, the text expands the concept of firar beyond illness to any situation where death is dominant, such as a ship in a storm. Conversely, if safety is dominant, like in a fort or battle formation, firar does not apply. The passage concludes with further examples, such as a pregnant woman during labor, and a clarification that if a bedridden person is killed, his wife inherits due to firar regardless of the cause of death.

Key Terms
فرار (firār): A divorce in marad al-mawt or similar extreme danger with the intent to deprive the wife of inheritance; the text treats it as a legal cause for the wife to inherit despite the divorce.
صاحب فراش (ṣāḥib al-firāsh): A bedridden patient who cannot fulfill his needs independently, e.g., cannot go to mosque or toilet.
مرض موت (maraḍ al-mawt): A fatal illness where death is feared; the text expands it to any situation where death is dominant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following best explains why a wife inherits from a husband who divorced her while exiting a battle line to fight?
A) Because the divorce was given in a state of anger.
B) Because the husband was in a death-dominant situation, making the divorce a firar.
C) Because the husband died in battle, which always causes inheritance.
D) Because the wife did not accept the divorce.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a wife inherits from a husband who divorced her during a death-dominant situation (firar) to prevent the husband from evading her inheritance right, but not if the situation is safety-dominant.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
10 min
Defining Marad al-Mawt and the Concept of Firar
Expansion probe: definitions of marad al-mawt and firar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define marad al-mawt (fatal illness) and firar (escape divorce) according to the Hanafi school, and identify the conditions under which a divorce is considered firar.

Core Idea
Firar is a divorce intended to deprive the wife of inheritance, triggered when death is the dominant fear.

This lesson delves into the precise definition of marad al-mawt and the concept of firar as presented in the Hidayah. The passage clarifies that firar is not limited to illness but extends to any situation where death is dominant. Various scholarly opinions on what constitutes marad al-mawt are examined, and the relied-upon position is that the wife's right to inheritance attaches when death is feared, regardless of the specific cause.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of firar
Firar is a ba'in divorce given by a husband when death is imminent, with the intent to deprive the wife of inheritance. The text states that firar applies when the wife's right attaches to the husband's wealth.
2
Identify when the wife's right attaches
The wife's right to inheritance attaches when the husband is in marad al-mawt (situation where death is feared). This includes being bedridden (sahib al-firash) or any analogous situation.
3
Analyze the definitions of bedridden (sahib al-firash)
The text provides examples from Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi: a faqih cannot go to mosque, a shopkeeper cannot go to his shop, a woman cannot climb to the roof. These illustrate inability to perform normal activities.
4
Examine the scholarly differences on marad al-mawt
Scholars of Bukhara vs. Balkh differ on whether inability to perform outdoor activities alone constitutes marad al-mawt. Later scholars introduced a three-step test, which is deemed weak.
5
Expand the concept beyond illness
Sahib al-Hidayah explicitly states that firar is not limited to illness; any situation where death is dominant (e.g., a ship in a storm) qualifies. This is a key expansion.
6
Apply to safety-dominant situations
If safety is dominant (e.g., fort, battle line), firar does not apply. The text uses the example of a pregnant woman: healthy normally, but in labor she is like a sick person.

اور اگر ایسا عارض ہے کہ جس کے پیش آنے کے بعد سلامتی غالب ہے تو اس سے فرار کا حکم ثابت نہیں ہوگا۔ پس چونکہ جوشخص قلعہ میں محصور ہے اور جو لڑائی کی صف میں ہے اس سے سلامتی غالب ہے۔ اسلئے اس سے فرار کا حکم ثابت نہیں ہوگا۔ سلامتی کے غالب ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قلعہ دشمن کے ضرر کو دور کرنے کیلئے ہوتا ہے اور یہی حکم لشکر کا ہے۔ اور وہ شخص جو مقابلہ کیلئے صف سے باہر نکل کر آیا یا قتل کیلئے پیش کیا گیا تو اس سے ہلاکت غالب ہے۔ لہذا اس سے فرار کا حکم ثابت نہیں ہوگا۔
اور اس مسئلے کے اور بہت سے نظائر ہیں جو اسی اصول پر تخریج کیئے جائیں گے مثلاً حاملہ عورت تندرست کے مرتبہ میں ہے۔ پس اگر دردزہ شروع ہو گیا تو وہ مریض کے مانند ہوگی۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ امام محمد کا قول اذا مات في ذالك الوجه او قتل اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ ان دونوں میں کوئی فرق نہیں کہ وہ اسی سبب سے مرایا دوسرے سبب سے۔ مثلاً ایک شخص مرض کی وجہ سے صاحب فراش ہے اس کو قتل کر دیا گیا تو اس کی بیوی حکم فرار کی وجہ سے وارث ہوگی۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
Chapter on Divorce of the Sick. Explanation: If a person is besieged in a fort or in the battle line, and he gives his wife three divorces, then dies, his wife does not inherit. But if he comes out of the line to fight or is brought forward for qisas, and then dies from that cause or another, his wife inherits. The basis of this is that the woman inherits by istihsan, not by qiyas. The reason for istihsan has been detailed earlier. The reason for qiyas is that the cause of inheritance is the dissolution of marriage at death; here the marriage ended before death through divorce, so the cause is nonexistent. Thus, she does not inherit. As for when the ruling of firar applies: Sahib al-Hidayah says it applies when the wife's right attaches to the husband's wealth. That happens when the husband suffers from an illness where death is feared, e.g., he is bedridden. Sahib al-Hidayah defines bedridden as one who cannot fulfill his needs like a healthy person, e.g., cannot go to mosque or toilet. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi said a faqih is bedridden when unable to go to mosque, a shopkeeper when unable to go to his shop, a woman when unable to climb to the roof. If the patient can fulfill indoor needs but not outdoor, according to the scholars of Bukhara he is in marad al-mawt, but according to the scholars of Balkh he is healthy. Later scholars say if he can walk three steps without help, he is healthy, but this is weak. Sahib al-Hidayah says firar is not limited to illness; any situation where death is dominant is like marad al-mawt, e.g., on a ship in a storm. If a person in such a state gives a ba'in divorce, it is firar. If the situation is one where safety is dominant, like being in a fort or battle line, firar does not apply. The evidence that safety is dominant is that a fort is for protection. The person who goes out to fight faces death. There are many analogies; e.g., a pregnant woman is healthy, but when labor pains begin, she is like a sick person. Sahib al-Hidayah says Imam Muhammad's statement 'if he dies in that manner or is killed' indicates there is no difference whether he dies from that cause or another. For example, a bedridden person who is killed: his wife inherits due to firar. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling with proof from the commentary on the chapter of divorce of the sick. It begins with a specific scenario: a man in a siege or battle line divorces his wife thrice and then dies. The ruling is that the wife does not inherit. However, if the man exits the line to fight or is brought forward for qisas, and then dies, she does inherit. The text then explains the underlying principle: this ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference), not qiyas (analogy). Qiyas would say she does not inherit because the marriage ended before death, so the cause of inheritance is absent. But istihsan overrides this to prevent the husband from deliberately depriving the wife of inheritance by divorcing her when death is imminent. The passage then defines when the concept of 'firar' (escape from inheritance) applies: when the wife's right to inheritance has attached to the husband's wealth. This occurs when the husband is in marad al-mawt (a fatal illness where death is feared). The text provides a specific definition of being bedridden (sahib al-firash) as one who cannot perform normal activities like going to the mosque or toilet. Different scholarly opinions from Bukhara, Balkh, and later scholars are mentioned regarding the definition, with the later scholar's opinion being considered weak. Importantly, the text expands the concept of firar beyond illness to any situation where death is dominant, such as a ship in a storm. Conversely, if safety is dominant, like in a fort or battle formation, firar does not apply. The passage concludes with further examples, such as a pregnant woman during labor, and a clarification that if a bedridden person is killed, his wife inherits due to firar regardless of the cause of death.

Key Terms
فرار (firār): A divorce in marad al-mawt or similar extreme danger with the intent to deprive the wife of inheritance; the text treats it as a legal cause for the wife to inherit despite the divorce.
صاحب فراش (ṣāḥib al-firāsh): A bedridden patient who cannot fulfill his needs independently, e.g., cannot go to mosque or toilet.
مرض موت (maraḍ al-mawt): A fatal illness where death is feared; the text expands it to any situation where death is dominant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in the Hidayah, which of the following would NOT be considered a situation where firar applies?
A) A man is bedridden and cannot go to the mosque.
B) A man is on a ship during a violent storm.
C) A man is in a fort under siege but not fighting.
D) A woman is in labor with complications.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, firar is a divorce that allows the wife to inherit even after a ba'in divorce, provided the divorce occurred in a situation where death was the dominant fear, whether due to illness or other dangers.

Conditional Divorce and Inheritance During Illness: The Hanafi Framework
Details inheritance rules when a husband makes a conditional divorce in health or sickness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on inheritance when a conditional divorce is made in health and the condition occurs during illness, distinguishing the majority position from Zufar's view and applying the rule to each category of condition.

Core Idea
In conditional divorce, inheritance depends on when the ta'liq was made, not just when the divorce takes effect; intent determines firar.

Divorce in the context of terminal illness raises questions about the wife's right to inherit. When a husband makes a conditional divorce statement in health, but the condition occurs while he is ill, does the wife still inherit? The Hanafi school provides a detailed answer that distinguishes between four types of conditions and considers the husband's intent to flee (firar). This lesson unpacks the passage from Ashraf al-Bidayah and the intra-Hanafi dispute with Zufar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central scenario and ruling
Start with the base case: husband says in health, 'When the month begins, you are divorced.' The month begins while he is ill. According to the majority Hanafi position, the wife does not inherit. Note that the divorce is effective, but inheritance is blocked.
This is the foundation of the dispute.
2
Understand the exception: ta'liq in illness
If the ta'liq itself was made in illness, the wife generally inherits, unless the condition is the wife's voluntary act (e.g., 'if you enter the house') or other exceptions. This shows that the timing of the statement matters.
3
Analyze Zufar's objection and Hanafi response
Zufar argues that a suspended divorce, when the condition occurs, is like an immediate divorce (īqāʻ). Therefore, if the condition occurs in illness, the divorce is considered issued in illness, triggering firar and inheritance. The Hanafi response: the divorce becomes effective only in effect (hukman), not in intent (qasdan). Since there was no intent to harm at the time of ta'liq, there is no injustice.
The key distinction: hukman vs. qasdan.
4
Trace the four categories and their subcases
The text classifies conditions into four: (1) time, (2) third party's act, (3) husband's own act, (4) wife's act. Each has two subcases: ta'liq in health & condition in illness, or both in illness. For each, determine whether the wife inherits based on the presence of firar.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) differs per category.
5
Apply the framework to the wife's act category
When the condition is the wife's act, the ruling further depends on whether the act is voluntary (she has a choice) or involuntary (she is compelled). The dispute between Muhammad and Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf on this point highlights the role of coercion.
This shows the nuance of Hanafi jurisprudence.

Source Text

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو بدایہ جلد پنجم
۲۵
باب طلاق المريض
مرد کا عورت کو حالت صحت میں کہنا اذا جاءا براس الشهر يا اذا دخلت الدار یا از اصلی فلان الظہر یا اذادخل فلان الدار تو تم طلاق والی ہو اور یہ تمام امور پائے گئے لیکن شوہر مریض ہے تو عورت وارث نہیں ہوگی اور اگر شوہر کا قول حالت مرض میں تھا وارث ہوگی
واذا قال الرجل لامرأته وهو صحيح اذاجاء راس الشهر او اذا دخلت الدار او اذا صلي فلان الظهر او اذا دخل فلان الدار فانت طالق فكانت هذه الاشياء والزوج مريض لم ترث وان كان القول في المرض ورثت الافي قوله اذا دخلت الدار وهذا على وجوه اما ان يعلق الطلاق بمجئ الوقت أو بفعل الاجنبى او بفعل نفسه او بفعل المرأة و كل وجه على وجهين اما ان كان التعليق فى الصحة والشرط في المرض او كلاهما في المرض اما الوجهان الاولان وهو ما ان كان التعليق بمجئى الوقت بان قال اذاجاء رأس الشهر فانت طالق او بفعل الاجنبى بان قال اذادخل فلان الدار او صلى فلان الظهر وكان التعليق والشرط فى المرض فلها الميراث لان القصد الى الفرار قد تحقق منه بمباشرة التعليق فى حال تعلق حقها بماله وان كان التعليق في الصحة والشرط فى المرض لم ترث وقال زفر ترث لان المعلق بالشرط ينزل عند وجود الشرط كالمنجز فکان ايقاعا في المرض ولنا ان التعليق السابق يصير تطليقا عند الشرط حكما لا قصداولاظلم الاعن قصدفلایر د تصرفه فاما الوجه الثالث وهو ما اذا علقه بفعل نفسه فسواء كان التعليق في الصحة والشرط في المرض او كانافى المرض والفعل مماله منه بد اولا بدله منه فيصير فارالوجود قصد الابطال امابا لتعليق او بمباشرة الشرط فى المرض وان لم يكن له من فعل الشرط بدفله من التعليق الف بدفير د تصرفه دفعا للضرر عنها واما الوجه الرابع وهو ما اذا علقه بفعلها فان كان التعليق والشرط فى المرض والفعل مما لها منه بدككلام زید و نحوه لم ترث لانها راضية بذلك وان كان الفعل لابدلها منه كا كل الطعام وصلوة الظهر و كلام الابوين ترث لانها مضطرة فى المباشرة لمالها فى الامتناع من خوف الهلاك في الدنيا اوفى العقبى و لارضاء مع الاضطرار واما اذا كان التعليق فى الصحة والشرط فى المرض ان كان الفعل ممالها منه بدفلا اشكال انه لاميراث لهاوان كان مما لا بدلهامنه فكذلك الجواب عند محمد وهو قول زفر لانه لم يوجد من الزوج صنع بعد ما تعلق حقها بماله وعند ابي حنيفة وابي يوسف ترث لان الزوج الجأها الى المباشرة فينتقل الفعل اليه كانها الة له كمافي الاكراه
Ashraf al-Bidayah Sharh Urdu Bidayah Volume 5, Chapter on Divorce of the Sick. A man says to his wife in health: 'When the month begins, or when you enter the house, or when so-and-so prays Zuhr, or when so-and-so enters the house, you are divorced.' All these occur while the husband is sick: the woman does not inherit. But if the statement was made in sickness, she inherits, except for 'when you enter the house.' This has categories: either he suspends divorce on a time, an act of a third party, his own act, or the woman's act. Each has two subtypes: the suspension was in health and the condition in illness, or both in illness. As for the first two (time or third party's act): if both suspension and condition are in illness, she inherits because the intent to flee (firar) is realized. If suspension in health and condition in illness, she does not inherit; but Zufar says she inherits because the suspended divorce occurs at condition like an immediate divorce, thus it is issued in illness. Our proof: the earlier suspension becomes a divorce at condition in effect, not intent; there is no injustice without intent, so his action is not restricted. Third category: suspending on his own act, whether suspension in health or illness, and the act is voluntary or involuntary: it is firar because he intends to nullify her right. Fourth category: suspending on her act: if both suspension and condition in illness and the act is voluntary (e.g., speaking to Zayd), she does not inherit because she is content. If the act is involuntary (e.g., eating food, praying Zuhr, speaking to parents), she inherits because she is compelled. If suspension in health and condition in illness: if the act is voluntary, no inheritance; if involuntary, according to Muhammad it is the same (no inheritance), which is Zufar's view, because no action from husband after her right attached. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, she inherits because the husband compelled her to perform, so the act transfers to him as if she is his tool, like in coercion.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute discussing inheritance rules for conditional divorce (ta'liq al-talaq) when the husband is ill. The text begins with a scenario: a husband makes a conditional divorce statement in health, such as 'when the month begins' or 'when you enter the house,' and the condition occurs while he is sick. The ruling: the wife does not inherit. But if the statement was made in sickness, she inherits, except for 'when you enter the house.' This exception is due to the wife's control. The text then breaks down the types of conditions into four categories based on what the condition is tied to: (1) a time, (2) an act of a third party, (3) the husband's own act, or (4) the wife's act. Each category has two subcases: whether the suspension (ta'liq) was in health and the condition in illness, or both in illness. For the first two categories (time or third party), if both suspension and condition are in illness, she inherits because the intent to flee (firar) is clear. If suspension was in health, she does not inherit. Zufar opposes, arguing that the divorce takes effect at the condition as if it were immediate, so it is considered issued in illness. The Hanafi response: the earlier suspension becomes a divorce in effect, not in intent, so it is not firar. For the third category (husband's own act), in all cases it is firar because the husband intends to nullify her right. For the fourth category (wife's act), the ruling depends on whether the act is voluntary or involuntary for her. If she has a choice, she is considered content and does not inherit; if she is compelled (e.g., eating, praying, speaking to parents are necessary), she inherits. If the suspension was in health and condition in illness, Muhammad and Zufar say no inheritance even for involuntary acts, because no new action from the husband. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say she does inherit because the husband's compulsion makes the act his, like a tool. This shows the importance of the husband's intent and the wife's freedom in determining inheritance after a conditional divorce during illness.

Key Terms
تعلیق (taʻlīq): Suspending the occurrence of divorce upon a future condition, e.g., 'if you enter the house, you are divorced.'
شرط (sharṭ): The future condition that triggers the divorce; its occurrence may happen during the husband's illness.
ایقاع (īqāʻ): The actual execution or issuance of divorce. Zufar argues that the divorce is considered issued (īqāʻ) at the time of the condition, not at the time of ta'liq.
فرار (firār): The act of fleeing from the wife's inheritance rights by intentionally causing a divorce during terminal illness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position, if a husband says in health, 'When the month begins, you are divorced,' and he becomes ill before the month begins, then the month arrives while he is ill, does the wife inherit?
A) Yes, because the divorce takes effect in illness.
B) No, because the ta'liq was in health.
C) Yes, but only if he dies immediately.
D) No, because the wife entered the house.

Key Takeaway
In conditional divorce, the wife's inheritance depends on whether the husband's intent to flee (firar) existed at the time of suspension (ta'liq), not merely the timing of the divorce's effect.

Conditional Divorce in Terminal Illness: When Does the Wife Inherit?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on conditional divorce and inheritance in terminal illness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the four categories of conditional divorce (ta'liq al-talaq) in terminal illness and state the Hanafi ruling on inheritance for each, including the dispute between Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad/Zufar.

Core Idea
In terminal illness, wife inherits only when husband's intent to deprive (firar) is evident; timing and condition type determine the ruling.

When a husband is terminally ill, his actions are scrutinized for attempts to deprive his wife of inheritance. Conditional divorces (ta'liq al-talaq) raise complex questions: does the wife inherit if the divorce is triggered during his illness? This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah classifies scenarios based on whether the condition involves time, a stranger, the husband's own act, or the wife's act, and whether the ta'liq was made in health or illness. The Hanafi school has a nuanced position, with a known difference among its founding imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories of condition
The passage divides conditional divorces into four types based on what the divorce is suspended upon: (1) arrival of time, (2) act of a stranger, (3) the husband's own act, (4) the wife's act.
Each category is further split based on whether the ta'liq was made in health or terminal illness.
2
Apply the principle of firar (intent to deprive)
The wife inherits only if the husband's action shows a clear intent to deprive her of inheritance (firar). If the ta'liq and condition both occur in illness, firar is presumed. If ta'liq was in health, firar is absent unless the husband compelled the wife to fulfill the condition.
Imam Zufar differs: he treats the suspended divorce as immediate upon condition, so the timing of ta'liq matters less.
3
Analyze the fourth category (wife's act) and the internal dispute
For the wife's act, distinguish between acts she has an alternative to (e.g., speaking to Zaid) and unavoidable acts (e.g., eating, praying, speaking to parents). If the act is unavoidable and ta'liq was in health but condition in illness, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say she inherits; Muhammad and Zufar say she does not.
The key issue: did the husband's ta'liq in health count as an action after the wife's right attached? The majority view (Abu Hanifa/Yusuf) protects the wife by attributing the act to the husband's compulsion.
4
Determine the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position
The view that grants inheritance in cases of the wife's unavoidable act, even if ta'liq was in health, is considered mufta bihi to remove hardship from the wife. This aligns with the principle of darar (harm) being removed.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa today.
5
Review the other categories for completeness
For time-based or stranger's act conditions: if both ta'liq and condition in illness, she inherits; if ta'liq in health and condition in illness, she does not. For the husband's own act: if unavoidable, his disposal is rejected; if avoidable, he is considered an escapee.
These rulings are consistent across the Hanafi imams except Zufar's divergence on the first two categories.

وهو ما اذا علقه بفعل نفسه فسواء كان التعليق في الصحة والشرط في المرض او كانافى المرض والفعل مماله منه بد اولا بدله منه فيصير فارالوجود قصد الابطال امابا لتعليق او بمباشرة الشرط فى المرض وان لم يكن له من فعل الشرط بدفله من التعليق الف بدفير د تصرفه دفعا للضرر عنها واما الوجه الرابع وهو ما اذا علقه بفعلها فان كان التعليق والشرط فى المرض والفعل مما لها منه بدككلام زید و نحوه لم ترث لانها راضية بذلك وان كان الفعل لابدلها منه كا كل الطعام وصلوة الظهر و كلام الابوين ترث لانها مضطرة فى المباشرة لمالها فى الامتناع من خوف الهلاك في الدنيا اوفى العقبى و لارضاء مع الاضطرار واما اذا كان التعليق فى الصحة والشرط فى المرض ان كان الفعل ممالها منه بدفلا اشكال انه لاميراث لهاوان كان مما لا بدلهامنه فكذلك الجواب عند محمد وهو قول زفر لانه لم يوجد من الزوج صنع بعد ما تعلق حقها بماله وعند ابي حنيفة وابي يوسف ترث لان الزوج الجأها الى المباشرة فينتقل الفعل اليه كانها الة له كمافي الاكراه۔
Chapter of Divorce of the Sick. And there are many other parallels to this issue that will be derived on this principle, for example, a pregnant woman is in the status of a healthy woman. So if labor pain begins, then she will be like a sick person. The author of Al-Hidayah states that Imam Muhammad's statement 'when he dies in that manner or is killed' is evidence that there is no difference between the two, that he died from that cause or another cause. For example, a person is bedridden due to illness, he is killed, then his wife will inherit due to the ruling of escape. And Allah knows best what is correct. A man saying to his wife in a state of health: 'When the beginning of the month comes, or when you enter the house, or when so-and-so prays Dhuhr, or when so-and-so enters the house, then you are divorced.' And all these matters occurred, but the husband is sick, then the wife will not inherit. And if the husband's statement was in a state of illness, she will inherit. And if the husband said to his wife while he is healthy: 'When the beginning of the month comes, or when you enter the house, or when so-and-so prays Dhuhr, or when so-and-so enters the house, then you are divorced.' Then these things occurred while the husband is sick, she does not inherit. And if the statement was in illness, she inherits, except in his statement 'when you enter the house'. And this has aspects: either he suspends the divorce on the arrival of time, or on the act of a stranger, or on his own act, or on the act of the wife. And each aspect has two ways: either the suspension was in health and the condition (occurrence) in terminal illness, or both are in terminal illness. As for the first two aspects, which are when the suspension is on the arrival of time, such as saying 'when the beginning of the month comes, you are divorced', or on the act of a stranger, such as saying 'when so-and-so enters the house' or 'when so-and-so prays Dhuhr', and the suspension and condition were in illness, then she has inheritance because the intent to escape has been realized from him by undertaking the suspension at a time when her right has become attached to his property. And if the suspension was in health and the condition in illness, she does not inherit. And Zufar said: she inherits because the suspended (divorce) at the occurrence of the condition becomes like an immediate (divorce), so it is an execution of divorce in illness. And for us (the Hanafi proof) is that the prior suspension becomes a divorce at the condition in terms of ruling not intent, and there is no injustice except with intent, so his disposal is not rejected. As for the third aspect, which is when he suspends it on his own act, then it is the same whether the suspension was in health and the condition in illness or both were in illness, and the act is something from which he has no alternative or has an alternative, then he becomes an escapee due to the presence of intent to invalidate, either by the suspension or by undertaking the condition in illness. And if he has no alternative from the act, he has thousands of alternatives from the suspension, so his disposal is rejected to remove harm from her. As for the fourth aspect, which is when he suspends it on her act, then if the suspension and condition were in illness and the act is something from which she has an alternative, like speaking to Zaid and the like, she does not inherit because she is pleased with that. And if the act is inevitable for her, like eating food, praying Dhuhr, and speaking to parents, she inherits because she is compelled in performing it, as she has no way to abstain due to fear of destruction in this world or the Hereafter, and there is no consent with compulsion. As for when the suspension was in health and the condition in illness: if the act is something from which she has an alternative, there is no doubt that she has no inheritance. And if it is something inevitable for her, then the same answer according to Muhammad, and it is the statement of Zufar, because no action from the husband occurred after her right attached to his property. And according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, she inherits because the husband compelled her to perform, so the act is transferred to him, as if she is his tool, just as in coercion.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah expands upon the chapter of divorce in terminal illness (marad al-mawt). The central issue is whether a conditional divorce (ta'liq al-talaq) pronounced by a husband in health or illness affects the wife's right to inherit from him when the condition is fulfilled after his death or during his terminal illness. The text first notes parallels: a pregnant woman in labor is treated as sick. Imam Muhammad's statement on death by cause is cited to show that the manner of death does not change the rule of inheritance due to 'firar' (escape). The main discussion classifies conditional divorces into four categories based on the condition: (1) arrival of time, (2) act of a stranger, (3) husband's own act, (4) wife's act. Each category has sub-cases depending on whether the ta'liq was made in health or illness and the condition fulfilled in health or illness. The Hanafi position is that the wife inherits only when the husband's intent to deprive (firar) is evident. For the first two faces, if both ta'liq and condition occur in illness, she inherits; if ta'liq in health and condition in illness, she does not. Imam Zufar opposes, arguing the condition makes the talaq immediate at fulfillment. The Hanafi rebuttal (wa lana) is that the prior suspension becomes a talaq only in legal effect (hukman), not in intent (qasdan), and injustice is only with intent. For the third face (husband's act), regardless of timing, if the act is avoidable, the husband is considered an escapee; if unavoidable, his disposal is rejected. For the fourth face (wife's act), if both ta'liq and condition in illness: if the act is avoidable, she does not inherit (she consented); if unavoidable (e.g., eating, praying, speaking to parents), she inherits due to compulsion (idtirar). If ta'liq in health and condition in illness, and the act is unavoidable, Imam Muhammad and Zufar say no inheritance (no husband's action), but Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say inheritance because the husband compelled her, transferring the act to him as if she were his tool, like in coercion (ikrah). The mufta bihi position is the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf for this last scenario, as it removes harm from the wife.

Key Terms
تعليق (ta'liq): Suspending the occurrence of divorce upon the fulfillment of a condition.
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): A terminal illness that is likely to lead to death, during which the husband's actions are scrutinized for intent to deprive the wife of inheritance.
فرار (firar): The husband's deliberate act of divorcing his wife in terminal illness to prevent her from inheriting from him.
إلجاء (ilja'): Compelling someone to act by creating a situation where they have no reasonable alternative.
إكراه (ikrah): Coercion that negates free consent, often used as an analogy to ilja'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, in which scenario does the wife inherit from the husband who divorced her in terminal illness?
A) When the husband conditioned divorce on the wife's avoidable act in both health and condition in illness.
B) When the husband conditioned divorce on the wife's unavoidable act (like eating) in health, and the condition was fulfilled in illness.
C) When the husband conditioned divorce on his own unavoidable act in health and condition in illness.
D) When the husband conditioned divorce on the arrival of a time in health and the time arrived in illness.

Key Takeaway
In terminal illness, a husband's conditional divorce only bars the wife's inheritance if no intent to deprive (firar) is proven; when the wife is compelled to fulfill an unavoidable condition, the act is attributed to the husband and she inherits.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
12 min
Inheritance of a Woman Divorced by Suspension During Terminal Illness: The Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Explains when a divorced woman inherits from a sick husband based on timing of suspension and condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the four forms of suspended divorce (ta'liq) and determine when the wife inherits from the husband according to the Hanafi majority and Imam Zufar.

Core Idea
Intent to flee (firar) at time of suspension determines inheritance, not the condition's occurrence.

The chapter on divorce of the sick person addresses a critical question: if a husband divorces his wife during his terminal illness, does she still inherit from him? The answer turns on whether the divorce was a 'fugitive divorce' (talaq al-farr)—one made to deprive her of inheritance. This lesson unpacks the various scenarios of suspended divorce (ta'liq) presented in al-Hidayah, focusing on the timing of the suspension (ta'liq) and the occurrence of the condition (shart). We will explore the main dispute between the Hanafi majority and Imam Zufar, and the further intra-Hanafi difference when the divorce is suspended on the wife's unavoidable act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four forms of ta'liq
Recognize that the husband may suspend divorce on a future time, an act of a stranger, his own act, or the wife's act. The passage categorizes these as the four forms.
These correspond to: (1) time, (2) third party act, (3) husband's own act, (4) wife's act.
2
Distinguish timing: suspension vs condition
For each form, note whether the suspension (ta'liq) occurred in health or terminal illness, and whether the condition occurred in health or illness. The ruling depends on both timings.
The passage omits cases where suspension is in illness and condition in health, or both in health.
3
Apply the principle of firar (intent to flee)
If the husband suspended in illness, the intent to flee is presumed because he acted after his wife's inheritance right had attached. If suspended in health, no such intent exists at that time, so no firar unless he later compelled the condition.
The husband's own unavoidable act is treated as if he compelled it, establishing intent.
4
Compare with Imam Zufar's view
Imam Zufar holds that the divorce occurs at the moment of condition, so if condition is in illness, it is as if divorced in illness, making it a fugitive divorce. He thus concludes the wife inherits even if suspension was in health.
Zufar's proof: a suspended divorce occurs like an immediate divorce at condition.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Practically, in cases of suspension in health with condition in illness, the majority says no inheritance; Zufar says yes. Also, note the intra-Hanafi split on the wife's unavoidable act: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold she inherits; Muhammad and Zufar hold she does not.
The mufta bihi is the majority view, except in the wife's unavoidable act where Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf prevail.
