Apostasy vs. Mutāwa'ah After Divorce in Fatal Illness: Inheritance Effect
Distinguishing apostasy from mutāwa'ah for inheritance after divorce in illness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the effect of apostasy from mutāwa'ah on inheritance after divorce in fatal illness, and explain the legal reasoning (talil) for the difference.

Core Idea
Apostasy destroys inheritance eligibility; mutāwa'ah does not — because mahram status does not affect inheritance.

This lesson examines a specific scenario from the chapter on divorce of the sick (talāq al-marīḍ). After a husband divorces his wife in his fatal illness, two different actions by the wife lead to opposite inheritance outcomes. Understanding why apostasy bars inheritance while committing zinā with the husband's son does not requires grasping the Hanafi concept of ahlīyah al-irth (eligibility for inheritance) and the effect of mahram status.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
First, read the passage and note the two cases: (1) wife apostatizes after divorce then returns to Islam; (2) wife does not apostatize but submits to intercourse with husband's son (mutāwa'ah). Both occur during iddah after a divorce in the husband's fatal illness.
2
Extract the ruling
State the inheritance outcome for each case: in the apostasy case, she does not inherit; in the mutāwa'ah case, she does inherit. Confirm this from the text.
3
Analyze the reason (talil)
Examine the reasoning given: apostasy nullifies ahlīyah al-irth (eligibility for inheritance) because an apostate cannot inherit. Mutāwa'ah does not nullify eligibility because becoming a mahram (unmarriageable relative) does not prevent inheritance; it only prohibits marriage.
4
Distinguish the boundary case
Note the exception: if mutāwa'ah occurred while the marriage was still intact (before divorce), she would not inherit because it establishes separation (furqah), demonstrating her consent to nullify the marriage. After three divorces, this effect does not apply because the separation is already complete.
5
Apply the principle
Understand the broader rule: acts that remove Islamic identity (apostasy) destroy inheritance eligibility; acts that create mahram prohibitions (like zinā with son) do not affect eligibility. This principle can be applied to similar cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب طلاق المريض
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم
مرض الموت میں عورت کو طلاق دی عورت ( العیاذ باللہ ) مرتد ہوگئی پھر مسلمان ہوگئی پھر شوہر اس مرض میں فوت ہو گیا اور یہ عدت میں تھی وارث نہیں ہوگی اور اگر مرتد نہیں ہوئی
بلکہ شوہر کے بیٹے کو اپنے اوپر جماع کی قدرت دے دی وارث ہوگی ، وجہ فرق
ولوطلقها فارتدت والعياذ بالله ثم اسلمت ثم مات من مرض موته وهى فى العدة لم ترث وان لم ترتدبل طاوعت ابن زوجها في الجماع ورثت وجه الفرق انها بالردة ابطلت اهلية الارث اذالمرتد لايرث احدا و لابقاء له بدون الاهلية وبالمطاوعة ما ابطلت الاهلية لان المحرمية لاينا في الارث وهو الباقي بخلاف ما اذا طاوعت في حال قيام النكاح لانها تثبت الفرقة فتكون راضية ببطلان السبب وبعد الطلقات الثلث لا تثبت الحرمة بالمطاوعة لتقد مها عليها فافترقا
ترجمہ اور اگر عورت کو ( مرض الموت میں ) طلاق دے دی پھر معاذ اللہ وہ عورت مرتد ہوگئی ۔ پھر اسلام لائی۔ پھر شوہر اپنے اسی مرض میں مر گیا۔ درانحالیکہ وہ عورت عدت میں ہے تو عورت وارث نہ ہوگی اور اگر مرتد نہیں ہوئی بلکہ اپنے شوہر کے بیٹے کی جماع کے سلسلہ میں مطاوعت کی تو وارث ہوگی۔ وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ عورت نے مرتد ہو کر میراث کی لیاقت باطل کر دی۔ اسلئے کہ مرتد کسی کا وارث نہیں ہو سکتا اور بغیر وارث ہونے کی اہلیت کے وراثت باقی نہیں رہتی ہے اور مطاوعت ابن زوج کی وجہ سے عورت نے لیاقت باطل نہیں کی ہے۔ کیونکہ دائی حرام ہو نا وراثت کے منافی نہیں ہے اور وہ باقی ہے، برخلاف اس کے کہ عورت نے نکاح موجود ہونے کی حالت میں مطاوعت کی ہو۔ کیونکہ مطاوعت ابن زوج قیام نکاح کی حالت میں فرقت ثابت کرتا ہے۔ پس وہ سبب کے بطلان پر راضی ہوگی اور تین طلاقوں کے بعد مطاوعت کی وجہ سے حرمت ثابت نہیں ہوتی ۔ مطاوعت پر حرمت کے مقدم ہونے کی وجہ سے پس ( دونوں صورتوں میں ) فرق
ظاہر ہو گیا۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر شوہر نے اپنی بیوی کو تین طلاقیں یا ایک طلاق بائن دے دی ۔ پھر وہ مرتد ہو گئی ۔ معاذ اللہ ! پھر دوبارہ اسلام میں داخل ہوئی۔ پھر شوہر اپنے اس مرض کی وجہ سے مر گیا اور عورت ابھی عدت میں ہے۔ تو یہ عورت اس کی وارث ہوگی اور اگر مرتد نہیں ہوئی بلکہ اپنے شوہر کے سابقہ بیٹے سے جماع کر لیا تو یہ وارث ہو گئی۔ دونوں مسئلوں میں وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ مرتد ہونے کی وجہ سے وراثت کی لیاقت باطل ہو جاتی ہے۔ کیونکہ مرتد کسی کا وارث نہیں ہوسکتا اور بغیر اہلیت کے وراثت باقی نہیں رہتی ہے۔ اس وجہ سے ہم نے کہا کہ مرتد ہونے کی صورت میں عورت وارث نہیں ہوگی اور مطاوعت ابن زوج کی وجہ سے اہلیت باطل نہیں ہوتی ۔ کیونکہ محرمیت وراثت کے منافی نہیں ۔ بلکہ نکاح کے منافی ہے جیسے ماں اور بہن میں محرمیت یعنی دانگی حرام ہونا، نکاح کے منافی تو ہے مگر وراثت کے منافی نہیں ہے بہر حال مطاوعت ابن زوج کی صورت میں وراثت باقی ہے۔ اس وجہ سے ہم نے کہا کہ اس صورت میں عورت وارث ہوگی۔
ہاں البتہ اگر عورت نے نکاح کے موجود رہتے ہوئے ابن زوج سے مطاوعت کر لی تو بالیقین وارث نہیں ہو گی۔ دلیل یہ کہ مطاوعت ابن زوج کی وجہ سے فرقت ثابت ہوئی ہے۔ پس ثابت ہوگا کہ عورت وراثت کے سبب ( نکاح ) کو باطل کرنے پر راضی ہوگئی ہے اور اگر
Chapter on Divorce of the Sick. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary of Hidaya Volume Five. He divorced the woman in fatal illness; she apostatized (may Allah protect us), then became Muslim, then the husband died in that illness while she was in iddah; she will not inherit. But if she did not apostatize rather she submitted to intercourse with the husband's son, she will inherit. The reason for the difference: And if he divorces her and she apostatizes (may Allah protect), then becomes Muslim, then he dies of his fatal illness while she is in iddah, she does not inherit. But if she does not apostatize but submits to intercourse with the husband's son, she inherits. The reason for the difference is that by apostasy she nullified her eligibility for inheritance because an apostate does not inherit anyone, and there is no continuation without eligibility. By submission (mutāwa'ah) she did not nullify eligibility because becoming a mahram (prohibited for marriage) does not prevent inheritance; it remains. Contrary to if she submitted while the marriage was still in effect, because it establishes separation (furqah) and she is content with the nullification of the cause. After three divorces, prohibition (hurmah) is not established by submission because it precedes it. So they differ. Translation: And if he divorces her in fatal illness, then she apostatizes (may Allah protect), then becomes Muslim, then the husband dies in that illness while she is in iddah, she will not inherit. But if she did not apostatize but submitted to intercourse with the husband's son, she will inherit. The reason for the difference is that by apostasy she nullified her eligibility for inheritance because an apostate cannot inherit anyone, and inheritance does not remain without eligibility. By submission she did not nullify eligibility because becoming a mahram is not contrary to inheritance; it remains. Contrary to if she submitted while the marriage was still in effect, because submission with the husband's son under existing marriage establishes separation, so she is content with nullifying the cause. After three divorces, prohibition is not established by submission because it precedes it. So they differ. Commentary: The case is: If the husband gave his wife three divorces or one irrevocable divorce (bā'in), then she apostatized, then re-entered Islam, then the husband died of that illness while she is in iddah, she will not inherit. But if she did not apostatize but committed intercourse with the husband's son, she inherits. The reason for the difference is that apostasy nullifies eligibility for inheritance because an apostate cannot inherit; without eligibility inheritance does not remain. So we said in the case of apostasy she does not inherit. Submission with the husband's son does not nullify eligibility because mahram status is not contrary to inheritance; it is contrary to marriage. For example, mahram status like mother and sister prohibits marriage but not inheritance. So in the case of submission, inheritance remains. Therefore we said she inherits. But if she submitted while the marriage was still in effect, she definitely does not inherit because submission with the husband's son under existing marriage establishes separation, proving she is content with nullifying the cause of inheritance (nikah).
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling and its reasoning for two scenarios after a divorce during fatal illness. The first scenario: the wife apostatizes after divorce, then returns to Islam, and the husband dies in his illness while she is in iddah. She does not inherit because apostasy destroys eligibility for inheritance (ahlīyah al-irth). The second scenario: instead of apostasy, she commits zinā with her husband's son (mutāwa'at ibn al-zawj). She inherits because becoming a mahram (like a mother-in-law) does not affect inheritance eligibility. However, if she committed this act while the marriage was still intact (before divorce), she would not inherit because it would establish separation (furqah), showing her consent to nullify the marriage. After three divorces, the act does not establish hurmah because the divorce already created complete separation. The commentary clarifies the distinction: apostasy removes eligibility entirely; becoming a mahram does not.

Key Terms
مطاوعت (mutāwa'ah): Voluntary submission to sexual intercourse; here specifically with the husband's son after divorce during fatal illness.
محرمیت (mahramiyyah): The state of being a mahram (unmarriageable relative); here it refers to the relationship created by nursing or marriage affinity.
اہلیت میراث (ahlīyah al-irth): Eligibility for inheritance; a legal capacity that requires being Muslim at the time of death of the deceased.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi ruling state that a woman who commits zinā with her husband's son after being divorced in fatal illness still inherits?
A) Because she repented.
B) Because becoming a mahram does not nullify inheritance eligibility.
C) Because the husband's divorce was invalid.
D) Because she is still in iddah.

Key Takeaway
Apostasy destroys inheritance eligibility; mutāwa'ah (becoming mahram) does not, because mahram status only affects marriage, not inheritance.

Why Zina with Step-son Does Not Bar Inheritance but Apostasy Does
Explains the rational distinction between apostasy and zina regarding inheritance capacity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the effects of apostasy and zina with a stepson on a wife's inheritance after a divorce during fatal illness, and state the underlying principle of legal capacity.

Core Idea
Apostasy destroys legal capacity for inheritance; zina with stepson does not.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents a nuanced distinction in inheritance law for a wife divorced during the husband's fatal illness. Two superficially similar scenarios – the wife's apostasy and her zina with a stepson – yield opposite rulings on her right to inherit. The key lies in whether her action undermines her legal capacity (ahliyyah) for inheritance. Let's explore the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The wife is divorced during the husband's fatal illness. In scenario 1, she apostatizes (may Allah protect) and then returns to Islam while still in iddah. In scenario 2, she does not apostatize but commits zina with her husband's son (from another wife).
Both are sinful acts, but the legal consequences differ.
2
State the ruling for each scenario
In scenario 1, the wife does NOT inherit from the husband. In scenario 2, she DOES inherit.
The ruling applies only if the husband dies from the same fatal illness while she is still in iddah.
3
Identify the distinguishing factor (wajh al-farq)
Apostasy destroys the capacity (ahliyyah) to inherit, because an apostate cannot inherit anyone. Zina with a stepson does not destroy capacity, because the resulting mahram relationship (permanent prohibition of marriage) does not affect inheritance; it only affects marriage.
The principle: capacity to inherit is a legal status that is only nullified by actions that remove that status, such as apostasy.
4
Consider the exception when zina occurs during marriage
If the wife commits zina with the stepson while the marriage is still ongoing, she does NOT inherit. This is because her action causes a separation (firqah) showing she agreed to nullify the cause of inheritance (the marriage itself).
The timeline matters: zina after the divorce (after the three divorces have been pronounced) does not affect inheritance, because the separation was already caused by the husband.
5
Confirm the ruling after three divorces
If the husband pronounces three divorces first, and then the wife commits zina with the stepson, she inherits. The separation was from the husband's side, not her action, so her capacity remains intact.
This is the opposite scenario: the husband initiated the separation, so the wife is considered 'imra'ah farr' (a woman like a widow) and inherits.

Source Text

And if he divorces her and she apostatizes (may Allah protect) then accepts Islam, then he dies in his fatal illness while she is in iddah, she does not inherit. But if she did not apostatize rather she acquiesced (committed zina) with her husband's son, she inherits. The reason for the difference is that she has rejected the capacity for inheritance through apostasy, because an apostate cannot inherit anyone and there is no remaining without the capacity. And through acquiescence she did not reject the capacity because a prohibited relationship does not prevent inheritance, and it remains. Unlike when she acquiesced while the marriage existed, because it establishes separation, so she is satisfied with the nullification of the cause. And after three divorces, prohibition is not established through acquiescence because it precedes it. So they differ.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from al-Hidayah on the inheritance of a wife divorced during the husband's fatal illness. The matn presents two scenarios: (1) The wife apostates after divorce, then returns to Islam, then the husband dies while she is in iddah – she does not inherit. (2) She does not apostate but commits zina with her husband's son (from another wife) – she does inherit. The sharh explains the difference: Apostasy destroys the legal capacity (ahliyyah) for inheritance because an apostate cannot inherit anyone. Zina with the son does not destroy this capacity because the resulting mahram relationship (permanent prohibition of marriage) does not prevent inheritance; it only affects marriage. The commentary further distinguishes when the zina occurs during the ongoing marriage: if the wife commits zina with the stepson while the marriage still exists, she does not inherit because that action causes separation (firqah) during the marriage, showing she agreed to nullify the cause of inheritance (the marriage). But if the three divorces have already been pronounced before the zina, the separation was caused by the husband, not by her action, so she still inherits. This illustrates the principle that in fatal illness, a woman is considered an 'imra'ah farr' (a woman who is like a widow) and inherits if the separation was initiated by the husband.

Key Terms
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): A fatal illness from which the person is expected to die and actually dies.
مطاوعت (mutāwa‘ah): Acquiescence; here meaning the wife voluntarily commits zina with her stepson.
محرمیت (maḥramiyyah): A relationship that makes marriage permanently prohibited, such as mother, sister, stepmother.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a husband divorces his wife during fatal illness, and the wife then commits zina with the husband's son (from another wife) while in iddah, does she inherit from the husband?
A) Yes, because zina does not affect her capacity to inherit.
B) No, because zina breaks the marriage tie.
C) Yes, but only if she repents.
D) No, because she has committed a major sin.

Key Takeaway
A wife divorced during fatal illness retains inheritance capacity unless she commits an act that nullifies that capacity, such as apostasy; zina with stepson does not nullify it.

Li'an During Fatal Illness: Effect on Wife's Inheritance
Dispute between Imam Muhammad and the Shaykhayn on inheritance of a wife after li'an during fatal illness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a wife's inheritance after li'an during fatal illness and apply the principle of compulsion (ilja') to determine the ruling.

Core Idea
When a wife is compelled to seek li'an to clear her honor, her inheritance right is preserved.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute about the interaction between li'an and inheritance. The key question: if a husband accuses his wife of zina while healthy but only performs li'an during his fatal illness, does the wife inherit? The answer hinges on whether the wife's involvement in the li'an process was voluntary or compelled. Understanding this distinction is critical for applying the correct inheritance ruling in such cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Separate the scenario where qadhf (accusation) occurs while healthy and li'an during illness, from the scenario where both occur during illness. The ruling differs.
In the second scenario, all Imams agree she inherits.
2
State the positions of the Imams
For the first scenario: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (Shaykhayn) rule that the wife inherits; Imam Muhammad rules she does not.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Understand the argument based on compulsion
The Shaykhayn argue that the wife is compelled (mulja'ah) to seek li'an to defend her honor; thus the separation is not voluntary. Imam Muhammad argues that since the accusation occurred when the husband was healthy, the wife could have sought li'an earlier, making her action voluntary.
The concept of ilja' is central.
4
Apply the analogy to conditional divorce
The text states this is like a conditional divorce tied to an act from which the wife has no escape. When she is forced to act, the divorce is not by her choice.
Analogical reasoning (qiyas) supports the Shaykhayn view.
5
Evaluate the practical difference
The thamarah al-khilaf is whether the wife inherits. In the Shaykhayn view, she does; in Muhammad's view, she does not. A qadi must decide based on which position is mufta bihi.
The text does not specify the mufta bihi, but the Shaykhayn view is widely adopted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن قذف امرأته وهو صحيح ولاعن في المرض ورثت وقال محمد لاترث وان كان القذف في المرض ورثته فى قولهم جميعا وهذا ملحق بالتعليق بفعل لا بدلها منه اذهي ملجاة الى الخصومة لدفع عار الزناء عن نفسها وقدبينا الوجه فيه
ترجمہ اور جس شخص نے تندرستی کی حالت میں اپنی بیوی کو زنا کی تہمت لگائی اور مرض الموت میں احان کیا ، تو عورت وارث ہوگی اور امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ عورت وارث نہیں ہوگی اور گر تہمت لگانا مرض الموت میں ہوا تو باتفاق ائمہ ثلاثہ عورت اس کی وارث ہوگی اور یہ صورت ملحق ہے ایسے فعل کی تعلیق کے ساتھ کہ عورت کیلئے اس سے چارہ نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ عورت لا چار خصومت پر مجبور ہوئی اپنے اوپر سے زنا کی عار کو دور کرنے کیلئے اور ہم اس میں وجہ بیان کر چکے ہیں۔
تشریح مسئلہ، اگر کسی شخص نے بحالت صحت اپنی بیوی کو زنا کے ساتھ متہم کیا اور لعان کیا مرض الموت میں پھر حاکم نے ان دونوں میں تفریق کر دی۔ اس کے بعد شوہر عورت کی عدت ہی میں مر گیا تو یہ عورت وارث ہو گی۔ یہ شیخین کا مذہب ہے اور امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ وارث نہیں ہوگی۔ اور اگر زنا کی تہمت لگانا بھی مرض الموت میں پایا گیا تو ائمہ ثلاثہ کے نزدیک یہ عورت وارث ہوگی۔
And whoever accuses his wife while he is healthy and performs li'an during illness, she inherits. And Muhammad said: she does not inherit. And if the accusation was during illness, she inherits in all their statements. And this is connected to a conditional divorce by an act from which she has no escape, because she is compelled to litigation to repel the disgrace of zina from herself. And we have explained the reason in it.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding inheritance when a husband accuses his wife of zina (qadhf) and performs li'an (mutual imprecation) during his fatal illness. The matn states: If the husband accuses his wife while healthy but performs li'an only when sick, then according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the Shaykhayn), the wife inherits. Imam Muhammad disagrees: she does not inherit. However, if both the accusation and li'an occur during the fatal illness, all three Imams agree she inherits. The sharh explains that this ruling is analogous (mulhaq) to a conditional divorce tied to an action the wife cannot avoid — here, she is forced to go to court to defend her honor. Her initiation of litigation does not indicate willingness to end the marriage; rather, she is compelled. The authority of this ruling is from al-Hidayah, and the difference hinges on the timing of the qadhf: if it was before the illness, the wife's seeking li'an may be seen as voluntary, but the Shaykhayn consider it still compelled because she must defend herself. The commentary notes that this point has been previously discussed under the topic of conditional divorce with no escape.

Key Terms
قذف (qadhf): Accusing a chaste person of zina without four witnesses.
لعان (li‘ān): Mutual imprecation between spouses when the husband accuses wife of zina without witnesses; leads to separation.
ملجأة (mulja’ah): Compelled; forced to do something against one's will.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a husband accuses his wife of zina while healthy but performs li'an during his fatal illness, which Hanafi imams agree that the wife inherits?
A) Only Abu Hanifa
B) Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (Shaykhayn)
C) All three (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad)
D) Only Imam Muhammad

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, when a wife is compelled (mulja'ah) to seek li'an to defend her honor, the separation is not considered voluntary, and she retains her inheritance right according to the Shaykhayn.

Ila and Inheritance: The Timing of the Vow Matters
Ruling on wife's inheritance when husband makes ila' while healthy vs. during fatal illness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a wife's inheritance when her husband makes ila' during health versus during fatal illness, and apply it to a given scenario.

Core Idea
A wife inherits from her husband who dies after ila' only if the ila' itself occurred during his fatal illness.

This lesson focuses on a concise ruling from al-Hidayah regarding the intersection of ila' (a vow of marital abstinence) and inheritance during fatal illness. The key determinant is not when the separation takes effect, but when the ila' was originally made. Understanding this nuance prevents common errors in applying the general principle that a husband's actions during illness may be scrutinized for intent to deprive his wife of inheritance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Scenarios
The text presents two scenarios: (1) ila' made while husband is healthy, separation occurs during illness; (2) ila' made while husband is ill, separation occurs during illness. Memorize each.
2
State the Ruling for Each
For scenario 1: wife does not inherit. For scenario 2: wife inherits. Commit these to memory.
3
Understand the Reasoning
The ruling is based on the principle that actions during health that take effect during illness may be considered evasions of inheritance rights. If ila' was in health, the presumption of evasion applies and she is barred. If ila' itself was in illness, the presumption does not apply and she inherits.
This is explained in the sharh of al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان الى امرأته وهو صحيح ثم بانت بالايلاء وهو مريض لم ترث وان كان الإيلاء ايضافى المرض ورثت
And if he makes ila' with his wife while he is healthy, then she becomes bainah (separated) by the ila' while he is sick, she does not inherit. And if the ila' was also in the illness, she inherits.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This is a concise matn ruling from al-Hidayah on the effect of ila' (a vow of abstinence from marital relations for four months or more) on inheritance during fatal illness. The ruling: If the husband performs ila' while healthy, but the separation (ba'in) occurs via the expiration of the waiting period while he is sick, the wife does not inherit. However, if both the ila' and the subsequent separation occur while he is in his fatal illness, then she does inherit. The reasoning, as explained in the sharh (not included in this snippet but implied from the context), aligns with the general principle: a separation that is caused by the husband during health and takes effect during illness is considered an evasion of inheritance rights, so the wife is not entitled. But if the entire process occurs during illness, the presumption of evasion is not applied, and she inherits. This is a straightforward ruling without additional proof or dispute.

Key Terms
إيلاء (īlā’): A vow by the husband to abstain from sexual relations with his wife for four months or more.
بائن (bā’in): Irrevocably separated (a type of divorce where the husband cannot take his wife back without a new marriage).
مرض الموت (marḍ al-mawt): Fatal illness; a terminal illness that leads to death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband makes ila' while healthy, and the wife becomes bainah (separated) due to ila' while the husband is in his fatal illness, does the wife inherit?
A) Yes, because separation occurred during illness.
B) No, because the ila' was made in health.
C) Yes, but only if she is in iddah.
D) No, because ila' does not affect inheritance.

Key Takeaway
For a wife to inherit from her husband who made ila', the ila' itself must have been made during his fatal illness; if made in health, she does not inherit regardless of when separation occurs.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate

Ilā' in Health vs. Deathbed Illness: Inheritance of the Wife
Ruling on wife's inheritance when ilā' occurs in health vs. deathbed illness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that distinguishes whether a wife inherits from her husband when ilā' leads to divorce before his death in deathbed illness, based on the timing of the ilā'.

Core Idea
Ilā' in health does not entitle inheritance; ilā' in deathbed illness does, because the separation is tied to the time of the vow.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah deals with a nuanced scenario: a husband makes ilā' (vow of abstention), the wife becomes bā'in after four months, and then the husband dies during deathbed illness. The key is whether the ilā' was done before or during the deathbed illness. The Hanafi school makes a precise distinction based on attributing the cause of divorce to the time of the vow.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The text presents two cases: ilā' in health, and ilā' in marad al-mawt (deathbed illness). Recognize that the ruling differs based solely on this factor.
2
Determine the ruling for each scenario
For ilā' in health: the wife does not inherit. For ilā' in marad al-mawt: the wife inherits, provided the husband dies during her 'iddah.
The separation (bā'in) occurs after four months; the timing of the vow determines inheritance.
3
Understand the reasoning (ta'līl)
Ilā' is a conditional divorce suspended on the passage of four months without intercourse. The divorce is attributed to the time of the vow, not the time it takes effect. If the vow was made in health, the cause precedes the illness, so the husband is not considered a fārr (one who fraudulently deprives inheritance).
The text states: 'the separation is attributed to the husband's ilā', and in deathbed illness nothing is found from the husband, neither the effect of the cause nor the condition.'
4
Apply the principle of firār
The doctrine of firār (fraudulent deprivation) is applied: acts done during deathbed illness to deprive heirs are probative. When ilā' is performed in marad al-mawt, the entire process is linked to the illness, indicating intent to deprive, thus the wife inherits.
This prevents abuse where a husband might try to circumvent inheritance rules by setting up conditions before he becomes ill.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب طلاق المريض لان الايلاء في معنى تعليق الطلاق بمضى اربعة اشهر خال عن الوقاع فيكون ملحقا بالتعليق بمجئى الوقت وقد ذكرنا وجهه
ترجمہ اور اگر تندرستی کی حالت میں اسنے اپنی بیوی سے ایلاء کیا۔ پھر ایلاء کی وجہ سے وہ بائنہ ہو گئی ۔ درانحالیکہ وہ مرد مریض ہے تو عورت اس کی وارث نہیں ہوگی اور اگر ایلاء کرنا بھی مرض الموت میں ( واقع ) ہوا ہو، تو وارث ہو گی ۔ کیونکہ ایلاء کرنا چار ماہ جماع سے خالی گذرنے پر طلاق کو معلق کرنا ہے تو یہ صورت ایلاء بھی وقت کے آنے پر متعلق کرنے کے ساتھ ملحق ہے اور ہم اس کی وجہ ذکر کر چکے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی شخص نے تندرستی کے زمانہ میں اپنی بیوی سے ایلاء کیا، یعنی قسم کھائی کہ چار ماہ یا زیادہ تک تجھ سے ولی نہیں کروں گا۔ پھر ایلاء کی وجہ سے۔ یعنی چار ماہ بغیر ولی کے گذر جانے کی وجہ سے عورت بائنہ ہو گئی ۔ درانحالیکہ شوہر مرض الموت میں ہے تو عورت، اپنے اس شوہر کی وارث نہیں ہو گی۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ بینونت شوہر کے ایلاء کی طرف منسوب ہے اور مرض الموت میں شوہر کی طرف سے کوئی چیز نہیں پائی گئی نہ علت کا عمل اور نہ شرط کا۔ پس شو ہر فار نہیں ہوگا۔ لہذا اس کی بیوی امراۃ فارنہ ہونے کی وجہ سے وارث نہیں ہو گی۔ ( مینی شرح ہدایہ) اور اگر ایلاء کرنا بھی مرض الموت میں واقع ہوا ہو اور پھر بینونت کے بعد شوہر عدت کے زمانہ میں مر گیا تو یہ عورت وارث ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ ایلاء کے معنی ہیں طلاق کو ایسے چار ماہ گذر جانے پر معلق کرنا جو جماع سے خالی ہوں۔ لہذا یہ صورت طلاق کو وقت کے آنے پر معلق کرنے کے ساتھ ملحق ہوگئی اور اس کی وجہ ہم سابق میں بیان کر چکے ہیں ، ملاحظہ کر لیا جائے۔
Chapter: Divorce of the sick person. Because ilā' is in the meaning of suspending divorce upon the passage of four months devoid of intercourse, so it is attached to suspension upon the arrival of time, and we have mentioned its reasoning. Translation: And if in a state of health he made ilā' from his wife, then due to the ilā' she became bā'in, while the man is sick, then the woman will not inherit from him. And if the ilā' also occurred in deathbed illness, then she will inherit. Because ilā' is suspending divorce upon the passage of four months devoid of intercourse, so this form of ilā' is also attached to suspension upon the arrival of time, and we have mentioned its reasoning. Explanation of the issue: If a person in a time of health made ilā' from his wife, i.e., swore that he will not have intercourse with her for four months or more, then due to the ilā', i.e., due to the passage of four months without intercourse, the woman became bā'in while the husband is in deathbed illness, then the woman will not inherit from this husband. The proof is that the separation is attributed to the husband's ilā', and in deathbed illness nothing is found from the husband, neither the effect of the cause nor the condition. So the husband is not a fārr (one who intends to deprive inheritance). Therefore his wife will not inherit because she is not a wife of a fārr. (From Sharh Hidayah) And if the ilā' also occurred in deathbed illness, and then after separation the husband died during the 'iddah period, then this woman will inherit. Because the meaning of ilā' is suspending divorce upon the passage of four months that are devoid of intercourse. Hence this form is attached to suspending divorce upon the arrival of time, and we have already explained its reasoning – please refer to it.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses the ruling on inheritance when a husband makes ilā' (vow of abstention) and the wife becomes bā'in (irrevocably divorced) due to the elapse of four months without intercourse. The key distinction is whether the ilā' was pronounced in a state of health or during deathbed illness (marad al-mawt). If the ilā' was made in health, the separation is attributed to the husband's act performed while healthy, and thus the wife does not inherit even if the husband later dies in illness. The husband is not considered a fārr (one who fraudulently divorces to deprive inheritance) because the cause of separation originated before the deathbed illness. However, if the ilā' itself was performed during deathbed illness, then the wife inherits because the divorce is effectively suspended until the condition (four months) occurs, and the entire process is connected to the period of illness. The reasoning is that ilā' is similar to a conditional divorce (ta'līq al-talāq) where the divorce takes effect upon the arrival of a specified time; in the deathbed scenario, the husband's action is deemed to be an attempt to deprive the wife of inheritance, so it is treated as effective divorce during illness, entitling her to inherit. The text also notes that this ruling is based on the principle of attributing the divorce to the time of the cause (the ilā' act) rather than the subsequent event.

Key Terms
ایلاء (īlā'): A vow of abstention from sexual intercourse with one's wife for four months or more, leading to automatic divorce upon the elapse of four months without intercourse.
بائنہ (bā'inah): A woman divorced irrevocably; the marriage ends and she cannot be taken back without a new marriage contract.
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): Deathbed illness, a condition from which one is likely to die, affecting legal dispositions like divorce to prevent inheritance fraud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, what is the inheritance ruling for a wife who becomes bā'in due to ilā' made in health, when the husband later dies in deathbed illness?
A) She inherits because the divorce occurred during illness.
B) She does not inherit because the ilā' was performed in health and the separation is attributed to that.
C) She inherits only if the husband explicitly intended to deprive her.
D) She inherits full share regardless of the timing.

Key Takeaway
The wife inherits only if the ilā' itself was performed during deathbed illness, not if performed earlier in health.
